# Auditoría UX/UI + Usabilidad TREINO — 2026-06-16

Evaluación multi-agente de **43 pantallas + 11 user journeys** contra el design system, heurísticas de Nielsen, accesibilidad (a11y), estados (loading/empty/error), i18n y consistencia.

**Total: 418 findings** — high=107, medium=179, low=132

### Por categoría

- **states**: 92
- **accessibility**: 85
- **microcopy-i18n**: 64
- **design-system**: 39
- **usability**: 58
- **consistency**: 41
- **visual-hierarchy**: 6
- **navigation**: 24
- **responsive**: 9


### Findings por pantalla (high/med/low)

# Detalle por pantalla

## lib/features/auth/presentation/forgot_password_screen.dart (auth module)

_Solid, well-structured screen: strings fully routed through AppL10n, colors via AppPalette, icons via TreinoIcon, and it correctly implements the security requirement (REQ-AUTH-011) of treating userNotFound as success. The strongest issues are accessibility (icon-only back button has no Semantics label and is 40pt, below the 44pt iOS minimum) and a silent error path: the generic `catch (_)` clears loading but shows the user nothing, leaving them stuck with no feedback. Secondary issues: empty EN translations (es-AR only is filled), a few off-scale spacing values, the hero font not being a documented token, and no resend affordance in the success state._

- **[HIGH · states]** The generic `catch (_)` branch in `_submit()` only resets `_isLoading = false` and gives the user NO feedback. Any non-AuthFailure error (network timeout, platform exception, unexpected error) leaves the form looking idle as if nothing happened — the user taps 'ENVIAR LINK', the spinner disappears, and there is no banner, no message, no state change. This violates Nielsen's 'visibility of system status' and is the most impactful gap on the screen.
  - **Fix:** In the `catch (_)` branch, set a generic failure into `_failure` (e.g. an AuthFailure.unknown / network variant) so `AuthFailureBanner` renders, mirroring the `on AuthFailure` else-branch. Never swallow an error silently in a user-initiated async action.
  - **Evidencia:** forgot_password_screen.dart:74-77 — `catch (_) { if (!mounted) return; setState(() => _isLoading = false); }`

- **[HIGH · accessibility]** The circular back button is icon-only with no accessible label. `AuthCircleBackButton` renders an `Icon(TreinoIcon.back)` inside an `InkWell` with no `Semantics`/`semanticLabel`/`tooltip`, so VoiceOver announces it as an unlabeled button. The sibling `legal_document_screen.dart` already sets `tooltip: 'Volver'` on its back affordance, so this is an inconsistency as well as an a11y defect. Affects login and register too since they share the widget.
  - **Fix:** Wrap the InkWell in `Semantics(button: true, label: l10n.commonBack /* 'Volver' */, child: ...)` inside AuthCircleBackButton (fix once, benefits all auth screens). Pass a label param if it should vary.
  - **Evidencia:** auth_circle_back_button.dart:28-40 (InkWell + Icon, no semantics); used at forgot_password_screen.dart:95-98

- **[MEDIUM · accessibility]** Back button tap target is 40x40pt (default `size = 40` in AuthCircleBackButton), below the iOS HIG / WCAG 2.5.5 minimum of 44pt. The icon itself is only 18pt. Small target at the top-left corner is harder to hit, especially one-handed.
  - **Fix:** Bump default `size` to 44 in AuthCircleBackButton, or wrap the tap region so the hit area is >= 44pt even if the visual circle stays 40. Keep the visual style; only the touch target needs to grow.
  - **Evidencia:** auth_circle_back_button.dart:13 (`this.size = 40`) and :31-39 (SizedBox width/height = size, Icon size 18)

- **[MEDIUM · microcopy-i18n]** All EN translations for this screen are empty strings. `authForgotTitle`, `authForgotBody`, `authForgotCta`, `authForgotSuccess`, etc. are '' in intl_en.arb / app_l10n_en.dart, while es-AR is fully populated. A device in English locale would render a blank title, blank body, and a blank CTA button — effectively a broken screen for any non-Spanish user.
  - **Fix:** Fill the English ARB values (this is a project-wide auth gap — login/register keys are also empty). If Spanish-only is intentional for launch, pin the app locale to es-AR so English falls back to the populated strings instead of rendering empty.
  - **Evidencia:** intl_en.arb:29-35 (all '') and app_l10n_en.dart:84-102 vs intl_es_AR.arb:28-34 (populated)

- **[MEDIUM · states]** The success state has no 'resend' affordance and no way back to the form. After sending, the screen shows the success message, a disabled (read-only) email field, and a single 'Volver al login' TextButton. If the email never arrives (spam, typo) the user's only recourse is to go to login and start over — they cannot resend or edit the address. This weakens user control & freedom.
  - **Fix:** Add a secondary 'Reenviar link' action in the success branch (re-runs `_submit`), and/or allow returning to the editable form to correct the address. At minimum keep the field editable so a re-send with a corrected email is possible.
  - **Evidencia:** forgot_password_screen.dart:122-153 — success branch: disabled AuthInput (`enabled: false`) + only a 'back to login' TextButton, no resend

- **[LOW · design-system]** Spacing uses several off-scale values. The documented scale is 8·12·14·18·20 (explicitly 'No usar 4/16/24'), but the screen uses SizedBox heights of 24 and 28. The hero title also uses `GoogleFonts.spaceGrotesk` (size 40), which is not a documented type token — design-system specifies headings as Barlow Condensed. This matches the sibling login_screen (so it's consistent within the module) but diverges from the written tokens.
  - **Fix:** Replace 24/28 gaps with on-scale values (e.g. 20) unless there is an explicit design exception; either way, document the auth hero exception. If Space Grotesk is the intended auth display font, add it to design-system.md as a named token so it stops reading as an ad-hoc value.
  - **Evidencia:** forgot_password_screen.dart:99 (SizedBox height 24), :121 (height 28), :103 (GoogleFonts.spaceGrotesk fontSize 40); design-system.md:42-49 (Barlow Condensed headings; scale 8·12·14·18·20)

- **[LOW · usability]** Primary-action gating depends only on non-empty text, not a valid email. `onPressed` is disabled when the trimmed field is empty, but any non-empty string (e.g. 'abc') enables 'ENVIAR LINK' and triggers a round-trip. AuthInput supports a `validator` but none is passed here, so there is no inline email-format validation / error prevention before submit.
  - **Fix:** Pass an email-format `validator` to AuthInput (or gate `onPressed` on a basic email regex) so malformed addresses are caught before the network call — recognition of the error at the field rather than after submit.
  - **Evidencia:** forgot_password_screen.dart:156-166 (AuthInput, no validator) and :174 (`onPressed: ...isEmpty ? null : _submit`); auth_input.dart:35 supports `validator` but it is unused here

## lib/features/auth/presentation/legal/legal_document_screen.dart (module: auth) — full-screen viewer for Terms & Privacy legal documents, pushed via Navigator from TermsCheckbox during registration

_Structurally solid screen: clean StatelessWidget, zero HEX literals, all colors via AppPalette.of(context), TreinoIcon.back used correctly, SafeArea + Expanded ListView so content and large dynamic type never clip, back affordance is clear and predictable (maybePop). It is purely static content (no AsyncValue), so there are no missing loading/error/empty states to flag. The substantive gaps are: (1) every user-facing string is hardcoded while the rest of the auth module uses AppL10n; (2) the back IconButton and the legal links have no Semantics/screen-reader treatment; (3) typography uses raw GoogleFonts + ad-hoc font sizes instead of shared tokens, and the section-heading style ignores the design-system UPPERCASE heading rule._

- **[HIGH · microcopy-i18n]** Every user-facing string on this screen is hardcoded in Spanish. The header tooltip 'Volver' (line 44), the footer 'Última actualización: ... / Consultas: ...' (lines 74-75), the two screen titles 'Términos y Condiciones' / 'Política de Privacidad' passed from terms_checkbox.dart (lines 47-49), and the entire body of legal_content.dart (kTermsSections / kPrivacySections, 25 sections) are literals. This directly violates design-system.md rule #3 ('Nunca hard-code de strings de UI') and is inconsistent with the rest of the auth module — register_screen.dart, login_screen.dart, forgot_password_screen.dart and welcome_screen.dart all resolve strings via AppL10n.of(context) (e.g. l10n.authRegisterTitle, l10n.authForgotBody). The AppL10n infrastructure already exists (lib/l10n/app_l10n.dart, intl_es_AR.arb).
  - **Fix:** Move at least the chrome strings ('Volver', the footer 'Última actualización'/'Consultas' labels) into AppL10n keys (e.g. legalBack, legalLastUpdated, legalContact) and resolve via AppL10n.of(context). The legal section bodies are a special case — legal copy is often kept verbatim and reviewed by counsel, so it can stay in legal_content.dart, but the screen TITLES should still come from l10n. At minimum, document the deliberate exception for the legal body so it does not read as an oversight.
  - **Evidencia:** legal_document_screen.dart:44 (tooltip 'Volver'), :74-75 (footer text), legal_content.dart:19-186; contrast with forgot_password_screen.dart:83 final l10n = AppL10n.of(context)

- **[HIGH · accessibility]** The section heading and the document title are styled as visual headings but carry no semantic heading marker. Screen-reader users get a flat run of paragraphs with no way to jump between the 11-14 sections of a long legal document. The Text at lines 48-58 (document title) and lines 89-97 (section.heading) should expose header: true so VoiceOver/TalkBack treat them as navigable headings.
  - **Fix:** Wrap the title Text and each section heading Text in Semantics(header: true, child: ...), or pass semanticsLabel where appropriate. This is the single biggest a11y win on a content-heavy legal screen because it restores document structure for assistive tech.
  - **Evidencia:** legal_document_screen.dart:48-58 (title), :89-97 (section heading)

- **[MEDIUM · accessibility]** The back IconButton has a tooltip 'Volver' (good for hover/long-press) but no explicit semanticsLabel, so it relies on the tooltip and the underlying Phosphor caretLeft glyph for its accessible name. More importantly, the links that lead HERE (terms_checkbox.dart lines 87-97: tappable 'Términos' / 'Política de Privacidad' TextSpans driven by TapGestureRecognizer) are not exposed as buttons/links to screen readers and are not announced as tappable — a screen-reader user has no signal that those words open a document. This is the entry affordance for this screen, so it is in scope.
  - **Fix:** On the back button, the tooltip doubles as the a11y label so this is minor — but for the inbound links in TermsCheckbox, wrap each tappable TextSpan's intent in a Semantics(link: true / button: true) treatment (e.g. via Semantics around the Text.rich or by splitting the links into Semantics-wrapped GestureDetectors) so they announce as actionable.
  - **Evidencia:** legal_document_screen.dart:41-45 (IconButton, tooltip only); terms_checkbox.dart:87-97 (link TextSpans, no Semantics)

- **[MEDIUM · design-system]** Typography uses raw GoogleFonts.barlowCondensed / GoogleFonts.barlow with hardcoded font sizes (24, 16, 14, 12) and letterSpacing inline rather than shared text tokens, and the section-heading style violates the documented heading rule. design-system.md states headings are 'Barlow Condensed 700, UPPERCASE, letter-spacing 0.5-1.0px', but the section headings here render in Title Case (section.heading values like '1. Aceptación') with letterSpacing 0.3 (below the 0.5 floor). The font sizes 24/16/15/12 also do not map cleanly to any defined scale. The project has no AppTypography token class yet (styles are inlined across screens), so this is a module-wide pattern, but it is worth flagging that this screen drifts from the heading spec.
  - **Fix:** Either uppercase the section headings and bump letterSpacing into the 0.5-1.0 range to match the heading spec, or formalize a shared text-style helper (AppTypography) and consume it here so the heading rule is enforced in one place. Short term, raise letterSpacing to >=0.5 on the barlowCondensed heading styles and apply UPPERCASE to be consistent with the documented system.
  - **Evidencia:** legal_document_screen.dart:52-57 (title style, ls 0.3), :91-96 (section heading, ls 0.3, Title Case); design-system.md:42 ('Barlow Condensed 700, UPPERCASE, letter-spacing 0.5-1.0 px')

- **[LOW · consistency]** Back-navigation pattern differs from sibling auth screens. This screen calls Navigator.of(context).maybePop() (line 43) because it is pushed via a raw MaterialPageRoute outside go_router — which is intentional and documented in the class doc (lines 11-14). However sibling screens use the go_router idiom context.canPop() ? context.pop() : context.go('/welcome') (register_screen.dart:154-156). The current approach is correct for this screen's deliberate off-router mount, but the header layout also differs: this screen puts the title inline next to the back button in a Row, while register/forgot use a left-aligned standalone back button above a separate headline. Minor visual inconsistency, not a defect.
  - **Fix:** No functional change needed — maybePop() is the right call for an off-router pushed screen. Optionally align the header composition (standalone back button + headline) with the rest of the auth module for visual rhythm, but only if a broader header-component pass is done.
  - **Evidencia:** legal_document_screen.dart:37-62 (inline Row header, maybePop); register_screen.dart:149-173 (standalone back + headline, context.pop/go)

- **[LOW · states]** The footer concatenates 'Última actualización: $kLegalLastUpdated.\nConsultas: $kLegalContactEmail' as plain muted text (lines 74-80). The contact email is presented but is not actionable — a user reading the privacy/terms doc who wants to exercise their Ley 25.326 rights (referenced repeatedly in the body) cannot tap to email. Recognition-over-recall and user-control are slightly weakened: the email is shown but the user must memorize/copy it manually.
  - **Fix:** Make kLegalContactEmail a tappable mailto link (TapGestureRecognizer in a Text.rich, styled with palette.accent + underline like the inbound links in TermsCheckbox), launching url_launcher. Low effort, improves the user-control/affordance on a screen whose body explicitly tells users to write to that address to exercise rights.
  - **Evidencia:** legal_document_screen.dart:73-80 (static footer); legal_content.dart:161-162, :183-184 (body repeatedly directs users to email for rights)

## lib/features/auth/presentation/login_screen.dart (module: auth)

_The login screen is well-built on the design-system axis: zero HEX literals, all colors via AppPalette.of(context), spacing entirely on the 8/12/14/18/20 scale, every user-facing string routed through AppL10n with correct Rioplatense voseo, and icons through TreinoIcon (the FontAwesome Google/Apple glyphs are a legitimate brand exception). The real problems are in validation, accessibility, and cross-screen consistency. The most serious is that the screen wires up a Form + GlobalKey<FormState> but never validates it and passes no validators to its inputs, so error prevention is effectively absent — a malformed email reaches the network before the user gets any feedback. The sibling register_screen does this correctly, which makes the gap a clear regression rather than a design choice. Secondary issues: icon-only back button has no Semantics/tooltip, a dedicated AuthCircleBackButton widget exists and is documented for this screen but is bypassed in favor of a raw IconButton, and secondary navigation stays live during the sign-in request._

- **[HIGH · usability]** The login screen builds a Form with a GlobalKey<FormState> (_formKey) but never calls _formKey.currentState.validate(), and neither AuthInput is given a validator. The only client-side guard is _fieldsEmpty (CTA disabled while empty). This means there is NO format validation: an invalid email like 'abc' or a too-short password is submitted directly to Firebase, and the user only learns it is wrong after a network round-trip via the error banner. This violates Nielsen's error-prevention heuristic. The sibling register_screen.dart does this correctly — it calls _formKey.currentState?.validate() (line 68) and passes EmailPasswordValidator.validateEmail / validatePassword to its fields (lines 193, 207), so the validator already exists and is unused here.
  - **Fix:** In _submit(), short-circuit with `if (!(_formKey.currentState?.validate() ?? false)) return;` before calling signIn, and pass `validator: EmailPasswordValidator.validateEmail` to the email AuthInput and a non-empty validator to the password AuthInput. Reuse lib/features/auth/domain/email_password_validator.dart exactly as register_screen does. Otherwise, if validation is genuinely not wanted, remove the dead Form/_formKey wiring so the code does not imply protection it does not provide.
  - **Evidencia:** login_screen.dart:54-64 (_submit never validates), :101-102 (Form/_formKey), :143-164 (AuthInput with no validator). Contrast register_screen.dart:68 and :193,:207.

- **[HIGH · accessibility]** The top-left back button is an icon-only IconButton (TreinoIcon.back) with no Semantics label, no tooltip, and no semanticLabel on the Icon. Screen-reader users hear an unlabeled button. The same omission applies to the TreinoLogo (an SvgPicture with no semantic label or excludeFromSemantics). Note the password eye-toggle inside AuthInput IS correctly wrapped in a Tooltip, which shows the pattern is understood elsewhere — the back button just missed it.
  - **Fix:** Wrap the back IconButton with a Semantics label (or add `tooltip: l10n.commonBack`) and add a localized semantic label to the back/forward icons. For TreinoLogo, either pass a semantic label ('TREINO') or set excludeFromSemantics on the decorative SVG. Add the back-label string to the ARB files.
  - **Evidencia:** login_screen.dart:107-116 (IconButton, no Semantics/tooltip); treino_logo.dart:37-44 (SvgPicture.asset with no semantic label). Grep for Semantics/tooltip in both files returned no matches.

- **[MEDIUM · consistency]** The auth module has a dedicated AuthCircleBackButton widget whose own doc comment states it is the back control 'used at the top-left of auth screens (ForgotPassword, Login, Register)'. forgot_password_screen.dart uses it (line 95). But login_screen.dart and register_screen.dart both bypass it with a raw IconButton + TreinoIcon.back (register's code even carries the comment 'same pattern as Login'). Result: the back affordance looks different on Forgot Password (circular outlined chevron) than on Login/Register (bare caret), within the same flow the user moves through linearly.
  - **Fix:** Replace the raw IconButton in login_screen.dart (and register_screen.dart) with AuthCircleBackButton to match forgot_password and the widget's documented intent. This also resolves the Semantics gap above, since the shared widget can carry the label/tooltip in one place. If the bare-caret style is the intended new standard, update forgot_password and delete AuthCircleBackButton instead — but pick one.
  - **Evidencia:** auth_circle_back_button.dart:6-8 (doc names Login/Register); forgot_password_screen.dart:95 (uses it); login_screen.dart:109-115 and register_screen.dart:151-157 (raw IconButton).

- **[MEDIUM · states]** During an in-flight email/password sign-in (authState.isLoading), only the primary CTA is locked (spinner + disabled) and the two social buttons are disabled. The back button, the 'Olvidé la contraseña' TextButton, and the 'Registrate' GestureDetector, and the trainer-inquiry card all remain fully tappable. A user can navigate away (context.push('/forgot-password') / '/register' / pop) while the auth request is still resolving, which can race with the post-await context.go('/home') in _submit and leave the navigation stack in an unexpected state.
  - **Fix:** Gate the secondary navigation affordances on isLoading too (disable or onPressed: isLoading ? null : ...) for the forgot-password link, the register link, and ideally the back button, so the screen presents a single coherent busy state while a request is pending. This matches how the social buttons already behave (login_screen.dart:223,231).
  - **Evidencia:** login_screen.dart:168-169 (forgot link, no isLoading guard), :249-250 (register GestureDetector, no guard), :112-114 (back button, no guard) vs :223,:231 (social buttons correctly guarded).

- **[LOW · microcopy-i18n]** Two minor hardcoded Spanish strings live in shared child widgets used by this screen rather than in AppL10n: the password-toggle tooltip ('Mostrar contraseña' / 'Ocultar contraseña') in AuthInput, and the 'Próximamente' tooltip on disabled AuthSecondaryButton. They are correct voseo-neutral Spanish but bypass the localization pipeline the rest of the screen follows, so they will not translate and are invisible to the ARB workflow.
  - **Fix:** Move these three strings into the ARB files (e.g. authShowPassword, authHidePassword, commonComingSoon) and read them via AppL10n.of(context) inside AuthInput and AuthSecondaryButton, consistent with every other string on this screen.
  - **Evidencia:** auth_input.dart:64 ('Mostrar contraseña'/'Ocultar contraseña'); auth_secondary_button.dart:78 (Tooltip message: 'Próximamente').

- **[LOW · visual-hierarchy]** Heading sizes diverge across the auth flow: Login title is Space Grotesk 28 (login_screen.dart:125) and Register is also 28, but Forgot Password is 40 (forgot_password_screen.dart:104). Since these screens sit in one linear flow, the jump from a 28pt headline to a 40pt headline on the very next screen breaks the typographic rhythm. Minor, but worth aligning.
  - **Fix:** Settle on one auth-headline size (or two deliberate tiers documented in design-system.md) and apply it consistently across login/register/forgot. If 40 is the intended hero size, bump login/register; if 28 is the standard, bring forgot down.
  - **Evidencia:** login_screen.dart:125 (fontSize: 28); register_screen.dart:165 (fontSize: 28); forgot_password_screen.dart:104 (fontSize: 40).

## lib/features/auth/presentation/register_screen.dart (auth module)

_The register screen is well-built: it uses AppPalette.of(context) and TreinoIcon consistently (zero HEX/Colors literals, zero direct PhosphorIcons in the screen), routes nearly all copy through AppL10n, mirrors the Login screen's structure, handles loading + error states cleanly, and wires up focus traversal, autofill hints, password strength feedback, and an in-app Terms/Privacy reader. The main gaps are accessibility (no Semantics/tooltip on the icon-only back button, no semanticsLabel on the Google logo SVG, a 28px IconButton tap target, and an inert disabled CTA with no explanation) plus two hardcoded Spanish strings in the social sign-in Terms gate that bypass AppL10n. Spacing uses tokens with one off-scale 4px and one 10px value. No invented problems; the screen is solid overall._

- **[HIGH · accessibility]** The top-left back button is an icon-only IconButton with no Semantics label or tooltip. A screen reader announces it as an unlabeled button, and there is no on-press affordance hint. This is the only way to leave the screen via the chrome, so it must be discoverable to VoiceOver/TalkBack users.
  - **Fix:** Add a tooltip and/or wrap the icon in a Semantics label, e.g. IconButton(tooltip: l10n.commonBack, icon: Icon(TreinoIcon.back, ...)). Add a new AppL10n key (e.g. 'Volver') rather than hardcoding. Login screen has the identical gap, so fix both for module consistency.
  - **Evidencia:** register_screen.dart:149-158 (Align > IconButton with TreinoIcon.back, no tooltip/semanticsLabel)

- **[MEDIUM · accessibility]** The back button's tap target is undersized. IconButton uses padding: EdgeInsets.zero with a default icon size of 24, yielding roughly a 24-28pt hit area, below the 44pt iOS / 48dp guideline. Removing the default padding removed the touch slop that normally guarantees the minimum target.
  - **Fix:** Drop padding: EdgeInsets.zero (or set constraints: BoxConstraints(minWidth: 44, minHeight: 44) and an explicit visualDensity) so the back affordance meets 44pt. If the zero padding is purely for left alignment, offset with a small negative Transform or align the row instead of shrinking the button.
  - **Evidencia:** register_screen.dart:151-153 (IconButton padding: EdgeInsets.zero)

- **[MEDIUM · accessibility]** The official Google G logo is rendered via SvgPicture.asset with no semanticsLabel, so the Google sign-in button's icon contributes nothing for screen readers. The text label 'GOOGLE' carries the meaning here, so it is partially mitigated, but the image is still an unlabeled graphic in the a11y tree.
  - **Fix:** Pass semanticsLabel: '' (explicitly decorative, since the adjacent 'GOOGLE' text labels the button) on the SvgPicture.asset, so it is correctly excluded rather than ambiguously unlabeled. The Apple button uses a FontAwesome glyph + text and is fine.
  - **Evidencia:** register_screen.dart:282-286 (SvgPicture.asset('assets/logo/google_g.svg') with no semanticsLabel)

- **[MEDIUM · states]** The primary CTA is disabled (onPressed: null) whenever fields are empty OR Terms is unchecked, but unlike the social buttons there is no explanation of WHY it is disabled. A user who filled the form but did not tick Terms sees a dead, dimmed 'CREAR CUENTA' button with no feedback — a visibility-of-system-status / error-prevention gap. Notably, the Google/Apple paths deliberately stay enabled and show a snackbar precisely to avoid this dead-end (see comment at lines 272-276), so the email CTA is inconsistent with that decision.
  - **Fix:** Either keep the CTA enabled and surface the same 'Aceptá los Términos...' snackbar on tap when Terms is unchecked (matching the social-button pattern), or add an inline helper/error near the Terms checkbox when the user attempts to submit. Prefer the snackbar approach for consistency with _signInWithGoogle/_signInWithApple.
  - **Evidencia:** register_screen.dart:65 (_canSubmit requires _termsAccepted), 246-250 (AuthPillButton onPressed: _canSubmit ? _submit : null) vs 272-296 (social buttons stay enabled with snackbar feedback)

- **[MEDIUM · microcopy-i18n]** The Terms-required snackbar message is a hardcoded Spanish literal in two places, bypassing AppL10n. Every other user-facing string on the screen goes through l10n, so this breaks the localization contract and will not translate when intl_en.arb is filled in.
  - **Fix:** Extract 'Aceptá los Términos y la Política de Privacidad para continuar' into a single AppL10n key (e.g. authRegisterTermsRequired) and reference it in both _signInWithGoogle and _signInWithApple. Wrap the snackbar Text with AppL10n.of(context).
  - **Evidencia:** register_screen.dart:88-90 (_signInWithGoogle) and 110-112 (_signInWithApple) — identical const Text(...) literal

- **[LOW · design-system]** Two spacing values fall outside the documented scale (8 / 12 / 14 / 18 / 20). There is a SizedBox(height: 4) after the password field and a SizedBox(height: 10) between the title and the logo. design-system.md explicitly bans 4 and only lists 8/12/14/18/20.
  - **Fix:** The 4px gap (password field to strength bar) is an intentional 'pegada al input' tight coupling per the inline comment — acceptable as a deliberate exception but worth a token or a documented note. The 10px gap (title to logo) has no such justification; round it to 8 or 12 to stay on-scale.
  - **Evidencia:** register_screen.dart:209 (SizedBox height: 4) and 172 (SizedBox height: 10)

- **[LOW · consistency]** The register and login screens diverge in input labeling without an obvious reason: register uses AuthInput with visible UC labels (EMAIL / CONTRASEÑA), while login uses the same component with hint-only, no labels. Both are valid, but the inconsistency between two sibling auth screens using the same widget is a minor hierarchy/recognition inconsistency a user moving between them may notice.
  - **Fix:** Confirm this is an intentional mockup-driven difference (login is icon+hint only, register is labeled). If so, leave it; if not, align the two. The current divergence appears deliberate per the comments, so this is informational, not a defect.
  - **Evidencia:** register_screen.dart:184-194 (label: l10n.authRegisterEmailLabel) vs login_screen.dart:143-152 (hint only, no label)

- **[LOW · accessibility]** Screen-reader reading order is logical (back, title, logo, subtitle, fields, terms, CTA, divider, social), but the TREINO brand wordmark (TreinoLogo / SvgPicture) carries no semantics. After the 'SUMATE A' headline a sighted user reads the TREINO logo as the second half of the title; a screen reader hears 'SUMATE A' followed by silence, losing the brand name from the heading.
  - **Fix:** Give TreinoLogo an optional semanticsLabel (e.g. 'TREINO') and pass it here so the headline reads as 'Sumate a TREINO' for assistive tech. Low severity since brand recognition is non-blocking, but it completes the heading.
  - **Evidencia:** register_screen.dart:162-173 (Text authRegisterTitle 'SUMATE A' + TreinoLogo(size: 44) with no label); treino_logo.dart:37-44 (SvgPicture.asset with no semanticsLabel)

## lib/features/auth/presentation/splash_screen.dart (auth module — Splash)

_The splash is visually clean and correctly uses AppPalette tokens (no HEX literals, no direct PhosphorIcons) with a properly themed logo. But it has three real problems worth fixing: (1) a silent dead-end — if the Firebase auth stream errors, the awaited future throws, _navigate() rejects, and the user is stranded on the splash forever with no error UI, no retry, and no spinner; (2) hardcoded Spanish copy that bypasses the existing AppL10n system even though a localized key (authSplashTagline) and the EN/ES/es_AR ARB entries already exist and the sibling welcome_screen.dart already localizes the same content; (3) off-design-system typography — it renders the headline in GoogleFonts.spaceGrotesk, a font that appears nowhere in docs/design-system.md (which mandates Barlow Condensed for headings). The content also drifts from the canonical brand tagline. None of the standard async states (loading/error) are surfaced on screen._

- **[HIGH · states]** _navigate() does `await ref.read(authNotifierProvider.future)` with NO try/catch. authNotifierProvider seeds from authStateChangesProvider.future (the Firebase auth stream). If that stream emits an error (network failure on token refresh, Firebase init error, etc.), the future rejects, the await throws, _navigate() aborts before any context.go() call, and the user is stranded on the splash indefinitely. There is no error branch, no retry affordance, and no loading indicator — the screen has only a 'happy path' designed. This is the classic AsyncValue handled without its error case.
  - **Fix:** Wrap the await in try/catch (or read the AsyncValue and branch on its error). On error, either route to /welcome as a safe fallback or render an inline error state with a retry button (the project already ships a 'Reintentar' string, e.g. l10n.coachRetryLabel). Also consider a timeout so a hung stream never traps the user. At minimum, surface a subtle status indicator so a slow auth resolve shows 'visibility of system status' rather than a frozen brand screen.
  - **Evidencia:** splash_screen.dart:24-39 (_navigate), specifically line 30 `await ref.read(authNotifierProvider.future);` with no error handling; auth_notifier.dart:9-18 build() returns ref.watch(authStateChangesProvider.future)

- **[HIGH · microcopy-i18n]** The headline copy 'MOVÉS EL HIERRO. NOSOTROS EL RESTO.' is hardcoded as raw TextSpans, violating design-system rule #3 (never hard-code UI strings). This is NOT a Fase-6-pending case: the project already has a full AppL10n system, and a dedicated key `authSplashTagline` already exists and is populated in all three ARBs (es: 'ENTRENÁ. COMPARTÍ. CRECÉ.', es_AR same, en: empty). The sibling welcome_screen.dart already localizes its strings via AppL10n.of(context). The splash is the one auth screen that ignores l10n entirely (it does not even import app_l10n.dart).
  - **Fix:** Import app_l10n.dart and render the tagline from AppL10n.of(context).authSplashTagline. Note the content mismatch too: the intended brand tagline for splash is 'ENTRENÁ. COMPARTÍ. CRECÉ.' (already in the ARBs), whereas the screen currently shows the welcome-headline copy 'MOVÉS EL HIERRO...'. Decide which is canonical with design, then drive it from a single l10n key so EN (currently empty) gets filled and long localized strings don't silently diverge across screens.
  - **Evidencia:** splash_screen.dart:77,87,97,107 (hardcoded TextSpans); contrast with intl_es_AR.arb:4 / app_l10n_es.dart:873 `authSplashTagline => 'ENTRENÁ. COMPARTÍ. CRECÉ.'` and welcome_screen.dart:23 `final l10n = AppL10n.of(context);`

- **[MEDIUM · design-system]** The headline uses GoogleFonts.spaceGrotesk, but docs/design-system.md defines only two type families — Barlow Condensed (headings/hero) and Barlow (body) — and Space Grotesk appears NOWHERE in the design docs. Additionally fontSize 24, letterSpacing -0.3, and height 1.2 are ad-hoc literals rather than shared typography tokens; the design system specifies UPPERCASE headings with letter-spacing 0.5–1.0px (positive), so the negative tracking here also contradicts the spec. The 20px horizontal padding and 20px SizedBox are on-scale, so spacing is fine — the issue is the type family and tracking.
  - **Fix:** Switch the headline to GoogleFonts.barlowCondensed with the heading weight/uppercase/letter-spacing the design system prescribes, matching how welcome_screen.dart renders the same brand line (_headlineLine uses the system fonts). If Space Grotesk is genuinely intended as a brand display font, it must be added to docs/design-system.md and a shared text-style token created — not used ad hoc in one screen. Either way, centralize the splash headline style so it can't drift from the welcome headline.
  - **Evidencia:** splash_screen.dart:78-114 (GoogleFonts.spaceGrotesk, fontSize 24, letterSpacing -0.3, height 1.2); design-system.md:42-44 (Barlow Condensed / Barlow only); rg for 'space grotesk' in docs returns nothing

- **[MEDIUM · accessibility]** The screen has no Semantics for screen readers. The TreinoLogo is an SvgPicture with no semanticsLabel (decorative is fine, but the brand name is then never announced), and the headline is built from four separate TextSpans split mid-phrase with an embedded '\n' ('EL HIERRO.\n'). VoiceOver/TalkBack will read these as fragmented chunks and may announce the newline awkwardly, so the screen-reader experience of the only content on the page is degraded. There are no interactive elements, so tap-target size is not a concern here.
  - **Fix:** Wrap the logo+headline in a single Semantics(label: <full tagline>, container: true) (or set a semanticsLabel on the merged text) so assistive tech announces one coherent brand statement instead of four fragments. Mark the decorative radial-glow Container as excludeSemantics. Once the copy comes from l10n, the Semantics label should reuse that same localized string.
  - **Evidencia:** splash_screen.dart:69 (TreinoLogo, no label), 72-118 (RichText with split TextSpans incl. literal '\n' at line 87); treino_logo.dart:37-44 (SvgPicture.asset with no semanticsLabel)

- **[LOW · states]** While auth resolves, the splash shows only the static brand frame with no progress indicator. On a slow or cold network this reads as a frozen screen (no visibility of system status). The code comment notes the artificial 1500ms minimum was intentionally removed, which is good, but nothing replaces it as a 'we're working' signal for genuinely slow resolves.
  - **Fix:** Add a subtle, low-emphasis progress cue (e.g. a small accent-tinted indicator or a gentle logo pulse) that appears only after a short grace period (~300–500ms) so fast resolves stay clean but slow ones communicate activity. Tie it to the loading state and hide it the moment auth resolves or errors.
  - **Evidencia:** splash_screen.dart:45-125 build() renders only Scaffold > Stack(glow + Center(logo+text)); no loading affordance; comment at lines 25-29

## lib/features/auth/presentation/welcome_screen.dart (auth module)

_The Welcome screen is visually polished and handles layout robustly (SliverFillRemaining + Flexible/Wrap guard against overflow and dynamic-type clipping, with good inline rationale). It correctly uses AppPalette tokens throughout — no HEX literals or Colors.* constants except the harmless Colors.transparent in the shared secondary button. The serious gaps are in STATES and ACCESSIBILITY: social sign-in has no error feedback and no in-flight loading indicator, diverging from the sibling login/register screens which both render an AuthFailureBanner; and several interactive/visual elements lack Semantics. There are also two hardcoded Spanish strings (one a known Fase-6 i18n debt) and minor spacing-token deviations._

- **[HIGH · states]** Social sign-in (Google/Apple) has NO error state. _signInWithGoogle/_signInWithApple await the notifier then navigate only when s.hasValue is non-null (lines 223-240). If the auth call fails or the user cancels the OAuth sheet (authNotifierProvider enters hasError), the screen shows nothing — no banner, no snackbar — leaving the user with a button that visibly did nothing. This silently swallows AuthFailure.
  - **Fix:** Mirror the sibling screens: in build(), derive `final failure = authState.hasError && authState.error is AuthFailure ? authState.error as AuthFailure : null;` and render the existing AuthFailureBanner (or a SnackBar) when failure != null. login_screen.dart:88-90,180-183 and register_screen.dart:130-132 already do exactly this — Welcome is the only auth entry point missing it.
  - **Evidencia:** welcome_screen.dart:223-240 (_signInWithGoogle/_signInWithApple, only handles success); contrast login_screen.dart:88-90 + AuthFailureBanner at :180-183

- **[HIGH · states]** No visibility of system status during the OAuth round-trip. While the Google/Apple call is in flight, isLoading only sets onPressed: null, which AuthSecondaryButton renders as a static 0.5-opacity button (auth_secondary_button.dart:47-48) — no spinner. AuthSecondaryButton has no isLoading prop at all. The user taps Google, the native sheet may take seconds to appear, and the UI gives zero feedback that anything is happening. The primary CTA also never uses AuthPillButton's isLoading (it just navigates), so the whole screen has no loading affordance.
  - **Fix:** Add an isLoading parameter to AuthSecondaryButton that swaps the icon/label for a small CircularProgressIndicator (matching AuthPillButton's pattern at auth_pill_button.dart:50-58), and pass the in-flight provider state to whichever social button was tapped. At minimum, show a spinner on the active provider button while authNotifierProvider.isLoading is true.
  - **Evidencia:** welcome_screen.dart:164-176 (onPressed: isLoading ? null : ...); auth_secondary_button.dart:47-48 (disabled = opacity only, no spinner)

- **[MEDIUM · microcopy-i18n]** Hardcoded Spanish UI string bypasses AppL10n: the account-deleted SnackBar uses a literal 'Tu cuenta fue eliminada' (line 36) instead of an AppL10n key. It's flagged in-code as known debt (`// i18n: Fase 6 Etapa 3`), but it's the only user-facing copy on this screen that won't localize and won't pick up es_AR voseo consistency from the ARB files.
  - **Fix:** Add an authAccountDeleted key to the ARB files (intl_es_AR.arb / intl_es.arb / intl_en.arb) and reference l10n.authAccountDeleted. All neighboring copy (eyebrow, body, CTA, sign-in link) is already localized, so this is the lone outlier.
  - **Evidencia:** welcome_screen.dart:34-37

- **[MEDIUM · microcopy-i18n]** The hero headline ('MOVÉS EL HIERRO.' / 'NOSOTROS EL RESTO.') is hardcoded inline in _headlineLine calls (lines 117-126) rather than coming from AppL10n. The two-tone light/bold RichText split is also baked into Dart, so any translation that doesn't split cleanly into a leading word + bold remainder will break the styling. This is the most prominent text on the marketing screen and is not translatable.
  - **Fix:** Move the headline lines into AppL10n. If the light/bold styling must be preserved per locale, model it as two keys per line (e.g. authWelcomeHeadlineLine1Light / ...Bold) or a single key with an agreed markup convention, and document that the bold split is locale-dependent.
  - **Evidencia:** welcome_screen.dart:117-126, _headlineLine at :242-270

- **[MEDIUM · accessibility]** The 'Iniciar sesión' sign-in link is a bare GestureDetector wrapping a Text (lines 196-206). It exposes no button semantics to screen readers (announced as plain text, not a tappable control), and its tap target is only the text's intrinsic height (~18-20pt) — well under the 44pt iOS minimum. Login screen uses the same GestureDetector pattern, so this is a module-wide issue, but it's a primary affordance here.
  - **Fix:** Wrap in a Semantics(button: true, label: l10n.authWelcomeSignIn) or use a TextButton/InkWell with a minimum 44x44 hit area (e.g. constrain with MaterialTapTargetSize or padding). Prefer a real button widget so semantics and tap target come for free.
  - **Evidencia:** welcome_screen.dart:196-206

- **[MEDIUM · accessibility]** No Semantics anywhere on the screen (grep returns zero Semantics/semanticLabel widgets in welcome_screen.dart and treino_logo.dart). The TreinoLogo SVG renders the brand wordmark but exposes no label to VoiceOver, and the decorative accent dot (lines 71-78) is not excluded from the semantics tree. The brand identity and the eyebrow tagline are thus poorly conveyed to screen-reader users.
  - **Fix:** Add a semanticLabel ('TREINO') to TreinoLogo (e.g. pass it to SvgPicture.asset's semanticsLabel), and wrap the purely decorative accent dot in ExcludeSemantics or Semantics(excludeSemantics). The social buttons inherit their label from the visible text, which is fine.
  - **Evidencia:** welcome_screen.dart:99 (TreinoLogo, no label), :71-78 (decorative dot); treino_logo.dart:37-44 (SvgPicture without semanticsLabel)

- **[LOW · design-system]** Two spacing values fall outside the documented scale (8 · 12 · 14 · 18 · 20; design-system.md:49 explicitly forbids 4/16/24): SizedBox(height: 48) at line 68 and SizedBox(height: 24) at line 100. 24 is on the explicit forbidden list. The bottom SizedBox(height: 20) and the others are compliant.
  - **Fix:** Replace 24 with 20 (allowed) and re-derive 48 as a multiple of the scale (e.g. 20+? or document an exception for the top hero inset). Minor, but the design system marks these as non-negotiable rules.
  - **Evidencia:** welcome_screen.dart:68 (height: 48), :100 (height: 24); rule at design-system.md:49

- **[LOW · consistency]** Typography on this screen uses GoogleFonts.spaceGrotesk for the hero headline (line 249/259) while the design-system.md (lines 42-44) specifies Barlow Condensed for headings/hero. The login screen's title also uses spaceGrotesk (login_screen.dart:124), so the two are internally consistent with each other but both diverge from the documented heading font. Eyebrow/body correctly use Barlow Condensed/Barlow.
  - **Fix:** Confirm with the design owner whether spaceGrotesk is the intended hero font for auth screens (in which case update design-system.md) or whether these should be Barlow Condensed. Flagging as a doc-vs-code discrepancy, not a clear bug, since both auth screens agree.
  - **Evidencia:** welcome_screen.dart:249,259 (spaceGrotesk); design-system.md:42-44 (Barlow Condensed for headings); same pattern in login_screen.dart:124

- **[LOW · navigation]** Welcome is the auth root (login/register are pushed on top via context.push), so the absence of a back button is correct — not a dead-end. Worth noting positively: the primary action (EMPEZAR CTA) is unmistakable and the secondary path (Iniciar sesión) is clearly differentiated. No change needed; recorded so it isn't re-flagged.
  - **Fix:** No action. Back affordance is intentionally absent on the root; sibling screens correctly provide AuthCircleBackButton / TreinoIcon.back.
  - **Evidencia:** welcome_screen.dart:149 (push /register), :197 (push /login); back buttons exist in forgot_password_screen.dart:95 and login_screen.dart:111

## lib/features/chat/presentation/chat_list_screen.dart (module: chat)

_The screen is structurally solid: all four AsyncValue states (loading/error/empty/data) are handled at both list and row level, it uses AppPalette tokens and TreinoIcon wrappers correctly with no HEX literals or direct PhosphorIcons, and it has a clean row skeleton, retry-on-error, and a thoughtful empty state. The serious gaps are (1) it is completely un-localized while the rest of the app uses a fully-wired AppL10n system (ES/es_AR voseo/EN), and (2) ChatListScreen is not wired into the router nor reached by any caller, so there is no in-app affordance to open the messages list. Accessibility gaps (no Semantics on the icon-only back button, no semantic label on avatars) and a 6px divider misalignment round out the list._

- **[HIGH · microcopy-i18n]** Every user-facing string on this screen is hardcoded Spanish: the title 'MENSAJES' (line 38), 'Usuario eliminado' (line 113), 'Iniciá la conversación' (line 139), the empty state 'Sin mensajes todavía' + 'Cuando tengas un vínculo activo con un PF, vas a poder chatear desde acá.' (lines 209, 219), the error 'No pudimos cargar tus mensajes.' + 'Reintentar' (lines 244, 248), and the relative-time tokens 'recién' / 'hace Xm/h/d' (lines 260-263). The app already ships a fully wired localization layer (AppL10n in lib/l10n/ with intl_es.arb, intl_es_AR.arb voseo, intl_en.arb; 500+ keys; localizationsDelegates registered in app.dart) that sibling modules (coach, workout, feed) use heavily. This screen bypasses it entirely, so it will render Spanish even under English locale and is the one chat surface with no i18n.
  - **Fix:** Route every string through AppL10n.of(context) with chat-scoped keys (e.g. chatListTitle, chatListDeletedUser, chatListStartConversation, chatListEmptyTitle, chatListEmptyBody, chatListErrorMessage, chatListRetry, plus relative-time keys). Keep the existing voseo phrasing in the es_AR ARB. Note chat_screen.dart has the same problem (hardcoded title/snackbar/hint), so fix the module together. AGENTS.md / design-system.md rule #3 explicitly forbids hardcoded UI strings.
  - **Evidencia:** chat_list_screen.dart lines 38, 113, 139, 209, 219, 244, 248, 258-263

- **[HIGH · navigation]** ChatListScreen is never referenced outside its own file. A repo-wide grep finds only the class definition and a doc comment in chat_providers.dart ('Lo consume ChatListScreen'). It is NOT registered in lib/app/router.dart and no widget pushes it. By contrast ChatScreen (the 1-1 thread) IS reachable from the router at line 412 and from the athlete detail 'MENSAJE' CTA. So the messages-list inbox has no in-app entry point: users can land in an individual chat but cannot open the list of all chats. This is a navigation dead-feature, not just a dead-end.
  - **Fix:** Wire ChatListScreen into navigation: add a route (or a messages entry point in the shell / profile / coach area) and an affordance to reach it (e.g. a messages icon in the relevant AppBar). If the inbox is intentionally deferred, mark it clearly as not-yet-shipped; right now it reads as a finished screen that is silently unreachable.
  - **Evidencia:** grep ChatListScreen across lib returns only chat_list_screen.dart (def) + chat_providers.dart (comment); router.dart line 412 wires ChatScreen but not the list

- **[MEDIUM · accessibility]** Icon-only controls lack semantic labels. The AppBar back button (lines 33-36) is a bare IconButton with no tooltip/Semantics — VoiceOver announces it generically. The PostAvatar images (lines 117-121) carry no semantic label, so a screen reader gets no person identity for each row, and the empty-state icon (line 206) is decorative but not excluded from semantics. Compare chat_screen.dart line 289 which at least gives the send button tooltip: 'Enviar'.
  - **Fix:** Add tooltip/Semantics to the back button (e.g. tooltip: l10n.commonBack). Wrap or label PostAvatar so the row reads as the contact name (the row Text already exposes the name, so consider marking the avatar image decorative via Semantics(excludeSemantics) to avoid duplicate announcements, or give it label = name). Mark the empty-state icon decorative. This is a module-wide pattern worth fixing in PostAvatar once.
  - **Evidencia:** chat_list_screen.dart lines 33-36 (back IconButton), 117-121 (PostAvatar), 206 (empty icon)

- **[LOW · states]** The list-level loading branch (lines 48-50) is a bare centered CircularProgressIndicator with no context, while the screen already has a much nicer per-row _RowSkeleton (lines 169-192). The bare spinner gives a jarring spinner-then-list flash and less perceived performance than a skeleton list, and is inconsistent with the polished row skeleton the screen otherwise uses.
  - **Fix:** Replace the centered spinner with a short ListView of 5-6 _RowSkeleton placeholders so the loading state matches the loaded layout (skeleton screens reduce perceived latency and keep visual continuity). Reuse the existing _RowSkeleton widget.
  - **Evidencia:** chat_list_screen.dart lines 47-50 (loading) vs 169-192 (_RowSkeleton)

- **[LOW · visual-hierarchy]** The separator Divider uses indent: 76 (line 62), but the actual text content starts at horizontal padding 20 + avatar 48 + gap 14 = 82px from the edge. The divider therefore under-indents by 6px and does not align with the start of the contact name / message text, breaking the spacing rhythm. 76 also isn't on the project spacing scale (8/12/14/18/20).
  - **Fix:** Set indent to 82 to align the divider exactly with the text column (or derive it from the same constants used for padding + avatar size + gap so it stays correct if the avatar size changes).
  - **Evidencia:** chat_list_screen.dart line 62 (indent: 76) vs lines 105/121/122 (padding 20 + avatar size 48 + SizedBox width 14)

- **[LOW · design-system]** Typography uses ad-hoc font sizes and TextStyle literals rather than shared text tokens/styles: row title fontSize 15/w700 (lines 129-133), subtitle 13 (140-143), timestamp 12 (154-157), and inline GoogleFonts.barlowCondensed calls for the AppBar title and empty-state heading (lines 39, 210). The design-system defines a Barlow/Barlow Condensed type scale but there is no shared TextStyle helper, so every screen re-specifies sizes. Values like 15 and 13 are also off the documented spacing/scale discipline. This is consistent with the rest of the codebase (GoogleFonts is called directly in many screens), so it is a systemic gap rather than a one-off violation.
  - **Fix:** Lower severity / systemic: introduce shared text styles (e.g. AppText.titleSm, AppText.body, AppText.caption, AppText.sectionHeading) sourced from the design-system scale and use them here instead of inline TextStyle + GoogleFonts. Not blocking for this screen alone, but flag so the chat screens adopt the helper when it lands.
  - **Evidencia:** chat_list_screen.dart lines 39-44, 129-133, 140-143, 154-157, 210-215

## lib/features/chat/presentation/chat_screen.dart (module: chat)

_The chat screen is structurally solid and mostly design-system compliant: it uses AppPalette.of(context) consistently (no HEX/Colors.* literals except intentional Colors.transparent on the scaffold/appbar), routes icons through TreinoIcon, and handles all three AsyncValue branches (loading/error/data) with a dedicated empty state. The main weaknesses are systemic, not cosmetic: (1) every user-facing string is hardcoded despite a live AppL10n + ARB infrastructure used across the rest of the app (the inline "i18n: Fase 6 Etapa 3" comments confirm this is known-pending); (2) accessibility gaps — icon-only back button has no semantic label, the send button's busy state isn't announced, and font sizes are hardcoded so large dynamic type can clip; (3) message bubbles show no timestamp even though Message.createdAt exists, hurting visibility of system status and recognition; (4) the error state is a dead-end with no retry, inconsistent with its sibling chat_list_screen which offers one. Several findings apply equally to the sibling, so fixes should be considered at module level._

- **[HIGH · microcopy-i18n]** Every user-facing string on the screen is hardcoded in Spanish instead of going through AppL10n.of(context), even though the app has a fully wired localization layer (lib/l10n/app_l10n.dart + intl_es.arb / intl_es_AR.arb / intl_en.arb) that dozens of other screens already consume (e.g. profile_cuenta_section.dart uses l10n.profileCuentaTitle). The chat module has zero entries in the ARB files. Affected strings: appbar fallbacks 'Usuario' (l99) and 'Usuario eliminado' (l107), error 'No pudimos cargar los mensajes.' (l146), send-failure snackbar 'No pudimos enviar el mensaje. Probá de nuevo.' (l72), composer hint 'Escribí un mensaje…' (l269), send tooltip 'Enviar' (l289), and the empty-state title/body (l312, l322). The English locale would render this screen entirely in Spanish.
  - **Fix:** Add chat keys to the ARB files (e.g. chatErrorLoadMessages, chatSendFailed, chatComposerHint, chatSendTooltip, chatEmptyTitle, chatEmptyBody, chatUserFallback, chatUserDeleted), regenerate AppL10n, and replace the literals with AppL10n.of(context).x. Keep the warm voseo tone that already exists. Do the same pass on the sibling chat_list_screen.dart, which has the identical problem.
  - **Evidencia:** chat_screen.dart lines 72, 99, 107, 146, 269, 289, 312, 322; ARB files have no chat* keys

- **[HIGH · accessibility]** The icon-only back button (IconButton with Icon(TreinoIcon.back), l93-96) has no tooltip and no Semantics label, so VoiceOver announces nothing meaningful for the primary way to leave the screen. The send button (l279-290) does have a tooltip 'Enviar' which screen readers announce, but when sending it swaps the icon for a CircularProgressIndicator with no semantic label, so the busy/disabled state is invisible to assistive tech. The PostAvatar in the appbar title also carries no explicit semantics.
  - **Fix:** Give the back IconButton a localized tooltip (e.g. l10n.commonBack -> 'Volver'). When _sending, wrap the spinner or button with a Semantics(label: 'Enviando…', enabled: false) so the state change is announced. Confirm PostAvatar exposes the author name to semantics or wrap it in Semantics(label: name).
  - **Evidencia:** chat_screen.dart lines 93-96 (back, no tooltip/semantics), 281-288 (spinner has no semantic label)

- **[MEDIUM · accessibility]** All text sizes are hardcoded pixel values (fontSize: 16 appbar, 14 bubble/composer, 13 empty body, 12 timestamps in sibling) with maxLines:1 + ellipsis on the appbar name. None of these scale with MediaQuery textScaler, and the bubble text has no maxLines guard. With large iOS Dynamic Type the appbar title will clip early and long messages stay readable but the composer (maxLines:5) plus enlarged text can crowd the send button. iOS-first apps are expected to honor Dynamic Type.
  - **Fix:** Prefer Theme text styles / tokens that respect textScaler over raw fontSize literals, or at minimum verify the layout at the largest accessibility text size. Avoid maxLines:1 on the conversation partner's name where vertical space allows, or test that ellipsis is acceptable at large scale.
  - **Evidencia:** chat_screen.dart lines 101, 120-122 (appbar 16 + maxLines 1), 224-225 (bubble 14), 264 (composer 14), 324 (empty body 13)

- **[MEDIUM · states]** The messages error branch (l142-150) is a dead-end: it shows static text 'No pudimos cargar los mensajes.' with no way to retry. The sibling chat_list_screen.dart handles the same situation with a Retry button that calls ref.invalidate (l51-52, l248), so this screen is inconsistent and leaves the user stuck if the stream errors transiently. Additionally, the send-failure path surfaces only a transient SnackBar (l70-74); a failed message simply disappears from the input with no persisted error affordance or way to re-send the drafted text.
  - **Fix:** Add a Reintentar action to the error state that invalidates messagesProvider(widget.chatId), mirroring the sibling's _ErrorState. Consider keeping the typed text in the field on send failure (currently it is only cleared on success, which is correct) and optionally showing an inline error/resend marker rather than relying solely on a SnackBar.
  - **Evidencia:** chat_screen.dart lines 142-150 (no retry) vs chat_list_screen.dart lines 51-52, 230-254 (retry exists)

- **[MEDIUM · usability]** Message bubbles render only message.text (l221-227) and never show a timestamp, even though the Message model has createdAt (a DateTime). This hurts visibility of system status and recognition-over-recall — the user cannot tell when anything was said, and there is no sent/delivered indicator on their own messages. The chat list already formats relative time, so the data and a formatting approach exist in the module.
  - **Fix:** Render a small timestamp (and optionally a sent indicator on isMine bubbles) using palette.textMuted, reusing a relative/absolute time formatter like the one in chat_list_screen.dart's _relativeTime. Group by day if feasible.
  - **Evidencia:** chat_screen.dart lines 221-227 (text only); message.dart createdAt field exists; chat_list_screen.dart _relativeTime helper

- **[MEDIUM · accessibility]** The send IconButton relies on Flutter's default IconButton hit area. The visual icon is small (default 24) and there is no explicit BoxConstraints/minimum size enforcing the 44pt iOS minimum tap target. Default IconButton padding usually yields ~48dp, so this is likely acceptable, but it is unverified and the spinner-state button (18x18 child) is visually tiny. Worth confirming the effective tap target is >= 44pt in both idle and sending states.
  - **Fix:** Verify the send button's hit area meets 44pt in both states; if not, add constraints: const BoxConstraints(minWidth: 44, minHeight: 44). Keep the visual spinner centered within that target.
  - **Evidencia:** chat_screen.dart lines 279-290 (IconButton, no explicit min-size constraints)

- **[LOW · consistency]** Spacing values mostly respect the documented scale (8/12/14/18/20) but a few ad-hoc values appear: bubble vertical margin 4 (l214) and the asymmetric bubble corner radius of 4 (l204-205). The design system says the spacing scale is only 8/12/14/18/20 and explicitly NOT 4. The radius 4 is a deliberate chat-tail flourish (defensible), but the 4px margin and the bubble radius 14 (a non-token value vs documented r-sm 12) drift from the system.
  - **Fix:** Align the bubble vertical margin to 8 and the bubble corner to the r-sm token (12) unless the chat tail intentionally requires 14/4; if intentional, note it as a sanctioned exception. Low priority since it is visually minor.
  - **Evidencia:** chat_screen.dart lines 201-205 (radius 14/4), 214 (margin vertical 4); design-system.md spacing scale 8/12/14/18/20, radii r-sm 12

- **[LOW · design-system]** The empty-state title uses GoogleFonts.barlowCondensed directly (l313) rather than a shared text token/component. This matches the sibling screen and the design-system heading spec (Barlow Condensed 700, uppercase, letter-spacing), but the title is 'Sin mensajes todavía' in Title Case, not UPPERCASE as the heading spec prescribes for section titles, while chat_list_screen uses 'MENSAJES' uppercase. Minor inconsistency in heading casing within the same module.
  - **Fix:** Decide on a consistent heading casing for empty-state titles (the system says UPPERCASE for headings) and ideally extract a shared heading text widget so casing/letter-spacing are not re-specified per screen.
  - **Evidencia:** chat_screen.dart lines 311-318 (Title Case heading) vs chat_list_screen.dart line 38 'MENSAJES' uppercase; design-system.md typography heading = UPPERCASE

## lib/features/coach/coach_screen.dart (Coach tab — athlete + trainer views)

_CoachScreen is a clean, well-reasoned role router (athlete vs trainer) that delegates to AthleteCoachView and TrainerCoachView. Loading/empty/error states are mostly handled across both child views, design-system discipline is generally strong (AppPalette + TreinoIcon throughout, no PhosphorIcons or HEX literals, Colors.* only used for the semantically-correct transparent). The notable gaps are: (1) a hard i18n bug — agendaButtonLabel is an empty string in English, so the Agenda button renders with no label; (2) significant inconsistency in localization — the two views mix ~5 AppL10n keys with a dozen hardcoded Spanish strings (status labels, button labels, confirm dialogs, snackbars) even though the module already has an L10n layer and a CoachStrings file; (3) zero Semantics labels and sub-44pt tap targets on icon-only controls (alias copy button, status pill avatars are decorative but the copy affordance is interactive); (4) minor spacing-token violations (16/4 used where the scale forbids them). None are architectural; most are localized polish + one real localization bug._

- **[HIGH · microcopy-i18n]** The Agenda button label is an empty string in the English locale. intl_en.arb:97 and app_l10n_en.dart:282 both define agendaButtonLabel as "". The button is rendered in _AgendaButton via l10n.agendaButtonLabel (athlete_coach_view.dart:600-601), so for any English-locale athlete with an active link the primary 'view PF agenda' button shows an icon followed by NO text — looks broken/unlabeled and is also unreadable to a screen reader.
  - **Fix:** Provide an English translation for agendaButtonLabel (e.g. "VIEW PF AGENDA" / "PF SCHEDULE") in intl_en.arb and app_l10n_en.dart. Add a CI check or arb-completeness lint so empty string values fail the build rather than shipping silently.
  - **Evidencia:** lib/l10n/intl_en.arb:97 ("agendaButtonLabel": ""); lib/l10n/app_l10n_en.dart:282; consumed at lib/features/coach/athlete_coach_view.dart:585,600-601

- **[MEDIUM · microcopy-i18n]** Inconsistent localization across the two views. A handful of strings go through AppL10n (athleteCoachViewLinkError, athleteCoachViewTrainerFallbackName, agendaButtonLabel) but the majority of user-facing copy is hardcoded Spanish literals: status labels SOLICITUD ENVIADA / TU PERSONAL TRAINER / VÍNCULO PAUSADO (athlete_coach_view.dart:229-232), every confirm-dialog title/body (lines 324-330, 382-383, 393-394), button labels CANCELAR SOLICITUD / MENSAJE / TERMINAR VÍNCULO (467,494,517,548), the share toggle + cuota copy (362,669,696,752,819), snackbars 'No pudimos abrir el chat...' / 'Alias copiado.' (570,804), and on the trainer side 'No pudimos cargar tus alumnos.' / 'Sin alumnos activos todavía.' / PAUSAR/REANUDAR/TERMINAR VÍNCULO (trainer_coach_view.dart:123,143,290,322,354). The design-system rule (#3) and the existing AppL10n layer + CoachStrings file make this an established expectation the screen only partially follows.
  - **Fix:** Route all user-facing strings in both views through AppL10n (or at minimum CoachStrings for the literals that are still pending l10n). This removes the per-string drift and prevents future empty-translation bugs like agendaButtonLabel from going unnoticed.
  - **Evidencia:** lib/features/coach/athlete_coach_view.dart:229-232,324-330,467,494,517,548,570,669,696,752,804,819; lib/features/coach/trainer_coach_view.dart:123,143,290,322,354

- **[MEDIUM · accessibility]** Icon-only / undersized interactive controls have no Semantics labels and tap targets below the 44pt iOS minimum. The alias 'copy' affordance is an Icon(size:18) inside Padding(all:4) ≈ 26x26pt with no semantic label — a screen reader announces nothing actionable and it's hard to hit (athlete_coach_view.dart:799-813). The TrainerCoachView segmented TabBar tabs are height:40 (<44pt) (trainer_coach_view.dart:74). Across both files there are zero Semantics/semanticLabel/tooltip usages, so screen-reader users get no description for the avatar-tap-to-profile gesture (_TrainerHeader GestureDetector, line 249) or the copy button.
  - **Fix:** Wrap the copy control in a Semantics(button:true, label:'Copiar alias') and give it a >=44pt hit area (e.g. IconButton with constraints or a SizedBox(48)). Raise the TabBar tab height to 44 (or add explicit minimum hit target). Add a Semantics label to the _TrainerHeader tappable row ('Ver perfil de <nombre>').
  - **Evidencia:** lib/features/coach/athlete_coach_view.dart:799-813 (copy icon 18px + 4px pad), :249-251 (avatar GestureDetector, no label); lib/features/coach/trainer_coach_view.dart:74 (Tab height:40)

- **[LOW · states]** Two AsyncValue reads lack explicit non-data branches, both intentional but worth noting. _CuotaSection collapses loading AND no-billing into the same SizedBox.shrink() via state==null (athlete_coach_view.dart:649), so a slow cuota fetch shows nothing with no skeleton/spinner — acceptable since it's a secondary section, but there's no visible 'cargando cuota' status. The trainer_byId alias read (line 651) has no error branch; on error rawAlias falls through to the 'todavía no cargó un alias' copy, which is a reasonable graceful degrade. The top-level CoachScreen loading view is a deliberate blank SizedBox.expand() (ADR-3) which is fine, but on a cold cache the entire Coach tab is empty with no indication anything is happening.
  - **Fix:** Consider a lightweight inline shimmer/placeholder for _CuotaSection while loading, and optionally a subtle delayed (e.g. 400ms) indicator on the cold-cache CoachScreen blank state so a slow first load doesn't read as a broken/empty tab. Low priority — current behavior is defensible per ADR-3.
  - **Evidencia:** lib/features/coach/coach_screen.dart:37-48; lib/features/coach/athlete_coach_view.dart:649,651-653

- **[LOW · design-system]** Spacing values outside the allowed scale (8·12·14·18·20). athlete_coach_view.dart uses SizedBox(height:16) at line 216 and SizedBox(height:4) at line 283, both explicitly banned by design-system.md ('No usar 4 / 16 / 24'). Radii are also slightly ad-hoc: cards use BorderRadius.circular(20) (=r-lg hero) for a standard link card where r-md(16) is the documented card token (line 191), and the trainer pill uses radius 24 (line 54) which isn't a defined radius token.
  - **Fix:** Replace height:16 with 14 or 18 and height:4 with the nearest token; align card radius to r-md(16) unless this is intentionally a hero card. Better long-term: expose the spacing/radii scale as named constants (AppSpacing.md etc.) so off-scale values are caught at the call site instead of by review.
  - **Evidencia:** lib/features/coach/athlete_coach_view.dart:216 (height:16), :283 (height:4), :191 (radius 20 on standard card); lib/features/coach/trainer_coach_view.dart:54 (radius 24)

- **[LOW · consistency]** The terminate review bottom sheet in _ActionRow uses backgroundColor: Colors.transparent (athlete_coach_view.dart:437) while the 30-day prompt sheet for the same ReviewBottomSheet uses backgroundColor: AppPalette.of(context).bgCard with a rounded top (lines 109-112). Same component, two different sheet chromes depending on entry point — the transparent one relies on the child to paint its own surface, the other doesn't. Inconsistent and easy to get subtly wrong visually.
  - **Fix:** Standardize how ReviewBottomSheet is presented (one helper that always applies bgCard + the top radius, or make the sheet always paint its own background and drop the per-call backgroundColor). Pick one and reuse it in both call sites.
  - **Evidencia:** lib/features/coach/athlete_coach_view.dart:105-112 vs :433-438

## lib/features/coach/presentation/athlete_agenda_screen.dart (Coach module — athlete's read-only agenda)

_The screen is well-structured and largely compliant with the TREINO design system: all colors go through AppPalette.of(context) with zero HEX literals, all icons use TreinoIcon.X, and the AsyncValue.when covers loading/error/data. The most important gaps are UX/completeness rather than design-token violations: there is no empty state for an athlete with zero upcoming sessions (the screen just shows a bare calendar), several user-facing strings are hardcoded in Spanish instead of AppL10n, icon-only elements lack Semantics labels, and tap targets in the day-sheet/calendar are below 44pt. Spacing also diverges from the documented 8/12/14/18/20 scale. None are blockers, but the empty state and the hardcoded strings are worth fixing before this ships._

- **[HIGH · states]** No empty state for an athlete with zero upcoming sessions. In _body (lines 122-140) the upcoming list is gated behind `if (upcoming.isNotEmpty)`. When the athlete has no confirmed/upcoming sessions, the body renders ONLY the calendar followed by nothing — no message, no guidance. This is the most common state for a new athlete and currently looks like a half-rendered screen. The _DaySessionsSheet has an empty branch ('No tenés sesiones este día.', line 333) but the main screen does not.
  - **Fix:** Add an explicit empty state below the calendar when `confirmed.isEmpty` (or `upcoming.isEmpty`): a centered icon + short copy explaining that the trainer schedules sessions and none are booked yet, e.g. an AppL10n key like agendaNoUpcomingSessions ('Tu PF todavía no te agendó sesiones.'). Reuse the muted-text + centered-icon pattern already used for the error state.
  - **Evidencia:** _body lines 100-142, esp. `if (upcoming.isNotEmpty) ...` line 123

- **[HIGH · microcopy-i18n]** Hardcoded user-facing Spanish strings bypass AppL10n, violating design-system rule #3 (never hard-code UI strings). Confirmed NOT present in any ARB/app_l10n_es.dart: 'No tenés sesiones este día.' (line 333) and the trainer-name fallback 'Tu PF' (lines 367 and 436, duplicated). The rest of the screen correctly uses AppL10n (agendaScreenTitle, agendaUpcomingAppointmentsHeading, agendaGenericError).
  - **Fix:** Move all three into AppL10n: add agendaDaySheetNoSessions and agendaTrainerFallbackName keys (es_AR + en placeholders), and replace the literals. Deduplicate the 'Tu PF' fallback so both _SessionRow and AppointmentTile read the same key.
  - **Evidencia:** lines 333 ('No tenés sesiones este día.'), 367 and 436 ('Tu PF')

- **[MEDIUM · accessibility]** Icon-only / decorative elements have no Semantics labels, so VoiceOver announces unlabeled buttons or skips meaning. The AppBar back IconButton (lines 58-61) has no semanticLabel/tooltip. The calendar chevrons (leftChevronIcon/rightChevronIcon, lines 261-262) are bare Icons. The leading clock icon (line 385) and calendar icon (line 449) inside list rows are decorative but not excluded from the semantics tree, adding noise. The sibling athlete_detail_screen.dart already sets tooltips on its IconButtons, so this screen is inconsistent with established module practice.
  - **Fix:** Add tooltip/semanticLabel to the back button (e.g. l10n back/'Volver') and to the calendar chevrons (mes anterior / mes siguiente). Wrap the purely decorative row icons in ExcludeSemantics or pass semanticLabel: '' so screen readers don't read them. This matches the tooltip pattern in athlete_detail_screen.dart:1537/1546.
  - **Evidencia:** lines 58-61 (back IconButton), 261-262 (chevrons), 385 & 449 (decorative icons)

- **[MEDIUM · accessibility]** No protection against large dynamic type. There is zero maxLines/overflow/FittedBox/textScaler handling anywhere in the file. The single-line range string in _SessionRow ('$start – $end · ${appointment.durationMin} min', line 373) and the dense AppointmentTile subtitle ('time · min · trainerName', line 468) sit in fixed-padding rows; at large accessibility text sizes plus a long trainer displayName they will overflow or clip. The trainer name is user-controlled length, compounding the risk.
  - **Fix:** Add softWrap/maxLines + TextOverflow.ellipsis (or allow wrapping) to the range and subtitle Texts, and verify rows grow vertically rather than clip under MediaQuery textScaler. Consider moving the trainer name to its own line on small widths.
  - **Evidencia:** lines 373/391-398 (_SessionRow range), 468 (AppointmentTile subtitle); no maxLines/overflow anywhere in file

- **[MEDIUM · accessibility]** Sub-44pt tap targets. Calendar day cells from table_calendar and the chevron Icons (lines 261-262, default ~24pt icons with no enforced padding) fall below the iOS 44pt minimum, making month navigation and day selection error-prone — especially relevant since tapping a day is the primary interaction that opens the day sheet (SCENARIO-510).
  - **Fix:** Wrap the chevron icons so their hit area is >=44pt (e.g. a sized IconButton/InkWell with padding) and set table_calendar's rowHeight / cell sizing to guarantee >=44pt day cells.
  - **Evidencia:** headerStyle chevrons lines 261-262; TableCalendar config lines 220-274 (no rowHeight set)

- **[LOW · design-system]** Spacing diverges from the documented scale. design-system.md restricts spacing to 8/12/14/18/20 and explicitly says NOT to use 4/16/24. The screen uses 16 and 24 repeatedly: ListView padding horizontal:16 (line 101), SizedBox(height: 24) (line 120), AppointmentTile padding horizontal:16 (line 440), and several 2px micro-gaps (lines 399, 466) which are off-scale. Colors and icons are fully compliant — this is the only token-level drift.
  - **Fix:** Normalize to the allowed scale: replace 16 with 14 or 18, 24 with 20, and the 2px gaps with 8 (or accept them as intentional optical kerning, but document it). Low severity since it is purely cosmetic rhythm, but it is a stated non-negotiable rule.
  - **Evidencia:** lines 101 (h:16), 120 (24), 440 (16), 399 & 466 (2px); rule at docs/design-system.md line 49

- **[LOW · states]** Loading and error states lack context. Loading is a bare centered CircularProgressIndicator (lines 73-75) with no skeleton or label; error (lines 176-181) shows only muted text with no retry affordance. Per Nielsen visibility-of-system-status and user-control, the athlete cannot recover from an error without leaving the screen.
  - **Fix:** Give the error state a retry action (button that calls ref.invalidate(appointmentsForAthleteStreamProvider)) and consider a lightweight skeleton/labelled spinner for loading. Low severity because the stream auto-recovers, but a retry improves perceived control.
  - **Evidencia:** lines 72-78 (when), 176-181 (_errorState)

- **[LOW · consistency]** Two near-identical appointment row widgets (_SessionRow lines 357-414 and AppointmentTile lines 421-481) duplicate layout, the 'Tu PF' fallback, the trainer-name provider watch, and styling with subtly different paddings (14/12 vs 16/14), radii (12 vs 14) and icons (clock vs calendar). This duplication is why the hardcoded fallback string appears twice and risks the two rows drifting visually over time.
  - **Fix:** Extract a shared private row widget (parameterized by icon + primary/secondary text) so styling, the l10n trainer-name fallback, and overflow handling live in one place and stay consistent across the list and the day sheet.
  - **Evidencia:** _SessionRow lines 357-414 vs AppointmentTile lines 421-481

## lib/features/coach/presentation/athlete_detail_screen.dart (Coach module — trainer's athlete drill-down)

_The screen is structurally solid (good AsyncValue handling with loading/error/empty branches in every section, correct AppPalette and TreinoIcon usage, pill CTAs, confirm-before-delete). The main issues are: (1) massive i18n debt — roughly 30+ user-facing Spanish strings are hardcoded inline instead of going through AppL10n, even though the file already imports and uses AppL10n for ~10 keys, making localization inconsistent and the es-AR/en ARB files incomplete; (2) several accessibility gaps — icon-only edit/delete buttons drop below the 44pt tap target via empty BoxConstraints, the back button and avatar lack Semantics labels, and fixed font sizes won't scale with dynamic type; (3) minor design-system spacing drift (a hardcoded fontSize:15 and width:4 outside the documented scale). No invented problems — the async-state coverage and palette discipline are genuinely good._

- **[HIGH · microcopy-i18n]** ~30+ user-facing strings are hardcoded in Spanish instead of routed through AppL10n, despite the file already importing AppL10n and localizing ~10 keys. This is inconsistent (some strings localized, neighboring ones not) and leaves intl_en.arb empty for these, so English/es-generic builds will show raw Spanish or blanks. Affected: section headers 'ANTROPOMETRÍA' (L464), 'RENDIMIENTO' (L727), 'COBRO' (L904), 'NOTA DEL ALUMNO' (L1242,1419), '+ Cargar' (L476,739), 'Configurar'/'Editar'/'Agregar' affordances (L917,1254), all card states ('Cargando…', 'No pudimos cargar las medidas.', 'Sin mediciones todavía. Cargá la primera.', 'Sin configurar.', 'Sin nota.', etc.), metric labels ('Peso','% Graso','Masa muscular','Cintura','CMJ','Sentadilla 1RM','Sprint 20m','VO2máx'), count lines ('medición/es registrada/s'), the delete-dialog body (L319), sheet titles/labels ('CONFIGURAR COBRO','PRECIO (ARS)','CADENCIA','GUARDAR' L1110-1206), TextField hints (L1136,1435), all SnackBar errors (L295,355,1078,1387), the 'Error cargando planes:' label (L139), and tooltips 'Editar plan'/'Eliminar plan' (L1537,1546).
  - **Fix:** Move every user-facing literal to AppL10n keys and fill intl_es_AR / intl_es / intl_en. Use ICU plural for the count lines ('{count, plural, one{medición registrada} other{mediciones registradas}}') instead of the manual ternaries at L578/831. The screen already has the AppL10n pattern established — apply it uniformly so no section is half-localized.
  - **Evidencia:** Lines 139, 295, 319, 355, 464, 476, 493-596, 645, 727, 739, 756-849, 881-884, 904, 917, 934-949, 1078, 1110-1206, 1242, 1254, 1271-1286, 1387, 1419-1471, 1537, 1546

- **[HIGH · accessibility]** The edit and delete IconButtons in _PlanCard pass `constraints: const BoxConstraints()`, which removes Flutter's default 48x48 minimum tap target. With an 18pt icon and only 8pt left padding, the effective hit area is well under the 44pt minimum, and the two buttons sit adjacent — easy to mis-tap (especially dangerous since one is a destructive delete).
  - **Fix:** Set `constraints: const BoxConstraints(minWidth: 44, minHeight: 44)` (or drop the override to keep the default) and rely on padding for visual spacing. Consider increasing horizontal gap between the two adjacent buttons given one is destructive.
  - **Evidencia:** _PlanCard, lines 1534-1549 (constraints: const BoxConstraints() at 1538/1547)

- **[MEDIUM · accessibility]** Icon-only / decorative controls lack Semantics labels. The back IconButton (L57-61) has no semanticLabel or tooltip — a screen reader announces only 'button'. The avatar placeholder Icon in _AthleteHeader (L384-385) is decorative with no label or ExcludeSemantics. The '+ Cargar', 'Configurar/Editar', 'Agregar/Editar' affordances are bare GestureDetector+Text (L473, 736, 913, 1251) with no Semantics button role, so they aren't reliably exposed as tappable actions to assistive tech and have no defined tap-target size.
