  - **Fix:** Add a semanticLabel/tooltip to the back button (localized 'Volver'). Wrap the avatar icon in ExcludeSemantics or give the header a single merged semantic label. Replace the GestureDetector+Text affordances with TextButton (gives button semantics + a 48pt target for free) or wrap them in Semantics(button: true, label: …).
  - **Evidencia:** Lines 57-61 (back), 384-385 (avatar), 473-483, 736-746, 913-924, 1251-1261 (GestureDetector affordances)

- **[MEDIUM · accessibility]** All typography uses fixed `fontSize:` values (12–20) with no MediaQuery textScaler clamping or layout headroom. Combined with single-line headers and Row-based metric chips, large dynamic type risks clipping/overflow. The metric values (e.g. 'VO2máx 45 ml/kg/min') already pack a lot into a Wrap; at large scale the header Row at L461-485 (title + Spacer + '+ Cargar') can overflow horizontally.
  - **Fix:** Verify the screen at the largest accessibility text size. Where fixed sizes are unavoidable, ensure parents allow wrapping/ellipsis and avoid Row layouts that can't reflow. Consider deriving sizes from the theme text styles so they participate in scaling.
  - **Evidencia:** Pervasive fixed fontSize usage; header rows at 461-485, 724-748, 901-926; metric chips 658-688

- **[MEDIUM · states]** Loading and error states give the user no recovery affordance and limited context. The top-level body shows a bare centered CircularProgressIndicator with no label (L116-120). The plans error branch (L131-154) dumps the raw `plansAsync.error.toString()` to the user — an internal/technical leak, and unlike the other sections it has no retry. None of the error cards (measurements, performance, billing, note) offer a retry/refresh action; the user is stuck unless they leave and re-enter.
  - **Fix:** Replace raw error.toString() with a friendly localized message (log the technical detail instead). Add a 'Reintentar' action to error states that calls ref.invalidate(...) on the relevant provider (the delete flow already uses invalidate, so the pattern exists). Optionally give the top spinner a localized 'Cargando…' label for visibility of system status.
  - **Evidencia:** Lines 116-120 (unlabeled spinner), 131-154 (raw error.toString, no retry), 500-509/763-772/938-944/1275-1281 (error cards without retry)

- **[LOW · consistency]** The athlete display name is rendered twice on first view: in the header bar next to the back button (L63-80) and again in _AthleteHeader inside the scroll body (L388-398). On load both show the '...' placeholder simultaneously, and once loaded the same name appears stacked near the top — redundant and slightly confusing about which is the title.
  - **Fix:** Pick one as the canonical title. Typically keep the name in the sticky header bar and make _AthleteHeader the avatar + a secondary line (e.g. role/email), or vice versa — avoid showing the identical name twice in the same viewport.
  - **Evidencia:** Header bar Text at lines 63-80; _AthleteHeader name Text at lines 388-398

- **[LOW · design-system]** A few values fall outside the documented design-system scales. The Cobro amount uses fontSize:15 (L960) — not on any documented type ramp and the only 15 in the file. SizedBox(width:4) appears at L62 and L676; 4 is explicitly called out in design-system.md as a value NOT to use (allowed scale is 8/12/14/18/20). The screen also has no shared card/section-header component: the `_card(...)` helper and the section-header Row are copy-pasted across four sections (Antropometría/Rendimiento/Cobro/Nota), so any token change must be made in several places.
  - **Fix:** Snap fontSize:15 to a ramp value (14 or 18) and replace the width:4 gaps with 8. Extract the repeated `_card` and section-header Row into shared widgets (e.g. CoachSectionCard / CoachSectionHeader) so spacing/typography stays consistent and DRY across the four sections.
  - **Evidencia:** fontSize:15 at L960; SizedBox(width:4) at L62 and L676; duplicated _card() at L611, 864, 1002, 1324 and header Rows at L461, 724, 901, 1239

## lib/features/coach/presentation/availability_editor_screen.dart (Coach module — Availability Editor)

_The Availability Editor is structurally clean and reuses palette tokens correctly, but it diverges from its own module's conventions on several real axes. It bypasses TreinoIcon for 7 raw Material icons, hardcodes ~12 Spanish UI strings despite a working AppL10n layer that the same file already uses, and—most importantly—has no loading/error states: it collapses both AsyncValue streams into `valueOrNull ?? []`, so a stream error renders as a deceptive empty list with no retry, while the sibling athlete_agenda_screen.dart does it right with `.when(loading/error/data)` and a `_errorState`. Save failures are silently swallowed, leaving the user with a stuck-feeling sheet. Destructive delete actions use the magenta `highlight` (a celebratory brand color) instead of the `danger` token, and icon-only buttons lack Semantics labels. None of these are nitpicks; each has a concrete fix and a same-module precedent._

- **[HIGH · states]** Both data streams are read with `rulesAsync.valueOrNull ?? const []` / `overridesAsync.valueOrNull ?? const []` (lines 78-79). This collapses loading AND error into the empty branch: on first load the user sees the empty-state hints ('Sin horarios configurados.') before data arrives, and if the stream errors they see the SAME empty state with no indication anything went wrong and no way to retry. The screen has no loading spinner and no error branch at all.
  - **Fix:** Mirror the module's own pattern in athlete_agenda_screen.dart: use `appointmentsAsync.when(loading:, error:, data:)` with a CircularProgressIndicator(color: palette.accent) for loading and the existing `_errorState`-style widget (a message + a 'Reintentar' button that calls `ref.invalidate(...)`) for error. Distinguish 'no rules configured yet' (true empty) from 'couldn't load' (error).
  - **Evidencia:** Lines 71-79 (valueOrNull fallbacks); contrast athlete_agenda_screen.dart:72-78 which uses .when() + _errorState() with retry.

- **[HIGH · states]** Both save flows swallow errors silently: `_save` in _RuleFormSheet (line 568 `catch (_) { // ignore save errors in this phase }`) and in _BlockOverrideFormSheet (line 710 `catch (_) { // ignore }`). On a failed write the spinner stops, the sheet stays open, and nothing tells the user the save failed — they will assume it worked or tap again, risking confusion/duplicates. This violates Nielsen's 'visibility of system status' and error-recovery.
  - **Fix:** On catch, show a SnackBar with an error message (via AppL10n) and keep the sheet open so the user can retry; only pop on success. The validation path already uses ScaffoldMessenger (line 537) — reuse that for the failure case too.
  - **Evidencia:** Lines 568-572 and 710-714 (empty catch blocks). Line 536-540 shows ScaffoldMessenger is already available for feedback.

- **[MEDIUM · design-system]** Seven icons are instantiated as raw Material icons instead of the mandated TreinoIcon wrapper, breaking the 'never PhosphorIcons/Material directly' rule and diverging from every sibling screen in the module (athlete_agenda_screen, trainer_agenda_tab, athlete_detail_screen all use TreinoIcon.*). Affected: Icons.arrow_back (43), Icons.edit_outlined (272), Icons.delete_outline (278, 352), Icons.add (779), Icons.calendar_today_outlined (642), Icons.access_time_outlined (883).
  - **Fix:** Swap to existing TreinoIcon constants: back→TreinoIcon.back, edit→TreinoIcon.edit, delete→TreinoIcon.trash, add→TreinoIcon.plus, calendar→TreinoIcon.calendar, time→TreinoIcon.clock. All already exist in lib/core/widgets/treino_icon.dart — no new icons needed.
  - **Evidencia:** Editor lines 43, 272, 278, 352, 642, 779, 883; treino_icon.dart defines back/edit/trash/plus/calendar/clock.

- **[MEDIUM · microcopy-i18n]** About a dozen user-facing Spanish strings are hardcoded even though AppL10n is wired up and already used in this same file (agendaEditorTitle, agendaAddRuleCta, etc.). Hardcoded: 'MIS HORARIOS DE TRABAJO' (85), 'Sin horarios configurados...' (90), 'EXCEPCIONES' (109), 'Sin excepciones.' (111), '¿Eliminar esta excepción?' (200), 'Editar' tooltip (274), 'Eliminar' tooltip (280/354), 'Editar horario' (428), and all form labels 'Día de la semana'/'Hora inicio'/'Hora fin'/'Duración del turno'/'Fecha a bloquear' (438-629). This blocks the EN locale (intl_en.arb has the agenda* keys) and contradicts design-system rule #3.
  - **Fix:** Move every literal to AppL10n keys (the agenda* namespace already exists). The mixed approach is the worst case — half-localized means EN users get a Spanglish screen. Also fill the empty EN values in intl_en.arb for these keys.
  - **Evidencia:** Lines 85, 90, 109, 111, 200, 274, 280, 354, 428, 438, 448, 462, 476, 629; AppL10n already used at lines 47, 102, 120, 154, 516.

- **[MEDIUM · design-system]** Destructive delete buttons are colored with `palette.highlight` (magenta #C123E0), which the design system reserves for achievements/avatar gradient/PF badge — a celebratory color. The palette defines a dedicated `danger` (#E53935) token explicitly documented 'for inline error states / destructive actions'. Using the achievement color for 'delete' sends the wrong affordance signal.
  - **Fix:** Use `palette.danger` for the delete IconButtons (lines 278, 352) and for the confirm button in _ConfirmDialog when the action is destructive. Reserve highlight for positive/brand emphasis.
  - **Evidencia:** Lines 278 and 352 (Icon delete colored palette.highlight); app_palette.dart:54 documents `danger` for destructive/error states; design-system.md lists highlight as 'Achievements, avatar gradient, badge PF'.

- **[MEDIUM · accessibility]** Icon-only IconButtons rely on `tooltip` ('Editar'/'Eliminar') which TalkBack/VoiceOver do read, but the destructive delete buttons give no per-item context — a screen-reader user hears 'Eliminar' with no idea WHICH rule/day it deletes. The day/date label and the delete control are separate nodes, so SR order announces them disconnected. The drag-handle Containers in the sheets (lines 415, 610) are decorative but not marked, adding noise.
  - **Fix:** Add Semantics labels that include the row identity, e.g. tooltip/label 'Eliminar horario del {dayLabel}' and 'Eliminar excepción del {dateStr}'. Wrap the decorative grab-handle Containers in `ExcludeSemantics`. Verify with the flutter-accessibility-audit skill.
  - **Evidencia:** Lines 271-281 and 350-355 (generic 'Editar'/'Eliminar' tooltips, no row context); drag handles at 414-424 and 609-619.

- **[LOW · consistency]** The 'Extra' override type renders an entirely hardcoded label built inline ('Extra HH:MM – HH:MM', line 314) while the 'block' type uses the localized agendaSlotBlockedLabel (line 312). The block-override creation sheet only ever creates block overrides, so 'extra' overrides can appear in the list but cannot be created/edited here — a read-only type with no affordance, which is a latent dead-end if extras are introduced elsewhere.
  - **Fix:** Localize the 'Extra' prefix via AppL10n and, if extra overrides are user-relevant, give them an edit/create path; otherwise confirm they are intentionally read-only and document it. At minimum the prefix string should not be hardcoded.
  - **Evidencia:** Lines 311-315 (block uses l10n, extra hardcoded); _BlockOverrideFormSheet (578-716) only builds AvailabilityOverride.block.

- **[LOW · design-system]** Spacing uses several values outside the documented scale (8·12·14·18·20). The screen uses SizedBox heights of 16, 24, 32 and EdgeInsets with 16/24 repeatedly (lines 100, 106, 118, 418, 435, 445, 459, 473, 501, 628, 656), and padding fromLTRB(20,8,20,24). design-system.md explicitly says 'No usar 4 / 16 / 24'.
  - **Fix:** Align vertical rhythm to the allowed scale: replace 16→18, 24→20 (or a documented multiple), 32→ a sanctioned section gap. If 16/24/32 are genuinely needed for this layout, raise it as a design-system gap rather than silently using off-scale values.
  - **Evidencia:** Lines 82, 100, 106, 118, 435, 445, 459, 473, 501, 628, 656 use 16/24/32; design-system.md spacing scale forbids 16/24.

- **[LOW · usability]** The rule form has no inline validation feedback while editing — invalid end<start windows are only caught on Save via a SnackBar (line 537), and the user must dismiss the keyboard/sheet to see it. There's also no guard preventing duplicate rules for the same day/overlapping windows, so a trainer can create conflicting availability with no warning (recognition over recall / error prevention).
  - **Fix:** Surface the window validity inline (e.g. disable the Save button or show a hint under 'Hora fin' when the window is invalid) so the error is prevented at input time rather than reported after submit. Consider warning on overlapping same-day rules.
  - **Evidencia:** Lines 531-541 (validation only at save time, SnackBar); no overlap/duplicate check in _save (530-573).

## lib/features/coach/presentation/trainer_public_profile_screen.dart (Coach module — Trainer public profile)

_The screen is structurally solid: it uses AppPalette tokens throughout (no HEX/Colors.* leaks except intentional Colors.transparent over the shell's AppBackground), uses TreinoIcon.back instead of raw Phosphor, wires its own user-facing strings through AppL10n, and correctly handles loading/error/not-found/data branches at the top level. The genuine problems are concentrated in (1) hardcoded Spanish UI strings inside the child CTAs and one state button, all marked "i18n: Fase 6 Etapa 7" as known debt; (2) missing Semantics on the icon-only back button (a systemic gap across the coach module, not unique here); (3) spacing values (24/16/6/4) that sit off the documented 8·12·14·18·20 scale; and (4) two minor state-design gaps in the embedded reviews section. Nothing is broken, but the i18n debt and a11y label gap are real and worth flagging._

- **[HIGH · microcopy-i18n]** Several user-facing strings on this screen are hardcoded Spanish literals instead of AppL10n keys. In trainer_contact_cta_stub.dart the two snackbars are hardcoded ('Solicitud enviada. Te avisamos cuando el PF responda.' line 57, 'No pudimos enviar la solicitud: $e' line 64) and the existing-link states are hardcoded ('SOLICITUD PENDIENTE', 'TU PERSONAL TRAINER', 'YA TENÉS UN PF' lines 121-124). In review_cta.dart the CTA labels and fallback name are hardcoded ('tu Personal Trainer' line 53, 'EDITAR MI RESEÑA' line 57, 'DEJAR UNA RESEÑA' line 58). In trainer_reviews_section.dart the header 'RESEÑAS' (line 30) and empty-state 'Sin reseñas todavía' (line 50) are hardcoded. The screen's own strings ARE localized, so these children break the contract inconsistently.
  - **Fix:** Move all these strings to AppL10n keys (the project already has coachStatsReviewsLabel='RESEÑAS' that the reviews header could reuse). The code itself flags them as 'i18n: Fase 6 Etapa 7' debt — clearing it removes the inconsistency where the parent screen is localized but its embedded CTAs are not.
  - **Evidencia:** trainer_contact_cta_stub.dart:57,64,121-124; review_cta.dart:53,57,58; trainer_reviews_section.dart:30,50

- **[MEDIUM · microcopy-i18n]** The _NotFoundState 'Volver' button uses a const hardcoded Spanish literal (Text('Volver'), line 124) while every other string in the same file goes through l10n (coachProfileNotFoundLabel, coachProfileErrorLabel, coachRetryLabel). This is an isolated leak in an otherwise fully-localized file.
  - **Fix:** Replace const Text('Volver') with an AppL10n key (e.g. a shared l10n.commonBack / coachBackLabel). Keeps the not-found state consistent with the error state directly below it.
  - **Evidencia:** trainer_public_profile_screen.dart:124

- **[MEDIUM · accessibility]** The icon-only back button (IconButton with TreinoIcon.back, lines 35-39) has no semantic label, so a screen reader announces it generically. IconButton's default 48x48 tap target is fine, but VoiceOver users get no spoken affordance for the only navigation control on the screen. This is a systemic gap (rg finds zero Semantics/semanticLabel usage across the entire coach module), so it is a module-wide issue surfacing here rather than a one-off.
  - **Fix:** Add a tooltip/semantic label to the back IconButton (e.g. tooltip: l10n.commonBack or wrap with Semantics(label: ...)). Given the systemic absence, consider establishing the pattern in the shared back-button affordance so the whole coach module benefits.
  - **Evidencia:** trainer_public_profile_screen.dart:35-39

- **[MEDIUM · design-system]** Spacing uses values outside the documented scale (8·12·14·18·20; 'No usar 4/16/24'). This screen and its children use 24 repeatedly (SizedBox height:24 lines 61,63,91 and ListView gaps; hero lines 29,65), 16 (line 70; hero line 65), 6 (hero line 52), and 4 (StatTile line 33). These ad-hoc values are technically off-scale per design-system.md.
  - **Fix:** Normalize to the documented scale (replace 24→20, 16→18, 6→8 where it doesn't break rhythm). If 24/16 are genuinely needed for hero breathing room, update design-system.md to legitimize them — right now code and spec disagree. Note this is widespread in the codebase, so treat as a token-hygiene cleanup rather than a blocker.
  - **Evidencia:** trainer_public_profile_screen.dart:61,63,70,91,95,97; trainer_profile_hero.dart:29,52,65; stat_tile.dart:33

- **[MEDIUM · states]** The embedded TrainerReviewsSection swallows its loading and error states: reviewsAsync.when returns SizedBox.shrink() for both loading (line 40) and error (line 41). On a slow/failed reviews fetch the section silently shows just the 'RESEÑAS' header with nothing under it — no spinner, no 'could not load' message, no retry. This violates visibility-of-system-status: the user cannot tell whether reviews are loading, empty, or failed.
  - **Fix:** Give the reviews section at least a lightweight loading affordance (small spinner or skeleton) and an error message distinct from the empty state. Reuse the empty-state text style so the header is never left dangling with an invisible body.
  - **Evidencia:** trainer_reviews_section.dart:39-41

- **[LOW · states]** The top-level error state (_ErrorState) discards the error object entirely (error: (_, __) => ...) and shows a generic message. That is acceptable for users, but combined with the reviews section also hiding errors, a partially-failed page can look 'fine' while data is missing. Also the main loading state is a bare centered CircularProgressIndicator with no context (line 42-44) — acceptable for a fast profile fetch but offers no skeleton of the hero/stats.
  - **Fix:** Low priority: consider a lightweight skeleton for the hero/stats during load for perceived performance, and ensure errors are at least logged (analytics/crash) even if not shown, so silent failures are observable.
  - **Evidencia:** trainer_public_profile_screen.dart:42-47; 133-161

- **[LOW · consistency]** The two primary CTAs on the screen are styled inconsistently. TrainerContactCtaStub (the primary 'PEDIR VÍNCULO' action) is an OutlinedButton with default radius and is NOT full-width (lines 88-97), while ReviewCta directly below it is a full-width OutlinedButton with an explicit pill radius (9999, line 87) per the design system's r-full for primary CTAs. The most important action (link request) thus looks less prominent and less pill-shaped than the secondary review CTA.
  - **Fix:** Make the primary CTA full-width with the r-full pill radius to match ReviewCta and the design system's 'CTAs principales = r-full' rule, reinforcing it as the primary action. Aligning both also fixes the visual-hierarchy inversion where the secondary CTA reads as more primary.
  - **Evidencia:** trainer_contact_cta_stub.dart:88-97 vs review_cta.dart:60-89

## lib/features/coach/presentation/trainers_list_screen.dart (Coach module — trainer discovery)

_The screen is well-architected for its happy path: it uses AppPalette tokens, TreinoIcon wrappers, and AsyncValue.when with loading/error/empty/data branches all designed. However it has notable gaps: ZERO Semantics labels anywhere (icon-only toggle pills, avatars, retry are not screen-reader friendly — and Semantics is absent across the entire coach module), every English (intl_en.arb) string for this screen is EMPTY (broken i18n for any non-es_AR locale), several user-facing strings are hardcoded instead of going through AppL10n (section headers, mode-tab labels, toggle labels, '\$rate', 'Gimnasio' fallback), tap targets on the toggle pills fall below the 44pt minimum, spacing uses values (4/6/16/24) explicitly banned by the design-system scale, and a documented test-only helper (setDeniedForTest) is invoked in production flow. The error branch also swallows the actual error and the gyms provider failure degrades silently._

- **[HIGH · accessibility]** No Semantics anywhere on the screen (and none across the whole coach module). The MAPA/LISTA toggle pills and the Presencial/Online mode tabs are icon+short-label GestureDetectors with no semantic role/state, so a screen reader cannot announce them as selectable toggles or report which is active. The trainer avatars (PostAvatar) and the active/disabled state of the map pill are also unlabeled.
  - **Fix:** Wrap the toggle pills and mode tabs in Semantics(button: true, selected: active, label: ...) (or use a real SegmentedButton/ToggleButtons). Add a Semantics label to the avatar in TrainerListTile and announce disabled state on the MAPA pill (e.g. 'Mapa, no disponible en modo Online'). Provide a meaningful label for the retry TextButton context.
  - **Evidencia:** trainers_list_screen.dart _TogglePill (GestureDetector L255-256, Icon L268), _ModeTab (GestureDetector L477), _ListMapToggle L205-219; trainer_list_tile.dart PostAvatar L61-65. grep: zero matches for 'Semantics' in lib/features/coach/presentation/.

- **[HIGH · microcopy-i18n]** Every English string for this screen is an empty string in intl_en.arb: coachErrorLabel, coachRetryLabel, coachEmptyLabel, coachDistanceUnknown, coachMonthlyRateUnit all = "". On any en locale the error/empty states render blank, the retry button has no label, and distance/rate show nothing. Only es_AR is populated.
  - **Fix:** Fill in the English values in lib/l10n/intl_en.arb (e.g. 'We couldn’t load trainers.', 'Retry', 'No trainers found in your area.', '—', '/mo'). Add a CI/test guard that fails when any locale has empty strings for keys present in the base locale.
  - **Evidencia:** lib/l10n/intl_en.arb L50-56 (coachErrorLabel/coachRetryLabel/coachEmptyLabel/coachDistanceUnknown/coachMonthlyRateUnit all ""); populated only in intl_es_AR.arb L49-55.

- **[MEDIUM · microcopy-i18n]** Many user-facing strings on this screen and its children are hardcoded in Spanish instead of going through AppL10n, contradicting design-system rule #3 (never hard-code UI strings). This breaks localization for the same locales already broken above.
  - **Fix:** Route these through AppL10n: section headers 'ESPECIALIDAD'/'FILTROS', toggle labels 'MAPA'/'LISTA', mode-tab labels 'PRESENCIAL'/'ONLINE', the 'Gimnasio' gym-cache-miss fallback, the 'ONLINE' virtual badge, the '$count reseña/reseñas' pluralization (use ICU plural), and 'Buscando ubicación...'/'Especialidad'/'Todos' in the filter rows.
  - **Evidencia:** trainers_list_screen.dart _SectionHeader text 'ESPECIALIDAD' L104 / 'FILTROS' L116, _TogglePill labels 'MAPA' L207 'LISTA' L216, _ModeTab 'PRESENCIAL' L429 'ONLINE' L445, _labelFor 'Gimnasio' L349; trainer_list_tile.dart 'ONLINE' badge L182, '$count reseña/reseñas' L151; trainer_compact_filter_row.dart 'Buscando ubicación...' L57, 'Especialidad' L86.

- **[MEDIUM · states]** Two state-handling gaps. (1) The error branch discards the real error: `error: (_, __) => _ErrorState(...)` shows a generic message and never logs/surfaces the cause, hurting visibility of system status and debuggability. (2) The gyms catalog failure is swallowed silently: gymsAsync is consumed only via valueOrNull, so if gymsProvider errors, every tile silently falls back to the 'Gimnasio' label with no indication anything failed.
  - **Fix:** Capture the error object for logging/telemetry in the error branch (even if the UI copy stays generic). For gyms, decide intentionally: either accept the 'Gimnasio' degradation explicitly with a comment, or surface a soft indicator when the catalog failed to load.
  - **Evidencia:** trainers_list_screen.dart error branch L309-311; gymsById built from gymsAsync.valueOrNull L300-303 with no error/loading handling; _labelFor 'Gimnasio' fallback L349.

- **[MEDIUM · usability]** Production code path invokes a helper explicitly documented as test-only. When the user declines the location rationale sheet, _maybeShowRationale calls notifier.setDeniedForTest(), whose doc comment says 'for test overrides' and the sibling setForTest says 'never call in production'. This conflates the real user-decline flow with a test seam and risks the denied state being treated inconsistently from a real OS denial.
  - **Fix:** Add a first-class public method on AthleteLocationNotifier for the user-declined-rationale case (e.g. declineRationale() / markDenied()) and call that instead of setDeniedForTest from the screen.
  - **Evidencia:** trainers_list_screen.dart L58 `notifier.setDeniedForTest();`; trainer_discovery_providers.dart setDeniedForTest doc 'for test overrides' L136-140 and setForTest 'never call in production' L130-134.

- **[MEDIUM · accessibility]** Toggle-pill tap targets are below the 44pt iOS minimum. Each _TogglePill is padding 10h/6v around a 14px icon + 12px text — roughly 26px tall — and the MAPA/LISTA control sits in the AppBar actions. Small targets are hard to hit, especially the segmented toggle.
  - **Fix:** Ensure each tappable pill has at least a 44x44 hit area (wrap the GestureDetector content with a SizedBox/constraints or increase vertical padding, or use a Material InkWell with minimum interactive size). Same check for the filter chips.
  - **Evidencia:** trainers_list_screen.dart _TogglePill EdgeInsets.symmetric(horizontal: 10, vertical: 6) L260 with Icon size 14 L268 and fontSize 12 L276.

- **[LOW · design-system]** Spacing uses values the design-system scale explicitly forbids. design-system.md states the only allowed spacing values are 8·12·14·18·20 and to NOT use 4/16/24. The screen uses 4, 6, 16, and 24 in multiple places, plus ad-hoc letter-spacing/font-size literals rather than typography tokens.
  - **Fix:** Normalize spacing to the allowed scale (replace SizedBox(height: 6)/(4) and the 16/24 paddings). If 16 padding is genuinely required for list gutters, document the exception or add a token; otherwise align to 14/18/20.
  - **Evidencia:** trainers_list_screen.dart SizedBox(height: 6) L105/L117, EdgeInsets ...16... L93/L317, _SectionHeader EdgeInsets.fromLTRB(20,4,20,0) L514; _EmptyState/_ErrorState EdgeInsets.all(24) L362/L381.

- **[LOW · design-system]** Direct Colors.* constants used instead of palette tokens. Colors.transparent appears for the Scaffold/AppBar backgrounds and inactive pill/tab backgrounds. While transparent has no palette equivalent and is arguably acceptable, design-system rule #1 says never use raw color constants in widgets; this is the only Colors.* leakage to flag (no HEX literals or PhosphorIcons direct usage were found — icons correctly go through TreinoIcon).
  - **Fix:** Acceptable as-is for transparency, but if the team wants strict compliance, expose a palette.transparent/none token or annotate these as intentional exceptions so lint/reviews don’t flag them inconsistently.
  - **Evidencia:** trainers_list_screen.dart Colors.transparent at Scaffold L72, AppBar L75, _TogglePill bg L250-251, _ModeTab decoration L484. (No HEX literals; TreinoIcon.mapPin/users used correctly L207/L216.)

- **[LOW · consistency]** Two visually near-identical segmented controls are implemented independently with duplicated styling: the AppBar MAPA/LISTA toggle (_ListMapToggle/_TogglePill) and the Presencial/Online tabs (_ModeTabs/_ModeTab). Both are pill-in-pill segmented controls but differ in active color (highlight vs accent), padding, and animation (one animates, one doesn’t), and neither reuses the not-yet-built TreinoChip/segmented base component the design-system anticipates.
  - **Fix:** Extract a single shared segmented-control widget (with built-in states normal/active/disabled and Semantics) and reuse it for both controls — this also resolves the accessibility and tap-target findings in one place, and matches the design-system guidance to build reusable base components used in 2+ places.
  - **Evidencia:** trainers_list_screen.dart _ListMapToggle/_TogglePill L178-285 (active=palette.highlight, no AnimatedContainer) vs _ModeTabs/_ModeTab L411-502 (active=palette.accent, AnimatedContainer 160ms).

## lib/features/coach_hub/presentation/coach_hub_dashboard_screen.dart (module: coach_hub) — Coach Hub web landing dashboard

_The screen is solid on the two hardest design-system rules — every color goes through AppPalette.of(context) and every icon through TreinoIcon, with zero HEX/Colors.* literals or direct PhosphorIcons. Structure, real-time stream wiring, and confirm dialogs for destructive link actions are well thought out. The real problems are: (1) 100% of user-facing strings are hardcoded Spanish while the rest of the app uses AppL10n (512 keys) — the entire coach_hub module is the i18n outlier; (2) inconsistent AsyncValue handling — one section renders loading+error, the other three silently swallow both via maybeWhen/orElse, so a Firestore failure shows a fake-empty dashboard; (3) accessibility is essentially absent — no Semantics, icon-only spinners with no label, sub-44pt tap targets; (4) destructive sign-out has no confirmation and sits beside the welcome title. None of these are invented nitpicks; they are concrete, fixable gaps measured against the project's own conventions._

- **[HIGH · microcopy-i18n]** Every user-facing string on the screen is a hardcoded Spanish literal: section headers ('TUS ALUMNOS', 'EN PAUSA', 'VÍNCULOS PASADOS'), CTA labels ('IMPORTAR PLAN DESDE EXCEL', 'Salir', 'Pausar', 'Reanudar', 'Terminar vínculo', 'Aceptar', 'Rechazar'), empty/error messages, dialog titles/bodies, snackbars, and the _reasonDisplay() map. The entire coach_hub module has ZERO AppL10n references (grep confirms), while coach/, workout/, reviews/ use it everywhere and the project ships 512 es keys. design-system.md rule 3 explicitly bans hard-coded UI strings.
  - **Fix:** Migrate all strings to AppL10n following the existing naming convention (e.g. coachHubDashboardTitle, coachHubImportPlanCta, coachHubActiveSectionLabel, coachHubPauseConfirmBody, coachHubLinkAcceptedSnack). At minimum, extract them into a coach_hub_strings.dart constants file mirroring features/coach/presentation/coach_strings.dart so the module stops being the i18n outlier and the strings become translatable/testable.
  - **Evidencia:** Lines 70-72 ('Cancelar'/'Confirmar'), 126 ('TREINO COACH HUB'), 136, 161 ('Salir'), 173 ('IMPORTAR PLAN DESDE EXCEL'), 247-249 (chips), 309/349/391 (section labels), 314/353/396 (empty states), 462/480 (dialog bodies), 471/491/582/603/812/831 (snackbars), 877 ('Quiere vincularse con vos'), 904/916 (Rechazar/Aceptar). _reasonDisplay lines 34-45.

- **[HIGH · states]** AsyncValue handling is inconsistent across the four sections that all watch the same trainerLinksStreamProvider. _ActiveStudentsList (line 299) uses full .when with loading + error branches. But _PausedStudentsList (342), _HistorialList (383) and _PendingRequestsList (749) use maybeWhen with orElse: SizedBox.shrink(), which silently swallows BOTH the loading and the error state. On a Firestore stream failure the active section shows 'No pudimos cargar tus alumnos' while paused/historial/pending vanish entirely — the trainer sees a half-broken dashboard that looks empty, with no signal that pending requests failed to load. This is a visibility-of-system-status (Nielsen) violation and a real data-integrity risk for the accept/decline queue.
  - **Fix:** Use a single source of truth for the load/error state. Either lift the .when() to the parent and pass resolved links down to the four sections, or give every section the same loading + error branches (reusing _SectionLoading / _SectionError). The pending-requests queue in particular must surface an error rather than disappearing.
  - **Evidencia:** Line 299 linksAsync.when(loading/error/data) vs lines 342, 383, 749 linksAsync.maybeWhen(data:..., orElse: () => const SizedBox.shrink()).

- **[HIGH · accessibility]** No Semantics anywhere on the screen (grep confirms zero). Concrete failures: (a) the busy spinner in _PendingRequestTile (lines 887-895) replaces the Aceptar/Rechazar buttons with a bare CircularProgressIndicator that has no semantic label — a screen-reader user hears nothing and loses the action; (b) the avatar (PostAvatar) and its initial-fallback carry no label, so VoiceOver reads only the adjacent name text with no 'foto de perfil' context; (c) the _SectionLoading spinner (line 421) and the inline pending spinner give no 'Cargando' announcement.
  - **Fix:** Wrap action spinners in Semantics(label: 'Procesando…', child: ...) or add a liveRegion announcement; add a Semantics label to the avatar (e.g. 'Foto de $name') or mark it decorative with excludeSemantics if the name is already read; give the loading indicators a semantic label so state changes are announced.
  - **Evidencia:** Lines 887-895 (icon-only spinner, no Semantics), PostAvatar usages at 506/620/696/854, _SectionLoading line 421.

- **[MEDIUM · accessibility]** Tap targets fall below the 44pt iOS minimum. The 'Pausar'/'Terminar vínculo' and 'Reanudar'/'Terminar vínculo' TextButtons sit in a row with default TextButton sizing and no minimumSize, so on a card row the touch height is driven by text (~36pt) rather than 48. The 'Salir' TextButton.icon (148) and the decline TextButton (897) have the same issue. The primary CTA correctly uses minimumSize Size.fromHeight(48), proving the pattern is known — it just isn't applied to the row buttons.
  - **Fix:** Set TextButton.styleFrom(minimumSize: Size(0, 44)) (or wrap in a 44pt-min constrained box) on the per-row action buttons so every interactive control meets the 44pt minimum. Also note two side-by-side text actions in a narrow card row are easy to mis-tap — consider an overflow menu or more horizontal separation.
  - **Evidencia:** TextButtons at lines 539-548 (Pausar/Terminar), 655-664 (Reanudar/Terminar), 148-163 (Salir), 897-905 (Rechazar) — none set minimumSize; compare CTA line 181 minimumSize Size.fromHeight(48).

- **[MEDIUM · usability]** Sign-out is destructive (ends the session, requires re-auth) yet has no confirmation and is placed in the header right next to the welcome title (Spacer pushes it to the top-right). The screen already has a clean _confirmAction() AlertDialog helper used for pause/resume/terminate, so the guard pattern exists and just isn't applied to the highest-consequence action. This is a user-control-&-freedom / error-prevention gap (Nielsen).
  - **Fix:** Route sign-out through _confirmAction (e.g. title 'Cerrar sesión', body '¿Seguro que querés salir?', confirmLabel 'Salir'), and/or move it away from the title cluster to reduce accidental taps.
  - **Evidencia:** Lines 148-163: TextButton.icon onPressed signs out immediately; _confirmAction helper at lines 53-77 is used for far less consequential pause/terminate flows.

- **[MEDIUM · navigation]** The CTA uses context.go('/upload-plan') (line 168) which REPLACES the navigation stack rather than pushing. Because the coach_hub router has no ShellRoute and the upload screen returns to the dashboard via context.go('/dashboard') (confirmed in coach_hub_upload_plan_screen.dart line 193), back navigation works only because both screens hardcode go() round-trips. There is no browser/system back stack and no breadcrumb on the dashboard itself. On web this means the browser Back button behavior is unpredictable for the import flow. Not a dead-end, but fragile.
  - **Fix:** Use context.push('/upload-plan') for the import flow so the back stack is real and the browser Back button / system back returns to the dashboard naturally, instead of relying on paired go() calls.
  - **Evidencia:** Dashboard line 168 context.go('/upload-plan'); upload screen line 193 context.go('/dashboard'); router (coach_hub_router.dart) has no ShellRoute and flat GoRoutes.

- **[LOW · consistency]** Card corner radius is 14 (lines 501, 615, 689, 849) and chips use the FilterChip default, but design-system.md defines radii as r-sm 12 / r-md 16 / r-lg 20 — 14 is off-scale. Card border uses the standard palette.border, but the pending-request card uses palette.highlight.withValues(alpha: 0.4) (line 850) as a one-off border treatment that isn't a documented token. Minor, but it drifts from the documented radii scale and card border convention.
  - **Fix:** Snap card radius to 16 (r-md) per the documented scale, or document 14 if it's intentional. Keep the highlighted pending-card border but consider promoting it to a named treatment so it reads as a deliberate token rather than an ad-hoc value.
  - **Evidencia:** BorderRadius.circular(14) at lines 501, 615, 689, 849; design-system.md Radii table (12/16/20). Pending card border line 850.

- **[LOW · visual-hierarchy]** Heading copy is intentionally split between filter chips (ACTIVOS/PAUSADOS/HISTORIAL) and section labels (TUS ALUMNOS/EN PAUSA/VÍNCULOS PASADOS) — the code comment (lines 256-261) explains this is for clear section boundaries and test disambiguation, which is reasonable. However all section labels render at the same 12px textMuted weight (_SectionLabel) while 'SOLICITUDES PENDIENTES' renders at 12px highlight color — so the pending header reads as higher priority, which is correct, but the three list headers are visually indistinguishable from each other and from the disabled/muted captions, flattening the hierarchy when multiple sections are visible at once.
  - **Fix:** Give the active list headers slightly more prominence than muted captions (e.g. textPrimary or a hair larger) so the three sections are scannable as distinct groups when stacked, while keeping pending as the top-priority highlight.
  - **Evidencia:** _SectionLabel lines 263-283 (all textMuted 12px) vs _PendingRequestsList header lines 758-766 (highlight 12px).

## lib/features/coach_hub/presentation/coach_hub_login_screen.dart (module: coach_hub)

_The Coach Hub login screen is structurally clean and disciplined on the design-system color front: it sources every color via AppPalette.of(context) with zero HEX literals or Colors.* constants, uses StadiumBorder pills per the radii spec, and reuses a shared _inputDecoration helper. Its error handling is genuinely well-thought (AsyncValue.guard in the notifier, humanized AuthFailure messages, button disabled while submitting, spinner in-button). The real gaps are accessibility-adjacent and consistency-with-siblings issues: no password-manager autofillHints, no password-visibility toggle, hardcoded Spanish strings despite an established AppL10n convention and an en locale, one off-scale spacing value, missing Semantics on the in-button spinner, and a couple of usability omissions (no submit on the email field, no account-recovery affordance) that the mobile auth screens already solve. None are blockers, but several diverge from patterns the same team already shipped in lib/features/auth/._

- **[HIGH · accessibility]** Neither the email nor password TextFormField declares autofillHints. On iOS/web this disables Keychain/password-manager integration: the OS cannot offer to fill or save the credential, and Safari/iOS won't surface the strong-password / saved-login UI. For a login screen whose whole purpose is credential entry, this is a real friction and accessibility regression — users relying on a password manager (a common assistive workflow) get no support.
  - **Fix:** Add `autofillHints: const [AutofillHints.username, AutofillHints.email]` to the email field and `autofillHints: const [AutofillHints.password]` to the password field, and wrap the Form (or the two fields) in an AutofillGroup so iOS recognizes the credential pair. The mobile auth screens already do this via the shared AuthInput widget (lib/features/auth/presentation/widgets/auth_input.dart:39, :99) — reuse that pattern.
  - **Evidencia:** coach_hub_login_screen.dart:130-160 (both TextFormFields have no autofillHints); contrast lib/features/auth/presentation/widgets/auth_input.dart:99 which wires autofillHints through.

- **[MEDIUM · usability]** The password field is obscured with no way to reveal it. There is no visibility toggle, which on a web/desktop login (where typos are easy and there's no autofill safety net here) hurts error prevention and forces blind re-entry on every failed attempt. The mobile auth flow already provides a show/hide toggle in AuthInput.
  - **Fix:** Add a suffixIcon visibility toggle to the password field's InputDecoration, toggling obscureText via local state. Use TreinoIcon for the eye / eye-off icons (the not_allowed sibling already imports TreinoIcon) rather than a raw Material icon, and give the IconButton a Semantics label like 'Mostrar contraseña' / 'Ocultar contraseña'. Mirror lib/features/auth/presentation/widgets/auth_input.dart (it manages an _obscured toggle).
  - **Evidencia:** coach_hub_login_screen.dart:148-160 (obscureText: true, no suffixIcon); auth_input.dart:54 (_obscured = widget.obscureText) shows the established toggle pattern.

- **[MEDIUM · microcopy-i18n]** Every user-facing string is hardcoded Spanish (TREINO/COACH HUB headings, the subtitle, both field labels, all four validator messages, the INGRESAR CTA, the footer, and the generic error fallback). This violates design-system rule #3 ('Nunca hard-code de strings de UI') and breaks the AppL10n convention used across ~20 files elsewhere in the app. The app declares an `en` locale and resolves via AppL10n.supportedLocales (lib/app/app.dart), so an English-locale PF lands on a fully Spanish login. The entire coach_hub module shares this gap (zero AppL10n references in the module), so this is a module-level decision, not just this file — but the login is the first screen an unauthenticated user sees, so it's the highest-impact instance.
  - **Fix:** Route the strings through AppL10n (the same way lib/features/coach/ does) — at minimum the validator messages, error fallback, CTA and subtitle. If Coach Hub is intentionally Spanish-only for MVP, document that decision explicitly in docs/design-decisions.md so it reads as a scope choice rather than an oversight, since it contradicts a 'no negociable' code rule.
  - **Evidencia:** coach_hub_login_screen.dart:98,108,122,136,139,142,152,156,188,198,74 (all literal Spanish); rg shows 0 AppL10n usages in lib/features/coach_hub/ vs widespread use in lib/features/coach/; lib/app/app.dart resolves Locale('es','AR') against AppL10n.supportedLocales which includes en.

- **[MEDIUM · accessibility]** The in-button loading state replaces the 'INGRESAR' label with a bare CircularProgressIndicator. To a screen reader the button loses its accessible name during submit — it announces nothing meaningful — and there is no semantic 'loading'/'ingresando' status announced, so a SR user gets no feedback that the system is working (Nielsen: visibility of system status for assistive tech).
  - **Fix:** Wrap the spinner branch in a Semantics(label: 'Ingresando…', child: ...) or keep a hidden text label, so the button retains an accessible name and the status change is announced. Optionally add an ExcludeSemantics around the purely-decorative spinner and expose the status on the button itself.
  - **Evidencia:** coach_hub_login_screen.dart:178-186 (spinner with no label replaces the text child).

- **[MEDIUM · usability]** The email field has no onFieldSubmitted handler and no textInputAction, while the password field submits on enter (line 153). On desktop/web — the actual Coach Hub target platform — pressing Enter or Tab→Enter from the email field does nothing useful, breaking the expected keyboard-only login flow. Recognition-over-recall and user-control suffer for keyboard users.
  - **Fix:** Set `textInputAction: TextInputAction.next` on the email field (focus moves to password) and `TextInputAction.done` on the password field. This is standard for a two-field login and matches keyboard expectations on web.
  - **Evidencia:** coach_hub_login_screen.dart:130-146 (email field: no onFieldSubmitted, no textInputAction) vs :153 (password has onFieldSubmitted).

- **[MEDIUM · usability]** No account-recovery affordance. A PF who forgets their password has a dead end: the only secondary text tells them to create an account from the mobile app (line 198), and there's no 'forgot password' link. The mobile login already exposes /forgot-password (lib/features/auth/presentation/login_screen.dart:169), so trainers locked out on web have a worse experience than on mobile.
  - **Fix:** Add a '¿Olvidaste tu contraseña?' text button that triggers a Firebase password-reset email (or routes to a reset screen). Even if web reuses the same Firebase Auth backend, surfacing the option here closes the dead-end. Keep the copy in voseo to match the rest of the screen ('¿Olvidaste…').
  - **Evidencia:** coach_hub_login_screen.dart:196-204 (only a 'create from mobile' footer, no recovery); lib/features/auth/presentation/login_screen.dart:169 shows the existing /forgot-password route.

- **[LOW · design-system]** SizedBox(height: 4) between the 'TREINO' eyebrow and 'COACH HUB' heading uses 4px, which is explicitly excluded by the spacing scale in docs/design-system.md ('Sólo estos valores: 8 · 12 · 14 · 18 · 20. No usar 4 / 16 / 24'). The not_allowed sibling repeats the same 4px gap, so it's a shared deviation, but it's still off-token.
  - **Fix:** Replace the 4px gap with the nearest allowed value (8px), or if the tight optical pairing is intentional for the eyebrow/heading lockup, capture that as a documented exception in the design system rather than an ad-hoc literal.
  - **Evidencia:** coach_hub_login_screen.dart:106 (SizedBox(height: 4)); docs/design-system.md:49 spacing scale forbids 4.

- **[LOW · accessibility]** Dynamic-type robustness is untested for this layout. Font sizes are fixed literals (14/32/14/13/14/12) inside a Column with crossAxisAlignment.stretch and a fixed 400px max-width. The screen is in a SingleChildScrollView (good — vertical growth won't clip), but the StadiumBorder CTA has a fixed 48px height (Size.fromHeight(48)); at large iOS text sizes the 14px CTA label can grow and crowd or clip within a fixed-height pill, and the two-line footer/subtitle could wrap awkwardly.
  - **Fix:** Verify at the largest iOS Dynamic Type setting. Prefer minimumSize/min-height over a hard 48px so the CTA can grow vertically, and confirm the spinner/label swap doesn't change button height. Since this is the lowest-risk item, a quick manual check at 200% text scale is enough to confirm or dismiss.
  - **Evidencia:** coach_hub_login_screen.dart:175 (minimumSize: Size.fromHeight(48) fixed height) and the fixed fontSize literals at 101,111,126,166,191,202.

## lib/features/coach_hub/presentation/coach_hub_not_allowed_screen.dart (module: coach_hub)

_Small, well-structured web-only "athlete tried to enter the Coach Hub" info screen. Correctly uses AppPalette.of(context) for every color (zero HEX/Colors.* literals) and TreinoIcon.X for both icons (lock, signOut) — design-system color/icon rules are fully respected. The most actionable gap is the sign-out action: it is a fire-and-forget async with no loading indicator and no error handling, so a slow or failed FirebaseAuth.signOut() leaves the user with no system-status feedback (the sibling login screen handles exactly this case correctly). Secondary issues are module-wide rather than screen-specific: hardcoded Spanish strings instead of AppL10n (a real l10n system with es/es_AR/en ARB files exists, but NO coach_hub screen uses it), ad-hoc spacing values (18/14/4) outside the documented 8·12·14·18·20 scale, and a missing Semantics label on the decorative lock icon. None of these are severe, and several are consistent with the rest of the coach_hub module._

- **[HIGH · states]** The 'Cerrar sesión' button calls `await FirebaseAuth.instance.signOut()` in a fire-and-forget onPressed with no loading state, no disabled state during the await, and no error handling. If sign-out is slow (network) the user gets zero feedback and may tap repeatedly; if it throws, the failure is swallowed and nothing happens. The redirect to /login only fires on success via the router refreshListenable. The sibling CoachHubLoginScreen (coach_hub_login_screen.dart:38-63) demonstrates the correct pattern for this same module: a `_submitting` flag, disabling the button, a spinner inside it, and a humanized error message.
  - **Fix:** Convert to a ConsumerStatefulWidget (or use a local AsyncValue) to track in-flight state: disable the button while signing out, show a CircularProgressIndicator inside it (mirror login's 18x18 spinner), and on caught error show an inline message (style with palette.danger like login does) instead of silently failing.
  - **Evidencia:** onPressed async at lines 68-71; button lacks any submitting/disabled logic vs. login screen's `_submitting` handling at coach_hub_login_screen.dart:38-63 and spinner at 178-186

- **[MEDIUM · microcopy-i18n]** All four user-facing strings are hardcoded ('COACH HUB', 'SOLO PARA PFs', the body paragraph, 'Cerrar sesión'), violating design-system rule #3 (no hard-coded UI strings). The project has a real localization system (lib/l10n/app_l10n.dart with intl_es.arb, intl_es_AR.arb, intl_en.arb) consumed elsewhere via AppL10n.of(context). Note: this is a MODULE-WIDE pattern — no coach_hub presentation screen uses AppL10n — so it is consistent with its siblings, but still a debt. The long body paragraph also carries truncation/reflow risk once translated to longer locales (e.g. en), though SingleChildScrollView mitigates clipping.
  - **Fix:** Either accept the module convention explicitly (Coach Hub web is es-only MVP) and document it, or route these strings through AppL10n alongside the rest of the module so the web hub and mobile app share one i18n contract. The voseo copy itself ('querés', 'descargá') is correct Rioplatense.
  - **Evidencia:** Hardcoded strings at lines 37, 47, 58, 78; AppL10n exists at lib/l10n/app_l10n.dart and is used e.g. in lib/features/auth/presentation/welcome_screen.dart:23; zero AppL10n usage across lib/features/coach_hub/

- **[MEDIUM · accessibility]** The 64px lock icon (line 30-34) is the visual anchor of the screen and conveys the 'locked / not allowed' meaning, but it has no Semantics label, so a screen reader skips it and the locked state is communicated only by the surrounding text. The sign-out button is fine (it has a visible text label, so the icon there is correctly decorative). Tap target is fine: the OutlinedButton sets minimumSize Size.fromHeight(44), meeting the 44pt minimum.
  - **Fix:** Wrap the lock Icon in a Semantics(label: ...) describing the locked state (e.g. 'Acceso restringido'), or confirm via the surrounding heading that the meaning is fully redundant and mark it Semantics(excludeSemantics) intentionally. Prefer an explicit label since the icon is the hero element.
  - **Evidencia:** Icon(TreinoIcon.lock, size: 64) at lines 30-34 with no Semantics wrapper; button tap target OK via minimumSize at line 83

- **[LOW · design-system]** Spacing uses values outside the documented scale. design-system.md restricts spacing to 8·12·14·18·20 and explicitly says NOT to use 16/24. This screen uses EdgeInsets.all(24) (line 24), SizedBox(height: 24) (line 66), and SizedBox(height: 4) (lines 45) — 24 is explicitly banned and 4 is off-scale. 18 and 14 are on-scale. The sibling login/dashboard screens commit the same drift (login uses 20/18 padding, dashboard uses 24), so it is a module-wide rhythm issue, not unique to this screen.
  - **Fix:** Snap to the documented scale: outer padding 20, the 24 gap before the button to 20, and the 4 micro-gaps to 8 (or accept 4 as an intentional kerning gap and add it to the scale). Aligning these would also tighten cross-screen consistency within the module.
  - **Evidencia:** EdgeInsets.all(24) line 24; SizedBox(height: 24) line 66; SizedBox(height: 4) line 45; scale defined in docs/design-system.md line 49

- **[LOW · design-system]** Typography is built with raw GoogleFonts.barlowCondensed / GoogleFonts.barlow calls plus inline fontSize/fontWeight/letterSpacing rather than a shared TextStyle/theme token. The values do follow the design-system intent (Barlow Condensed 700 uppercase for headings, Barlow for body), but every screen re-declares them, so a future type-scale change means editing every file. This is again a whole-codebase pattern (login and dashboard do the same), not a regression introduced here.
  - **Fix:** Extract the recurring heading/eyebrow/body styles into theme TextStyles or a small typography helper and reuse, so the type scale lives in one place. Low priority given it matches existing convention.
  - **Evidencia:** GoogleFonts.barlowCondensed with inline fontSize 14/28 at lines 38-43 and 48-54; GoogleFonts.barlow body at lines 60-64; identical inline pattern in coach_hub_login_screen.dart:99-127

- **[LOW · navigation]** As a terminal redirect target the screen is intentionally a dead-end for athletes (correct — there is nothing for them in the hub), and it provides one clear way out (sign out → router redirects to /login). That is good user control. The single gap: the primary action reads as 'Cerrar sesión', but the screen's docstring also mentions 'cerrar la pestaña' as an alternative; there is no on-screen affordance or hint for users who simply want to leave without signing out (e.g. they share the machine). Minor — closing the browser tab is an OS-level affordance.
  - **Fix:** Optional: add a one-line muted hint under the button clarifying that the real next step for athletes is the mobile app (the body already says this) and that sign-out returns to the login screen, reinforcing what the button does before they tap it. Not required.
  - **Evidencia:** Single OutlinedButton.icon action at lines 67-86; docstring at lines 12-13 references closing the tab as an alternative with no UI affordance

## lib/features/coach_hub/presentation/coach_hub_plan_preview_screen.dart (Coach Hub WEB — Importar Plan / Preview)

_Solid, design-system-compliant screen for the web-only Coach Hub PF tool: 100% colors via AppPalette, 100% icons via TreinoIcon, no HEX/Colors.* literals, and the _AthletePicker correctly designs loading/error/empty/data states. The real gaps are accessibility (zero Semantics anywhere in the module, sub-44pt manual-assign control, untoggled selection semantics on athlete rows), a couple of silent-fallback state issues (per-athlete name swallows loading/error into a generic "Atleta"), and an overflow-prone multi-athlete CTA. Hardcoded Spanish strings are flagged but are a deliberate module-wide convention (coach_hub uses zero AppL10n; it is a Spanish-only web surface), so they are low severity here, not a screen regression. Voseo Spanish is correct throughout._

- **[HIGH · accessibility]** The 'Asignar manualmente' control for each unmatched exercise uses TextButton.icon with tapTargetSize: MaterialTapTargetSize.shrinkWrap, minimumSize: Size(0,0) and vertical padding of only 4px. Effective height is roughly 24pt, well below the 44pt minimum touch/click target. This is the primary remediation action for the blocking 'sin match' state, so it is the most important affordance on the screen to hit reliably.
  - **Fix:** Remove shrinkWrap and the Size(0,0) override; give it minimumSize: Size(0, 44) (or wrap in a 44pt SizedBox). Keep the compact look with horizontal padding but guarantee the vertical hit area is >=44pt.
  - **Evidencia:** _DayCard, TextButton.icon at lines 597-617 (minimumSize: const Size(0, 0), tapTargetSize: MaterialTapTargetSize.shrinkWrap, padding vertical: 4)

- **[HIGH · accessibility]** There are zero Semantics widgets in the entire coach_hub module, and this screen has several controls that need them. The athlete multi-select rows (_AthleteOption) are a custom InkWell + Icon toggle with no semantic 'selected'/'toggle' state, so a screen reader announces only the name with no indication it is a selectable, currently-(un)selected item. The 'sin match' badge and the warning icon also carry meaning with no label.
  - **Fix:** Wrap each athlete row in Semantics(button: true, selected: selected, label: name) (or use a CheckboxListTile-style toggle). Add semanticLabel to the warning icon (e.g. 'Atención') and consider exposing the badge text as part of the row's semantics so the unmatched state is announced.
  - **Evidencia:** _AthleteOption InkWell + Icon(checkCircleFill/checkCircleEmpty) lines 906-944 (no Semantics, no selected state); _UnmatchedBadge lines 791-814; _UnmatchedWarning Icon(TreinoIcon.warning) line 494

- **[MEDIUM · states]** _AthleteOption resolves each athlete's display name with pubAsync.valueOrNull?.displayName ?? 'Atleta'. The loading and error branches of that AsyncValue are silently collapsed into the literal 'Atleta', so a PF selecting athletes can see multiple identical 'Atleta' rows (recognition-over-recall failure) and never learns a name failed to load. The parent _AthletePicker handles its own loading/error/empty correctly, but the per-athlete fetch does not.
  - **Fix:** Differentiate the states: show a subtle skeleton/placeholder while loading and a distinguishable fallback (e.g. show the athleteId tail or 'Atleta sin nombre') on error, rather than a generic 'Atleta' that masks both loading and failure and can collide across rows.
  - **Evidencia:** _AthleteOption line 903-904: final pubAsync = ref.watch(userPublicProfileProvider(link.athleteId)); final name = pubAsync.valueOrNull?.displayName ?? 'Atleta';

- **[MEDIUM · microcopy-i18n]** The primary CTA label 'ASIGNAR PLAN A {n} ATLETAS' is rendered with no maxLines/overflow handling inside a fixed-height (48pt) StadiumBorder button. With larger dynamic type or a higher athlete count, Barlow Condensed letter-spacing 1.4 can push this label to wrap/clip. Other labels in the file correctly set maxLines (header line 389, sheet title line 715) but this one does not.
  - **Fix:** Add maxLines: 1 with TextOverflow.ellipsis (or FittedBox) to the CTA, or shorten the label (e.g. 'ASIGNAR A {n} ATLETAS'). Test at the largest accessibility text scale.
  - **Evidencia:** ElevatedButton child Text lines 330-339: 'ASIGNAR PLAN A ${_selectedAthleteIds.length} ATLETAS' with no maxLines/overflow; button minimumSize Size.fromHeight(48)

- **[MEDIUM · usability]** User control & freedom (Nielsen): the back button in _Header and the plan-null guard both context.go('/upload-plan'), discarding the in-memory parsedPlanProvider. If the PF has already done manual exercise matches via _pickExerciseFor (which also fired addAlias side effects), backing out silently loses that work with no confirmation. There is no 'unsaved changes' guard.
  - **Fix:** If any manual matches have been applied, show a confirm dialog before navigating back (or persist the resolved plan so re-entering /preview restores it). At minimum, document that back is destructive and consider keeping the resolved state in the provider across the back navigation.
  - **Evidencia:** _Header IconButton onPressed: () => context.go('/upload-plan') line 361; plan-null path also context.go('/upload-plan') line 247; manual matches mutate parsedPlanProvider in _pickExerciseFor lines 171-174

- **[LOW · consistency]** Spacing/radii drift from the documented scale. design-system.md restricts spacing to 8/12/14/18/20 and radii to 12/16/20/full, yet this screen uses several off-scale values: vertical: 6 (lines 294, 561, 596), vertical: 2 (line 798), horizontal: 4 (line 764), and badge/divider radii of 8 and 2 (lines 705, 801). These are small but accumulate against the strict 'only these values' rule.
  - **Fix:** Snap to the token scale: use 8 instead of 6, 8 instead of 4, radius 12 instead of 8 for the badge. If sub-8 micro-spacing is genuinely needed, add an explicit exception token to the design system so it is intentional rather than ad-hoc.
  - **Evidencia:** SizedBox(height: 6) line 294; Padding vertical: 6 line 561; _UnmatchedBadge vertical: 2 / radius 8 lines 798-801; grabber radius 2 line 705; ListTile contentPadding horizontal: 4 line 764

- **[LOW · microcopy-i18n]** All user-facing strings on this screen are hardcoded Spanish ('Volver', 'PREVIEW', 'Asignar plan', error messages, etc.) rather than going through AppL10n. AppL10n is the established app-wide pattern (50 files use it), BUT the entire coach_hub module deliberately opts out (zero coach_hub files reference AppL10n) — it is a Spanish-only web PF tool. So this matches its sibling coach_hub_upload_plan_screen.dart and is a module convention, not a screen-level regression. Flagging for awareness, not as a defect to fix in isolation.
  - **Fix:** Leave as-is to stay consistent with the module unless/until coach_hub is intentionally localized. If localization ever comes to the hub, migrate the whole module together rather than this one screen. Voseo ('Elegí', 'Asignalos', 'Ajustá', 'Esperá') is correct and should be preserved.
  - **Evidencia:** Hardcoded strings throughout (e.g. lines 62-67, 103, 363/371 PREVIEW header, 605 'Asignar manualmente', 851-852 empty-athletes copy); rg confirms no AppL10n in lib/features/coach_hub/

- **[LOW · states]** Two full-screen guard states (plan == null and profile == null) render a bare centered CircularProgressIndicator with no label or context. The plan-null case is actually a redirect-in-progress (post-frame go to /upload-plan), so the spinner is momentary, but a screen reader and a slow connection both get an unlabeled spinner with no 'Cargando…' context (visibility of system status).
  - **Fix:** Add a brief label under the spinner (e.g. 'Cargando…') and a Semantics liveRegion/label so the loading state is announced. For the redirect case, an even faster transition or a one-line 'Redirigiendo…' avoids a confusing flash.
  - **Evidencia:** Lines 245-260: two Scaffold bodies with Center(child: CircularProgressIndicator(color: palette.accent)) and nothing else

## lib/features/coach_hub/presentation/coach_hub_upload_plan_screen.dart (module: coach_hub)

_A clean, well-structured upload screen. It follows the design system faithfully on the load-bearing rules — colors are all sourced via AppPalette.of(context) with zero HEX/Colors.* literals, icons go through TreinoIcon.X, and the spacing values used (8/12/14/18/20) are all on the documented scale. The primary-CTA pattern (accent stadium button, 48pt height, Barlow Condensed) matches the sibling preview and dashboard screens, and navigation is correct and predictable (back -> /dashboard, process -> /upload-plan/preview, both real routes). Loading and error states for both async actions (template download, file processing) are designed; the picked-file state has a sensible filled-card design. The findings below are real but mostly medium/low: the largest is that all user-facing copy is hardcoded Spanish while the app ships an AppL10n layer with es+en locales (a module-wide pattern that violates design-system rule #3), followed by missing Semantics labels on the icon-only back button image and a sub-44pt tap target on the inline 'Cambiar' button. No invented problems — the screen is genuinely solid._

- **[MEDIUM · microcopy-i18n]** Every user-facing string on the screen is a hardcoded Spanish literal: 'IMPORTAR PLAN', 'TREINO COACH HUB', '¿No tenés el template?', 'Descargar template', 'Subí tu plan', 'Archivo .xlsx, hasta 10 MB.', 'Elegir archivo', 'Cambiar', 'PROCESAR PLAN', plus all error messages ('No pudimos generar el template.', 'No pudimos leer el archivo. Volvé a elegirlo.', 'No pudimos procesar el archivo. Probá de nuevo.'). The app ships an AppL10n layer (lib/l10n/app_l10n.dart with es + en, used in 25+ feature files) and supportedLocales includes English (app.dart:131). design-system.md rule #3 explicitly forbids hardcoded UI strings. This is a module-wide pattern (no coach_hub file uses AppL10n), so the screen is consistent with its module but the module diverges from the rest of the app and the documented rule.
  - **Fix:** Route all literals through AppL10n. If the Coach Hub is intentionally Spanish-only for now, document that exemption in AGENTS.md / design-system.md so it is a deliberate decision rather than drift, and keep error copy centralized so it can be localized later.
  - **Evidencia:** Lines 166 (PROCESAR PLAN), 203/213 (header), 259/268 (template card), 324/333/341/387 (upload card), 63/75/100 (error strings); AppL10n usage confirmed absent across all coach_hub files.

- **[MEDIUM · accessibility]** The back affordance is an icon-only IconButton with a tooltip 'Volver' (line 192-196). The tooltip provides a hover/long-press label but is not a reliable screen-reader semantic label on all platforms; the Icon itself carries no semanticLabel. A VoiceOver/TalkBack user may hear an unlabeled or generic button. No other Semantics widgets exist anywhere on the screen.
  - **Fix:** Add an explicit semantic label to the back button (e.g. wrap the Icon with Semantics(label: 'Volver', button: true) or rely on IconButton's semanticLabel-equivalent). Audit the file-card icon (TreinoIcon.fileXls, line 359) and download/upload icons — decorative ones should be excluded from semantics, the actionable back button must be labeled.
  - **Evidencia:** Lines 192-196 (IconButton with tooltip only, no semantic label); zero Semantics/semanticLabel usage in the file.

- **[MEDIUM · accessibility]** The inline 'Cambiar' TextButton (lines 385-388) that lets the PF re-pick a file has no minimumSize, so it falls back to the default Material text-button height (~36pt) which is below the 44pt iOS tap-target minimum. This is the only way to change a wrongly-picked file from the filled-file state, so it is a real interactive control, not decorative.
  - **Fix:** Give it an explicit minimum tap target (e.g. style: TextButton.styleFrom(minimumSize: const Size(48, 44)) or wrap to ensure >=44pt), matching the 48pt height used on the other CTAs.
  - **Evidencia:** Lines 385-388: TextButton(onPressed: onPick, child: Text('Cambiar')) with no style/minimumSize.

- **[LOW · states]** The 'Descargar template' OutlinedButton spinner (lines 284-289) renders a CircularProgressIndicator with no explicit color, so it inherits the default theme indicator color rather than palette.accent. The sibling spinners on this screen (PROCESAR PLAN, line 160-163) correctly set color: palette.bg. On the dark bgCard the default indicator color may be low-contrast or off-brand, and it is inconsistent with the screen's other spinner.
  - **Fix:** Set color: palette.accent on the template-download spinner to match brand and guarantee contrast on the dark surface.
  - **Evidencia:** Lines 285-289 (no color) vs lines 160-163 (color: palette.bg).

- **[LOW · usability]** Two stated constraints are not enforced or surfaced as guidance before the user acts. The copy says 'Archivo .xlsx, hasta 10 MB.' (line 333) but there is no client-side size check in _processFile — a >10MB file is only rejected (if at all) downstream, and the picker already loads it fully into memory (withData: true), so a large file silently consumes memory. Also, after a successful template download there is no confirmation (e.g. snackbar) — the spinner just stops, giving weak 'visibility of system status' for an action whose result (a browser download) happens outside the app surface.
  - **Fix:** Add a lightweight size guard in _processFile that shows the existing inline error if file.size exceeds the documented 10MB, preventing a wasted parse round-trip (error prevention). Optionally show a brief 'Template descargado' snackbar after _downloadTemplate succeeds so the user knows the action completed.
  - **Evidencia:** Line 333 (10 MB claim), lines 69-104 (_processFile has no size check), lines 47-67 (_downloadTemplate ends silently).

- **[LOW · responsive]** Header title 'IMPORTAR PLAN' (line 212-221) uses height: 1 with fontSize 24 and no maxLines/overflow. With a longer localized title or large dynamic type, the tight line-height combined with the lack of overflow handling risks vertical clipping or awkward wrapping. The sibling preview screen header (coach_hub_plan_preview_screen.dart:380-391) sets maxLines:1 + ellipsis on its dynamic title, so this screen is slightly less defensive than its sibling. The screen overall scrolls (SingleChildScrollView) so large type is mostly safe, but this specific Text is the weak point.
  - **Fix:** For consistency with the preview header, consider maxLines + overflow handling (or softWrap) on the title, especially once strings are localized. Low priority since 'IMPORTAR PLAN' is short and fixed today.
  - **Evidencia:** Lines 212-221 (title, height:1, no maxLines) vs preview screen lines 380-391 (maxLines:1, ellipsis).

## lib/features/coach_hub/presentation/shell/proximamente_screen.dart (coach_hub module)

_ProximamenteScreen is a deliberate, minimal placeholder (ADR-CHW-009) for not-yet-shipped Coach Hub web sections. It is design-system clean on the hard rules: colors via AppPalette.of(context) with zero HEX literals or Colors.* constants, no direct PhosphorIcons usage (no icons at all), and spacing values 20/18 sit on the official scale {8,12,14,18,20}. The shell (CoachHubScaffold) owns the single Scaffold, sidebar navigation, and (stubbed) top bar/breadcrumb, so navigation affordances and loading/error/empty states are correctly out of this file's scope — there is no AsyncValue here. The real findings are scoped and mostly known debt: (1) hardcoded UI strings (the literal 'Próximamente.' and the injected label) violate the no-hardcoded-strings rule, but this is explicitly deferred project-wide for Coach Hub web via consistent // i18n: Fase W1 markers while AppL10n infrastructure already exists; (2) the body uses a bare TextStyle(fontSize:16) instead of the Barlow type token that the sibling SectionHeader applies via GoogleFonts; (3) no scroll wrapper creates a low-risk large-dynamic-type overflow. Overall a solid, intentionally thin screen — no invented problems._

- **[MEDIUM · microcopy-i18n]** User-facing strings are hardcoded rather than sourced from AppL10n. The literal 'Próximamente.' (line 27) and the injected 'label' (passed from sidebar_registry.dart, where all 19 labels are hardcoded es-AR) bypass the localization layer. This violates design-system rule #3 (never hard-code UI strings). It is acknowledged debt: every offending string carries a // i18n: Fase W1 marker and the AppL10n infrastructure already exists and is widely used elsewhere (lib/l10n/app_l10n.dart, accessed via AppL10n.of(context)). Until migrated, English/other-locale users see Spanish placeholder copy.
  - **Fix:** When Coach Hub web i18n lands (the planned Fase W1 follow-up), route both the placeholder body text and the section labels through AppL10n. Add a key like comingSoon for the body and localize sidebarRegistry labels. No action needed before that phase, but the // i18n markers should not be dropped silently.
  - **Evidencia:** proximamente_screen.dart:27 (Text 'Próximamente.'); label sourced from sidebar_registry.dart (e.g. lines ~57-70, label: 'Dashboard' // i18n: Fase W1)

- **[LOW · design-system]** The placeholder body text uses a bare TextStyle(color: palette.textMuted, fontSize: 16) instead of the project Barlow type token. The sibling SectionHeader in the same folder applies GoogleFonts.barlowCondensed for headings; per design-system.md, body copy should be Barlow. Using a raw TextStyle here means the font falls back to the theme/system default rather than the Barlow body family, and 16 is an ad-hoc size not tied to a documented token.
  - **Fix:** Use the body type token consistently, e.g. GoogleFonts.barlow(fontSize: 16, color: palette.textMuted) or pull from Theme.of(context).textTheme.bodyMedium configured with Barlow, mirroring how SectionHeader handles headings. Confirm the size against whatever body token the team standardizes.
  - **Evidencia:** proximamente_screen.dart:26-29 (TextStyle(color: palette.textMuted, fontSize: 16)); contrast with section_header.dart:19 (GoogleFonts.barlowCondensed)

- **[LOW · responsive]** The Column is not wrapped in a scroll view. Content is tiny (one header + one line) so it fits today, but at very large dynamic type sizes or a short/landscape viewport the fixed Padding plus header plus body could exceed available height and trigger a RenderFlex overflow with no way to scroll to the clipped content.
  - **Fix:** Wrap the content in a SingleChildScrollView (or use the module's existing content-area scroll pattern if CoachHubScaffold/ContentMaxWidth provides one) so the placeholder degrades gracefully under large type or constrained heights. Low priority given current content volume, but cheap insurance and a good default to establish before real section screens reuse this pattern.
  - **Evidencia:** proximamente_screen.dart:19-33 (Padding > Column with no scroll wrapper); shell content area is ContentMaxWidth(maxWidth:1240) inside an Expanded in coach_hub_scaffold.dart

## lib/features/feed/feed_screen.dart (feed module: FeedScreen + _FeedHeader, _AmigosBody, _MiGymBody, _PublicoBody, and child widgets FeedEmptyState, FeedSegmentPills, PostCard, PostAvatar)

_The Feed screen is structurally clean and disciplined on the design-system basics: it consistently uses AppPalette.of(context) (zero HEX literals, zero Colors.* constants) and TreinoIcon.X (no direct PhosphorIcons), all three segments handle data/loading/empty/error branches, and it correctly behaves as a root shell tab (no spurious back button). The real problems are systemic, not cosmetic. (1) I18N: the entire feed module hardcodes Spanish strings while the rest of the app (auth, coach, workout, profile, reviews) routes everything through AppL10n with full es/es-AR/en support — feed is the lone module violating design-system rule #3. (2) States/Usability: every error branch swallows the error and offers no retry, and there is no pull-to-refresh anywhere, even though the feed providers are FutureProviders (not auto-updating streams) — a failed or stale feed becomes a genuine dead-end with no user-driven recovery, inconsistent with the 'Reintentar' affordance used everywhere else. (3) Accessibility: the three icon-only actions (search, create, post overflow) have no Semantics labels and the search icon's tap target is ~20pt, well under the 44pt minimum. Fixing the i18n migration, adding retry + pull-to-refresh, and labeling/enlarging the icon buttons would bring this screen up to the standard the rest of the codebase already holds._

- **[HIGH · microcopy-i18n]** Every user-facing string in the feed screen and its children is hardcoded in Spanish, violating design-system rule #3 ('Nunca hard-code de strings de UI'). The project has a complete AppL10n setup with es, es-AR and en locales that is actively used by auth, coach, workout, profile and reviews modules — the feed module is the only one bypassing it. Hardcoded examples include 'FEED', the three pill labels ('AMIGOS', 'MI GYM', 'PÚBLICO'), all empty-state messages ('Aún no hay posts de tus amigos', 'Todavía no estás en un gym', 'Tu gym todavía no tiene posts', 'Aún no hay posts públicos'), the repeated error string 'No pudimos cargar tu feed. Intentá de nuevo.', and the relative-time strings in PostCard ('recién', 'hace ${m}m/h/d').
  - **Fix:** Migrate all feed strings to AppL10n keys (e.g. feedTitle, feedSegmentAmigos/Gym/Publico, feedEmptyAmigos/Gym/NoGym/Publico, feedLoadError, postRelativeTimeNow/Minutes/Hours/Days) following the same convention as coach*/workout* keys. Note the EN translations must actually be Spanish-free — right now even an English-locale user would see Spanish.
  - **Evidencia:** feed_screen.dart:113 'FEED'; :159/186/210/215/268 empty+error strings; feed_segment_pills.dart:23/30/37 pill labels; post_card.dart:173-179 relativeTime strings. grep confirms zero AppL10n references anywhere under lib/features/feed.

- **[HIGH · states]** All three error branches discard the error object (error: (_, __)) and render only a static centered sentence with no retry action. The rest of the app pairs every load error with a 'Reintentar' CTA (coachRetryLabel, workoutHistorialErrorRetry, plantillasRetryLabel, eliminarCuentaSheetRetryLabel all exist in AppL10n). Because the feed providers are FutureProviders (per the inline comments and public_profile_follow_button.dart which manually ref.invalidate(myFriendsFeedProvider)), they do NOT self-heal — a transient network failure leaves the user permanently stuck on the error text until they leave and re-enter the tab.
  - **Fix:** Add a retry button to each error branch that calls ref.invalidate(<feedProvider>) (myFriendsFeedProvider / myGymFeedProvider / feedPublicProvider). Extract the three near-identical error/loading/empty when() blocks into a single shared _FeedAsyncBody widget to remove ~100 lines of duplication and guarantee consistent recovery UX.
  - **Evidencia:** feed_screen.dart:182-194 (_AmigosBody), :240-252 (_MiGymBody), :293-305 (_PublicoBody) — identical error blocks, none with an onPressed/retry.

- **[HIGH · usability]** There is no pull-to-refresh on any feed segment. Since the feeds are FutureProviders (one-shot fetch, not streams), a user who lands on a stale or empty list has no in-screen way to re-fetch — the only refresh path is the indirect side effects triggered by creating a post or accepting a friend request. This breaks Nielsen's 'user control & freedom' and 'visibility of system status': the feed can silently go stale with no manual reload.
  - **Fix:** Wrap each ListView in a RefreshIndicator (color: palette.accent) whose onRefresh awaits ref.refresh(<feedProvider>.future). Apply it to the empty state too (wrap the empty Center in a scrollable so it can be pulled), so an empty 'Aún no hay posts' state is also refreshable.
  - **Evidencia:** feed_screen.dart:162-177/220-235/273-288 ListView.separated with no RefreshIndicator ancestor; grep for RefreshIndicator/onRefresh in feed returns no UI refresh control.

- **[HIGH · accessibility]** The icon-only actions have no accessible names. The header search icon (TreinoIcon.search) and the create-post '+' button are bare GestureDetector + Icon with no Semantics label, so a VoiceOver user hears nothing actionable. The post overflow IconButton explicitly sets tooltip: null and onPressed: null, giving it neither a label nor a hint of being a (future) control.
  - **Fix:** Wrap the search and create actions in Semantics(button: true, label: l10n.feedSearchA11y / l10n.feedCreatePostA11y) or use IconButton with a tooltip. For the overflow stub, either hide it from semantics (ExcludeSemantics) until it is wired up, or give it a tooltip; a disabled, unlabeled button is confusing to AT users.
  - **Evidencia:** feed_screen.dart:122-126 search GestureDetector; :128-140 create '+' GestureDetector; post_card.dart:98-108 IconButton(onPressed: null, tooltip: null).
