(1) i18n: only 6 strings are localized via AppL10n; ~25 user-facing strings (section labels, hints, validators, button labels, empty states, sheet titles, the "Quitar" tooltip) are hardcoded with no i18n-debt marker — worse than the sibling screen, which at least tags every hardcode. (2) States: gymsProvider is read with valueOrNull and no loading/error branch, so a gym's saved name silently degrades to the literal "Gimnasio"; _addGym awaits gymsProvider.future with no try/catch, so a failed load just no-ops with zero feedback. (3) Usability/navigation: in edit mode there is no dirty-state guard (the sibling personal screen has a discard-confirmation dialog), so a stray back tap discards edits; in onboarding mode the screen is a deliberate hard gate (PopScope + hidden back arrow + forced redirect) with no logout/escape, which is a dead-end if the user can't or won't complete it. Accessibility gaps: progress spinners and the avatar-equivalent icons lack Semantics labels, and a couple of tap targets (dropdown, "Detectar" TextButton) are likely under 44pt. Spacing also breaks the documented scale (uses 4px, which the design system explicitly forbids)._

- **[HIGH · microcopy-i18n]** ~25 user-facing strings are hardcoded in Spanish instead of routed through AppL10n, even though the screen already imports and uses AppL10n for 6 strings. Hardcoded examples: every _SectionLabel ('BIO', 'ESPECIALIDAD', 'PRECIO MENSUAL (ARS)', 'ALIAS / DATOS DE COBRO', 'GIMNASIOS DONDE TRABAJÁS', 'LUGARES PROPIOS'), all TextField hints, all inline validator messages ('Escribí una bio.', 'Al menos 20 caracteres.', 'Ingresá un número entero.', 'Mínimo $500.', etc.), button labels ('GUARDAR', 'Agregar gimnasio', 'Agregar lugar propio', 'GUARDAR LUGAR'), empty-state copy, sheet titles ('Elegí un gimnasio', 'Agregar lugar propio'), the trash tooltip 'Quitar', and the footer note. Unlike the sibling profile_edit_personal_screen.dart, these are NOT even marked with a '// i18n: Fase 6 Etapa 3' debt comment, so they are invisible to a future localization sweep. This also violates design-system.md rule §3 (never hard-code UI strings).
  - **Fix:** Move all user-facing strings into AppL10n keys (intl_es_AR.arb + generated). At minimum, until that lands, tag each hardcode with the same '// i18n:' marker the personal screen uses so the debt is greppable. Note the bio min-length message ('Al menos 20 caracteres.') and the price bounds are also business rules that belong in l10n with placeholders.
  - **Evidencia:** _SectionLabel calls lines 246/268/279/295/509/575; hints lines 255/285/303/800/997; validators lines 259-264, 288-290; button labels lines 358, 543, 601, 1072; tooltip 'Quitar' line 677; footer line 368.

- **[HIGH · states]** _GymsSection consumes gymsProvider via gymsAsync.valueOrNull with no loading or error branch. While gyms are still loading (or if the provider errors), gymsById is empty, so every saved gym card renders the literal fallback title 'Gimnasio' and a null address instead of the real name. The user sees generic placeholder cards with no indication that data is still arriving or failed to load — a silent degraded state.
  - **Fix:** Use gymsAsync.when(...) (or guard on isLoading/hasError) and render a per-card shimmer/placeholder while loading and an inline retry affordance on error, instead of collapsing both into the 'Gimnasio' fallback. The fallback string should only appear for a genuinely missing gym, not for a pending/failed fetch.
  - **Evidencia:** _GymsSection.build lines 500-504 (gymsAsync.valueOrNull ?? const <Gym>[]) and line 532 (gymsById[loc.gymId]?.name ?? 'Gimnasio').

- **[MEDIUM · states]** _addGym awaits ref.read(gymsProvider.future) with no try/catch. If the gyms fetch throws (network/Firestore error), the await rejects, the function aborts before showModalBottomSheet, and the user gets zero feedback — the 'Agregar gimnasio' button appears to do nothing. There is no visible loading indicator on the button during the await either, so on a slow connection the tap also feels dead.
  - **Fix:** Wrap the gymsProvider.future read in try/catch and surface a SnackBar (localized) on failure; optionally show a transient busy state on the trigger button while the future resolves so the tap registers as 'working'.
  - **Evidencia:** _addGym lines 94-111 (final gyms = await ref.read(gymsProvider.future); with no error handling, then showModalBottomSheet).

- **[MEDIUM · usability]** In edit mode there is no dirty-state protection. The user can fill in bio, price, locations, toggle online, then tap the AppBar back arrow (or iOS swipe-back) and lose everything with no confirmation. The sibling profile_edit_personal_screen.dart explicitly implements this safety net (_isDirty + _showDiscardDialog 'Descartar los cambios?'), so this screen is inconsistent with its own module and violates Nielsen's 'user control & freedom' / error-prevention.
  - **Fix:** Add dirty tracking (compare current form state against the seeded profile) and intercept back navigation with a discard-confirmation dialog, reusing the pattern already established in profile_edit_personal_screen.dart for consistency.
  - **Evidencia:** AppBar back uses default automaticallyImplyLeading with no onPop guard (lines 387-393); no _isDirty/_showDiscardDialog equivalent exists. Compare profile_edit_personal_screen.dart lines 258-329.

- **[MEDIUM · navigation]** Onboarding mode is a hard gate with no escape hatch. PopScope(canPop:false) blocks the OS back gesture, the AppBar back arrow is hidden (automaticallyImplyLeading:false), and router.dart force-redirects any incomplete trainer to this route. The only exit is a fully valid submit. A trainer who cannot complete the form right now (e.g. needs to look up their CBU, has no location yet, hits the save error repeatedly) is trapped with no way to log out, defer, or back out — a potential dead-end and a support-ticket generator.
  - **Fix:** Keep the gate, but add a low-emphasis escape affordance in onboarding mode: a 'Cerrar sesión' / 'Lo hago más tarde' text action, or at least surface logout. This preserves the completeness requirement while honoring user control & freedom.
  - **Evidencia:** PopScope lines 379-385; AppBar automaticallyImplyLeading false lines 391-392; forced redirect router.dart lines 137-141.

- **[MEDIUM · accessibility]** Icon-only and progress UI lack semantic labels. The save button's busy state is a bare CircularProgressIndicator (lines 349-356) with no Semantics, so a screen reader announces nothing while saving — failing 'visibility of system status' for non-sighted users. Same for the location-detect spinner (line 1045) and the full-screen load spinner (line 227). The trash IconButton has a tooltip ('Quitar') but it is generic — it does not say WHICH location is being removed, and the tooltip text is hardcoded (not localized). No Semantics on the leading location-type icons either.
  - **Fix:** Wrap progress indicators in Semantics(label: l10n.saving / l10n.detecting, liveRegion: true) or use a labelled loading state. Give the remove IconButton a contextual semanticLabel like 'Quitar {locationName}' so VoiceOver users know what they're deleting, and localize it.
  - **Evidencia:** Save spinner lines 348-356; detect spinner lines 1042-1046; full-screen spinner line 227; trash IconButton lines 674-678 (hardcoded tooltip 'Quitar', no contextual label).

- **[MEDIUM · accessibility]** Likely sub-44pt tap targets. The specialty DropdownButton sits in a Container with only horizontal padding and no minimum height enforced (lines 454-481) — default DropdownButton height can fall short of 44pt. The 'Detectar'/'Recalcular' TextButton (lines 1039-1051) and the gym-picker drag handle area also rely on default sizing. iOS HIG and WCAG 2.5.5 want >=44pt.
  - **Fix:** Enforce a minimum 44-48pt height on the dropdown container and on the Detectar TextButton (e.g. minimumSize / ConstrainedBox). The location-remove IconButton and OutlinedButtons are already fine (44/48).
  - **Evidencia:** Dropdown container lines 454-461 (padding horizontal only); Detectar TextButton lines 1039-1051 (default TextButton sizing).

- **[LOW · design-system]** Spacing values outside the documented scale. design-system.md states the spacing scale is ONLY 8·12·14·18·20 and explicitly says NOT to use 4 (or 16/24). The screen uses 4px in several places: _CustomLocationsSection SizedBox(height: 4) (line 576), _LocationCard SizedBox(height: 2) (line 660), and _OnlineToggle vertical: 4 padding (line 700). Minor but it's a direct, checkable violation of a 'no negociable' rule.
  - **Fix:** Replace 4/2px gaps with 8px (the smallest allowed token) or restructure so the rhythm uses only scale values. Consider centralizing the spacing scale as named constants so these slips are catchable in review.
  - **Evidencia:** line 576 (height: 4), line 660 (height: 2), line 700 (vertical: 4).

- **[LOW · design-system]** Inconsistent corner radii vs documented radii tokens. The design system defines r-sm=12 (inputs/chips) and r-md=16 (cards). This screen uses 14 for inputs AND cards almost everywhere (lines 405-414, 457, 516, 637, 703, 806, etc.) and 20 for sheets — while the sibling personal screen uses the documented 12 for the same input fields. So inputs are 14 here vs 12 there: a within-module inconsistency, and 14 is not one of the defined radius tokens.
  - **Fix:** Align radii with the documented tokens (12 for inputs/chips, 16 for cards) or, if 14 is an intentional house value, codify it in the design system. Either way, make inputs match the sibling screen so the two edit screens feel like one system.
  - **Evidencia:** Inputs use circular(14) lines 405/409/413/457/516/637/703; sibling profile_edit_personal_screen.dart uses circular(12) lines 537-560.

- **[LOW · consistency]** Two different heading patterns across the same module. This screen uses a Material AppBar with an AppBar title for the page header, while the sibling profile_edit_personal_screen.dart uses an inline custom header row (TreinoIcon.back + Barlow Condensed uppercase title) and no Scaffold AppBar. Same module, same 'edit my profile' task, two visually distinct chrome treatments — users moving between them get a subtle inconsistency in heading style and back-affordance placement.
  - **Fix:** Pick one header pattern for the profile-edit family. If the inline Barlow-Condensed header is the house style (it matches design-system typography guidance for section/page titles better than a default AppBar), adopt it here too.
  - **Evidencia:** This screen: Scaffold AppBar lines 387-393. Sibling: inline header row lines 354-374 with TreinoIcon.back + barlowCondensed.

- **[LOW · microcopy-i18n]** Custom-location subtitle exposes raw lat/lng coordinates as the user-facing label (e.g. '-34.6037, -58.3816'). This is recognition-over-recall hostile — coordinates are meaningless to a trainer reviewing their saved places, and the same raw-coordinate string appears in the add-sheet confirmation. There is also overflow risk: long localized section labels and gym names rely on ellipsis (good) but the coordinate subtitle and the online-toggle subtitle could clip awkwardly at large dynamic type.
  - **Fix:** Show the user-entered label prominently and demote coordinates to a muted secondary or a small map thumbnail, or drop coordinates from the card entirely (they were just detected, the label is what matters). Verify the layout with the largest dynamic-type setting.
  - **Evidencia:** _CustomLocationsSection subtitle line 591-592 (lat/lng toStringAsFixed(4)); add-sheet confirmation line 1030.

## lib/features/profile/presentation/profile_gym_screen.dart (profile module — gym selection)

_Solid, on-brand screen that correctly uses AppPalette tokens, TreinoIcon wrappers, and design-system spacing — zero HEX/Colors.* literals and zero direct PhosphorIcons. The real gaps are in STATES and ACCESSIBILITY: the save action swallows errors silently (no catch + no SnackBar, unlike the sibling edit screen), filtered search has no empty-results state, and icon-only/header controls lack Semantics labels. Microcopy is hardcoded but already tagged as tracked i18n debt (Fase 6 Etapa 3), so it is noted at lower severity. The gym catalog is synchronous/hardcoded, so a missing list loading/error branch is acceptable today but a latent risk once it becomes a Firestore stream._

- **[HIGH · states]** The save flow swallows failures silently. `_save` (lines 37-45) wraps the repository call in try/finally with NO catch branch. If `userRepositoryProvider.update()` throws (network/permission error), `_saving` is reset and the spinner disappears, but the screen does NOT pop and the user gets ZERO feedback — it looks identical to nothing happening. This violates Nielsen's 'visibility of system status' and the error-handling convention already established in this exact module.
  - **Fix:** Add a `catch` that shows a SnackBar with a voseo error message, mirroring profile_edit_personal_screen.dart (lines 182-195, 241-244): `catch (_) { if (mounted) ScaffoldMessenger.of(context).showSnackBar(SnackBar(content: Text('No pudimos guardar tu gimnasio. Probá de nuevo.', style: GoogleFonts.barlow(fontSize: 14)))); }`. Keep the existing finally to reset `_saving`.
  - **Evidencia:** _save() lines 37-45 (try/finally, no catch); contrast with sibling profile_edit_personal_screen.dart lines 182-195 and 240-244 which use try/catch + SnackBar.

- **[MEDIUM · states]** No empty-results state for the search filter. The ListView uses `itemCount: gyms.length + 1` (line 116), so when the query matches nothing, `filteredGymsProvider` returns an empty list and the user sees ONLY the trailing 'OTRO GYM / SIN GYM' card with no explanation that their search yielded no matches. The sibling profile_routines_screen.dart deliberately designs an empty state ('Tu PF todavía no te asignó ninguna rutina.'), so this screen is inconsistent with the module's own pattern.
  - **Fix:** When `gyms.isEmpty` and the query is non-empty, render a centered muted message above the OTRO GYM row, e.g. 'No encontramos gimnasios con ese nombre.' (Barlow 14, palette.textMuted), matching the routines-screen empty pattern.
  - **Evidencia:** ListView.separated itemCount line 116; filteredGymsProvider returns [] on no match (profile_setup_providers.dart lines 38-46); empty-state precedent in profile_routines_screen.dart lines 77-92.

- **[MEDIUM · accessibility]** The back control is not exposed as a button to screen readers. The header is a `GestureDetector` (lines 67-84) wrapping an icon + 'GIMNASIO' title with no Semantics; the icon-only affordance (TreinoIcon.back) has no label and no `button: true` role. VoiceOver will read 'GIMNASIO' as static text and the back gesture is undiscoverable. Same gap exists on the GymCard rows (selectable list items with no selected-state semantics).
  - **Fix:** Wrap the header GestureDetector in `Semantics(button: true, label: AppL10n...gymBack / 'Volver')`. For the back affordance specifically, consider a real IconButton or add `excludeSemantics` + a labeled Semantics so the title text isn't conflated with the action. On GymCard, expose `Semantics(selected: selected, button: true)` so VoiceOver announces the current selection.
  - **Evidencia:** Header GestureDetector lines 67-84 (no Semantics, icon-only TreinoIcon.back line 72); GymCard InkWell gym_card.dart lines 29-44 has no selected/button semantics.

- **[LOW · states]** The gym list has no loading/error branch. `filteredGymsProvider` is currently a synchronous Provider over a hardcoded catalog (_kHardcodedGyms), so today there is genuinely nothing to load — this is acceptable now. But the provider's own doc comment says it must become a Firestore StreamProvider, at which point this `Column(...gyms.length...)` consumes the list directly and would break / show a blank list during load or on error.
  - **Fix:** Acceptable as-is for the hardcoded catalog. Flag for the Firestore migration: when filteredGymsProvider becomes async, consume it via `.when(loading/error/data)` like profile_routines_screen.dart so loading and error are handled. No change needed today.
  - **Evidencia:** filteredGymsProvider is synchronous (profile_setup_providers.dart lines 38-46) with a comment 'Cuando se cree, reemplazar este provider por un StreamProvider'; consumed directly at profile_gym_screen.dart line 59.

- **[LOW · microcopy-i18n]** Four user-facing strings are hardcoded instead of routed through AppL10n: 'GIMNASIO' (line 75), 'OTRO GYM / SIN GYM' (line 130), 'No registramos tu gimnasio' (line 131), 'GUARDAR' (line 169). All are tagged `// i18n: Fase 6 Etapa 3`, so this is tracked debt, not an oversight. Separately, the already-localized `profileGymSearchHint` returns 'Buscar gym' in BOTH es and en (app_l10n_en.dart:705 == es), so the EN locale is not actually translated.
  - **Fix:** When Fase 6 Etapa 3 lands, move the four strings to AppL10n keys (e.g. profileGymTitle, profileGymNoGymName, profileGymNoGymSubtitle, profileGymSave) consistent with profileGymSearchHint. Also fix the EN translation of profileGymSearchHint (currently 'Buscar gym' should be e.g. 'Search gym').
  - **Evidencia:** Hardcoded strings lines 75, 130, 131, 169 (all tagged 'i18n: Fase 6 Etapa 3'); duplicated hint value in app_l10n_en.dart:705 and app_l10n_es.dart:734.

- **[LOW · usability]** Mixed dismissal model with no destructive-discard guard. The header back gesture pops immediately (context.pop, line 68) while a separate GUARDAR button persists — so a user who selects a different gym and then taps back loses the pending change with no confirmation. The change-detection is correct (saveEnabled = _pendingGymId != currentGymId), but there is no 'descartar cambios' prompt on back, unlike potential expectations for an edit screen.
  - **Fix:** Low priority given the action is a single-tap reselection (low data-loss cost). If parity with other edit screens is desired, intercept back when `_pendingGymId != currentGymId` and show a discard confirmation; otherwise leave as-is — the lightweight pop is defensible for a one-field picker.
  - **Evidencia:** Header pop line 68; saveEnabled diff check line 60; no PopScope/discard guard present.

## lib/features/profile/presentation/profile_routines_screen.dart (module: profile) — "MIS RUTINAS" trainer-assigned plans list

_Structurally solid screen: it correctly handles all four AsyncValue branches (loading/error/empty/data), uses AppPalette.of(context) for every color, uses TreinoIcon.back (no raw PhosphorIcons), and properly insets the ListView for the floating navbar via MediaQuery.paddingOf(context).bottom. The real problems are i18n and design-token discipline: every user-facing string is hardcoded even though the l10n key workoutMisRutinasSectionTitle => 'MIS RUTINAS' already exists and the sibling profile_gym_screen already migrated to AppL10n. Typography is built with inline GoogleFonts.* calls instead of the theme text tokens that its own child RoutineCard uses. Accessibility gaps: the icon+text back control is not exposed as a button to screen readers (no Semantics), and the error state is a dead-end with no retry. None of these block usage, but the i18n and typography findings are clear violations of the project's non-negotiable UI code rules._

- **[HIGH · microcopy-i18n]** Every user-facing string is hardcoded in the widget: the header 'MIS RUTINAS' (line 42), the error message 'No pudimos cargar tus rutinas. Intentá de nuevo.' (line 66), and the empty-state 'Tu PF todavía no te asignó ninguna rutina.' (line 82). This violates design-system.md rule #3 ('Nunca hard-code de strings de UI'). The l10n infrastructure is not only available — it is already POPULATED with the exact title: app_l10n_es.dart defines `workoutMisRutinasSectionTitle => 'MIS RUTINAS'`. The `// i18n: Fase 6 Etapa 3` comments are stale deferral markers; the sibling profile_gym_screen.dart in the same module/etapa already migrated its hint to `AppL10n.of(context).profileGymSearchHint`, so the migration window is past.
  - **Fix:** Route all three strings through AppL10n.of(context). Reuse the existing `workoutMisRutinasSectionTitle` for the header and add two new keys (e.g. profileRoutinesLoadError, profileRoutinesEmpty) to app_l10n.dart / _es / _en. The strings are already correct voseo ('Intentá', 'no te asignó'), so this is purely centralization. Remove the `// i18n: Fase 6 Etapa 3` comments once migrated.
  - **Evidencia:** lines 42, 66, 82; existing key app_l10n_es.dart:525 `workoutMisRutinasSectionTitle => 'MIS RUTINAS'`; sibling proof profile_gym_screen.dart:98 uses AppL10n

- **[MEDIUM · design-system]** Typography is constructed with inline GoogleFonts.barlowCondensed(...) (line 43) and GoogleFonts.barlow(...) (lines 68, 84) with hand-set fontWeight/fontSize/color, instead of the theme text tokens. This is inconsistent with the screen's own child: RoutineCard uses `theme.textTheme.titleMedium` and `theme.textTheme.bodySmall` (routine_card.dart:79,88). Hard-coding the font family and sizes per-screen defeats the central typography scale and drifts if the theme changes. (Note: the identical sibling profile_gym_screen.dart shares this anti-pattern, so it's a module-wide habit, not a one-off.)
  - **Fix:** Replace the inline GoogleFonts calls with Theme.of(context).textTheme entries (e.g. a titleLarge/headline style for the 'MIS RUTINAS' header and bodyMedium/bodySmall for the empty/error copy), overriding only color via copyWith(color: palette.textPrimary/textMuted). Align with how RoutineCard already consumes the theme.
  - **Evidencia:** lines 43-47, 68-72, 84-88 vs routine_card.dart:79,88

- **[MEDIUM · accessibility]** The back control (lines 34-51) is a GestureDetector wrapping an Icon + 'MIS RUTINAS' Text. To a screen reader it announces as two separate static items ('back-caret icon', then 'MIS RUTINAS' text) with no indication that the row is tappable and pops the route — there is no Semantics(button: true) and no label/tooltip. The icon itself has no semantic label. grep confirms zero Semantics/Tooltip in the screen (and in the gym sibling), so it's a module pattern. VoiceOver users get no 'go back' affordance and may not realize the header is interactive.
  - **Fix:** Wrap the GestureDetector in Semantics(button: true, label: <localized 'Volver' / 'Atrás'>, child: ...) or, better, use a real BackButton/IconButton for the caret (which carries the built-in MaterialLocalizations back tooltip and a guaranteed 48pt target) and keep the title as a plain heading. If keeping the merged row, add MergeSemantics so it reads as one actionable element.
  - **Evidencia:** lines 34-51; grep for Semantics|Tooltip returned no matches in this file or profile_gym_screen.dart

- **[MEDIUM · states]** The error branch is a dead-end: `error: (_, __)` (line 62) discards both the error object and stack trace, shows a static message, and offers NO retry action. On a transient network failure the only escape is the back row — the user cannot re-attempt the load in place. This breaks Nielsen 'user control & freedom' and 'help users recover from errors'. The discarded error params also mean nothing is logged for diagnostics.
  - **Fix:** Add a 'Reintentar' button under the error text that calls ref.invalidate(assignedRoutinesProvider(myUid)) (or ref.refresh) to retrigger the fetch. Capture the error/stack into a logger instead of `(_, __)` so failures are observable. Localize both the message and the retry label.
  - **Evidencia:** lines 62-75

- **[LOW · states]** The loading state is a bare centered CircularProgressIndicator (lines 57-61) with no contextual label, and the empty state (lines 78-91) is a single line of muted text with no icon, illustration, or call-to-action. Compared to the design system's expectation that empty/loading states communicate context, both are minimal. The empty state in particular gives the athlete no next step (e.g. nothing pointing them toward contacting their PF).
  - **Fix:** Loading: acceptable as-is for a fast list, but consider a skeleton of RoutineCard placeholders for perceived performance consistency with the rest of the app. Empty: pair the message with a TreinoIcon (e.g. tabWorkout/dumbbell) and, if applicable, a secondary affordance or hint so it doesn't read as a broken screen.
  - **Evidencia:** lines 57-61 (loading), 78-91 (empty)

- **[LOW · responsive]** The loading/error/empty branches use Center inside an Expanded that spans the full body height including the area BEHIND the floating translucent navbar (the shell uses extendBody: true and publishes the bar height via MediaQuery.padding.bottom — router.dart:561-571). The data ListView correctly compensates with `14 + MediaQuery.paddingOf(context).bottom` (line 96), but the centered states do not, so their content is vertically centered relative to a region partly occluded by the navbar, biasing the text slightly low. Not clipping, but a minor optical inconsistency. Long localized strings (German/Portuguese) in the error/empty copy are already protected by horizontal padding + TextAlign.center, so no overflow risk there.
  - **Fix:** For the centered states, either reduce the effective height by the bottom inset (e.g. Padding(bottom: MediaQuery.paddingOf(context).bottom) around the Center) or use Align(alignment: const Alignment(0, -0.1)) so the message sits in the optically centered, fully-visible region above the floating bar.
  - **Evidencia:** lines 56-92 (Center states) vs line 96 (ListView inset); shell extendBody router.dart:562

## lib/features/profile/profile_screen.dart

_probe5simple_

- **[MEDIUM · design-system]** Cards reinvent the border token instead of the dedicated palette dot border. Sibling TrainerProfileView uses it, so the two role branches render different hairlines.
  - **Fix:** Use the shared border token for all card borders and dividers.
  - **Evidencia:** profile screen 147

- **[HIGH · accessibility]** Zero Semantics anywhere. Avatar has no label, chevrons are unlabeled, tappable rows are bare GestureDetectors with no button semantics.
  - **Fix:** Add Semantics per tile, label the avatar, merge each stat.
  - **Evidencia:** profile section tile 50

- **[HIGH · microcopy-i18n]** i18n half-done: CUENTA localized but other sections are hardcoded Spanish. A key already exists but is unused.
  - **Fix:** Route remaining strings through AppL10n and reuse existing keys.
  - **Evidencia:** profile screen 72

- **[MEDIUM · states]** Stats row maps both loading and error to the same silent dash, so a failed fetch looks like a load and offers no retry.
  - **Fix:** Differentiate the error branch with a retry or distinct caption.
  - **Evidencia:** profile screen 156

- **[MEDIUM · usability]** Cerrar sesion logs out on one tap with no confirmation, unlike Eliminar cuenta which has a confirm sheet. signOut can throw but no listener surfaces the error.
  - **Fix:** Add a confirm before sign-out or show a SnackBar on failure.
  - **Evidencia:** profile screen 94

## lib/features/workout/presentation/custom_exercise_editor_screen.dart (workout module — create/edit a trainer's custom exercise)

_The screen is structurally clean and largely on-token (palette + TreinoIcon are used correctly throughout the editor itself, spacing follows the 8/12/14/18/20 scale, radii use r-sm/r-full, the delete flow has a proper confirmation dialog, and upload progress is well communicated). Three high-severity issues stand out: (1) edit mode reads its AsyncValue with no loading/error branch, so the form can silently render empty or stale while the trainer's exercise stream loads or fails; (2) all user-facing strings are hardcoded despite AppL10n being the established pattern across the rest of the workout module (arb files exist, including intl_es_AR); (3) the icon-only back button is a bare 20px GestureDetector with no Semantics label and sub-44pt tap target. Medium issues: no unsaved-changes guard on back/swipe (inconsistent with the delete confirmation already present), Colors.* literals in the upload button and the shared video-player child, and a misleading play icon used to signal upload-in-progress. The sibling my_exercises_screen.dart shares the hardcoded-strings and back-button gaps, so fixes should be applied consistently._

- **[HIGH · states]** In edit mode the screen reads the exercise from an AsyncValue with NO loading or error branch. Lines 71-74: `final listAsync = ref.watch(customExercisesForTrainerStreamProvider(uid)); final list = listAsync.valueOrNull ?? const []; existing = list.where(...).firstOrNull;`. While the stream is loading, `existing` is null, so the form renders EMPTY fields, the title/CTA still say 'EDITAR / GUARDAR CAMBIOS', and the Delete button is hidden (gated on `existing != null`, line 161). If the stream errors, the user silently sees a blank 'new' form. There is no visibility of system status (Nielsen #1) and the user could unknowingly overwrite/duplicate. The sibling `my_exercises_screen.dart` (lines 50-70) correctly uses `.when(loading/error/data)` — this screen should hydrate from the same source with explicit loading and error states.
  - **Fix:** Branch on the AsyncValue explicitly in edit mode: show a centered spinner (palette.accent) while loading, an error message + retry while errored, and only render the form once data arrives and the exercise is found. Add a 'not found' state for a deleted/invalid exerciseId rather than silently degrading to an empty form.
  - **Evidencia:** build(), lines 70-75 and 161 (delete button gated on existing); contrast with my_exercises_screen.dart:50-70

- **[HIGH · microcopy-i18n]** Every user-facing string is a hardcoded literal, violating design-system rule #3 ('Nunca hard-code de strings de UI') and breaking consistency with the rest of the workout module, which already uses AppL10n (e.g. mis_rutinas_section.dart, plantillas_section.dart, historial_section.dart all call `AppL10n.of(context)`; arb files exist at lib/l10n/intl_es_AR.arb). Affected: 'EDITAR/NUEVO EJERCICIO' (91), labels 'Nombre' (106) / 'Grupo muscular' (113) / 'Descripción / cues' (121) / 'Video del ejercicio' (129), hints (110, 125, 133), the long YouTube/Firebase explainer (146-148), 'BORRAR EJERCICIO' (181), 'GUARDAR CAMBIOS/EJERCICIO' (218-220), the delete dialog (338-363), and all five toast strings (245, 270, 290, 322, 378). The upload button strings (553-565) and the video player placeholder strings (exercise_video_player.dart:298-299, 70) are also hardcoded.
  - **Fix:** Move all strings into AppL10n following the existing `AppL10n.of(context).workout...` keys used by sibling widgets. Keep the warm voseo tone already present ('Poné un nombre', 'Subí tu video').
  - **Evidencia:** Lines 91, 106, 110, 113, 121, 125, 129, 133, 146-148, 181, 218-220, 245, 270, 290, 322, 338-363, 378, 553-565; child exercise_video_player.dart:70, 298-299

- **[HIGH · accessibility]** The back affordance is a bare `GestureDetector` wrapping a 20px `Icon(TreinoIcon.back)` (lines 83-88). It has no Semantics label (a screen reader announces nothing actionable, or just 'back' icon name) and no enforced 44pt tap target — the hit area is ~20pt plus whatever the opaque behavior covers in the Row, well under the iOS 44pt minimum. The module elsewhere uses `IconButton` with `tooltip:` (trainer_workout_view.dart:497/534, athlete_detail_screen.dart:1537) which gives both a 48pt target and a semantic label; this screen and its sibling don't.
  - **Fix:** Replace the GestureDetector with an `IconButton` (44-48pt min) or wrap in `Semantics(button: true, label: <l10n 'Volver'>)` and pad to a 44pt minimum hit area. Apply the same fix to my_exercises_screen.dart:30-35 for module consistency.
  - **Evidencia:** Lines 83-88; contrast trainer_workout_view.dart:489-497

- **[MEDIUM · usability]** No unsaved-changes guard. A user can fill name/description/muscle/video then tap the back chevron (line 84 `context.pop()`) or iOS swipe-back and lose all input with no confirmation — a user-control-and-freedom gap (Nielsen #3) that's especially costly here given video upload effort. Note the delete flow DOES have a confirmation dialog (lines 333-367), so the absence of any guard on discard is an inconsistency in the same screen.
  - **Fix:** Track a dirty flag (compare controllers/_selectedMuscle against the hydrated values) and show a 'Descartar cambios?' confirmation on pop when dirty, mirroring the existing delete-confirmation dialog style.
  - **Evidencia:** Back handler line 84; delete confirmation precedent lines 333-367

- **[MEDIUM · design-system]** Direct `Colors.*` literals are used instead of AppPalette tokens, violating rule #1 (no HEX/Colors constants in widgets). On this screen the violations are concentrated in the imported child widget `_UploadVideoButton` (Material `color: Colors.transparent`, line 528) and pervasively in exercise_video_player.dart (`Colors.black.withValues(...)` overlays at 95/258, `Colors.white` in the play overlay 116/119 and progress bar 274-275, `Colors.black` icon at 134). Some neutral overlays (translucent black scrims) are arguably acceptable, but the white/black brand surfaces should resolve from the palette so both Mint Magenta and Electric Violet themes stay consistent.
  - **Fix:** Replace `Colors.transparent` with `palette` equivalents or keep only where genuinely theme-neutral; route scrim/overlay colors through palette tokens (or add a documented `scrim`/`onMedia` token to AppPalette) rather than raw Colors constants.
  - **Evidencia:** custom_exercise_editor_screen.dart:528; exercise_video_player.dart:95, 116, 119, 134, 258, 274-275

- **[MEDIUM · states]** The upload-in-progress affordance shows `Icon(uploading ? TreinoIcon.play : TreinoIcon.plus)` (lines 542-544). Using the PLAY glyph to signal 'uploading' is misleading — play implies media playback, not progress. The percentage text and LinearProgressIndicator below do carry status, but the leading icon contradicts them.
  - **Fix:** While uploading, show a small CircularProgressIndicator or an upload/cloud-up glyph (add a semantic name to TreinoIcon if missing) instead of the play icon.
  - **Evidencia:** _UploadVideoButton.build, lines 541-545

- **[MEDIUM · accessibility]** Heavy reliance on fixed font sizes via GoogleFonts (e.g. 11px captions at 153/566/570, 12-13px labels and CTAs) with fixed-height buttons (`Size.fromHeight(44/48)`) and a `_Field` with `maxLines: 3`. With large Dynamic Type the small captions and the multiline description field risk clipping/overflow, and the screen does not appear to respect or cap textScaler anywhere. The video explainer block (lines 145-155) is a long 11px paragraph particularly exposed.
  - **Fix:** Verify with iOS largest accessibility text sizes; allow buttons to grow vertically (avoid hard-capping height with single-line text) and ensure caption text wraps rather than clips. Consider a minimum legible size for the 11px captions.
  - **Evidencia:** Lines 145-155, 153, 168, 205, 553-570; _Field maxLines 3 at line 127

- **[LOW · states]** Error feedback for save/delete/upload failures is delivered via a plain default SnackBar (`_toast`, lines 597-599) with no retry action and default (non-themed) styling. The module's mis_rutinas error state offers a retry affordance (workoutMisRutinasErrorRetry). Transient toasts for a failed save are also easy to miss after the user already left attention on the button.
  - **Fix:** Use a themed SnackBar (palette colors, optional floating) and add a 'Reintentar' action for save/upload failures so the user has a recovery path without re-tapping blindly.
  - **Evidencia:** _toast lines 597-599; used at 245, 270, 290, 322, 378

## lib/features/workout/presentation/exercise_detail_screen.dart (workout module — Exercise Detail screen)

_A genuinely solid screen. All four AsyncValue branches are handled (data/loading/error + null→not-found), with a loading skeleton, an error state with Reintentar retry, and empty states for technique and history. The persistent floating back button never lets a deep-linked user dead-end (falls back to context.go('/workout')). AppPalette tokens and TreinoIcon are used correctly throughout the screen and its child widgets — no HEX literals leak in (Colors.black/white are only used as legitimate translucent scrims/overlays over photos, which is the correct tool there, not a palette token). Spacing is almost entirely on the 8/12/14/18/20 scale. The findings below are real but mostly polish: the standout issue is the icon-only back button missing the tooltip/Semantics label that every other icon button in the app has. The hardcoded Spanish strings are a module-wide pattern (identical in the sibling RoutineDetailScreen), not a regression specific to this screen._

- **[HIGH · accessibility]** The icon-only back button in _BackBar has no accessibility label. The IconButton wraps only Icon(TreinoIcon.back) with no tooltip and no Semantics, so VoiceOver/TalkBack announces it as an unlabeled button (or just the raw icon code point). This is the primary navigation affordance and the only way out of a deep-linked screen.
  - **Fix:** Add tooltip: 'Volver' to the IconButton (Flutter exposes the tooltip as the semantic label automatically). This matches the established app-wide pattern — coach_hub_upload_plan_screen.dart, legal_document_screen.dart, chat_screen.dart and others all set tooltip on their back/icon buttons. The same fix should be applied to the identical _BackBar in routine_detail_screen.dart.
  - **Evidencia:** exercise_detail_screen.dart:111-115 (IconButton with icon only, no tooltip/Semantics). Contrast with rg results showing tooltip:'Volver' on coach_hub back buttons and the Semantics-wrapped exercise_slot_row.dart:151.

- **[MEDIUM · accessibility]** The hero photo (Image.asset) has no semantic treatment. It is informative content (a photo of the exercise) but exposes no semanticLabel; conversely the gradient errorBuilder fallback is purely decorative and should be hidden from the reader. As-is, screen readers get nothing useful for the image and may stop on the decorative gradient.
  - **Fix:** For the real photo, pass semanticLabel (e.g. the exercise name) to Image.asset. For the gradient/scrim DecoratedBoxes, wrap in ExcludeSemantics or set excludeFromSemantics so the reader skips decorative layers. Since the title text already conveys the exercise name visually and is read, an acceptable alternative is to mark the image decorative (excludeFromSemantics) to avoid redundancy — but make the choice explicit rather than leaving it undefined.
  - **Evidencia:** exercise_detail_screen.dart:267-271 (Image.asset, no semanticLabel/excludeFromSemantics); decorative scrims at lines 273-310.

- **[MEDIUM · accessibility]** The StatsCard renders three StatTiles whose values are all null, displaying '—' (1RM —, SESIONES —, PROGRESO —). A screen reader announces 'dash, 1RM' three times with no indication this means 'no data yet'. Sighted users infer 'not available'; non-sighted users get an ambiguous em-dash. This is a Fase-2 placeholder so the data is intentionally absent, but the empty meaning isn't conveyed.
  - **Fix:** In StatTile, when value == null, add a Semantics label such as 'Sin datos' / 'Aún no disponible' for the '—' glyph (e.g. Semantics(label: 'sin datos', child: Text('—'))), or expose value+label as a combined readable string. Keeps the visual placeholder while making it meaningful to assistive tech.
  - **Evidencia:** exercise_detail_screen.dart:162-168 (all StatTile value:null); widgets/stat_tile.dart:26 (renders value ?? '—' with no semantic substitution).

- **[MEDIUM · microcopy-i18n]** Every user-facing string on this screen is hardcoded Spanish: 'Ejercicio no encontrado', 'No pudimos cargar el ejercicio.', 'Reintentar', 'No hay instrucciones de técnica todavía', 'Aún no entrenaste este ejercicio', the muscle-group/category translation maps, and section headers. The project has an AppL10n system (lib/l10n/) used by profile, reviews, check_in and parts of the workout module, but this screen bypasses it entirely. Note this is a MODULE-WIDE pattern — the sibling routine_detail_screen.dart hardcodes the exact same strings — so it is not a regression introduced here.
  - **Fix:** Migrate these strings to AppL10n (or at minimum to a WorkoutStrings-style shim as already exists in workout_strings.dart) so they are centralized and testable, per design-system.md rule #3 ('Nunca hard-code de strings de UI'). Lowest priority of the i18n options if the team has consciously deferred l10n for this module — but the muscle/category maps in particular are display data that belongs in localization, not inline const maps.
  - **Evidencia:** exercise_detail_screen.dart:17-41 (_muscleGroupEs/_categoryEs maps), :76, :80, :180-181, :474, :535; vs existing AppL10n usage (rg: lib/l10n/app_l10n.dart, profile/check_in screens).

- **[MEDIUM · responsive]** The exercise title (_ExerciseTitle) renders at a fixed fontSize 36 with no maxLines/overflow and no Semantics, overlaid at the bottom of the 320px hero. Long exercise names (Spanish names like 'Press de banca inclinado con mancuernas') plus large dynamic type will wrap into the bottom scrim and can collide with the body content below or overflow the hero region. The badge breadcrumb (fontSize 11, single Text) has the same unbounded behavior.
  - **Fix:** Add maxLines (e.g. 2) + overflow: TextOverflow.ellipsis to _ExerciseTitle, or let it wrap but ensure the hero/scrim height accommodates it. Test with the longest catalogue name at the largest accessibility text scale. Consider clamping textScaler or using a slightly smaller title on overflow.
  - **Evidencia:** exercise_detail_screen.dart:358-375 (_ExerciseTitle: fontSize 36, no maxLines/overflow); positioned in hero at :312-324 inside a fixed height:320 SizedBox (:260).

- **[LOW · design-system]** Two off-scale spacing values. The design system restricts spacing to 8/12/14/18/20 (explicitly NOT 4/16/24). _CompactHeader uses SizedBox(height: 10) between breadcrumb and title (line 222), and the breadcrumb chip uses vertical: 4 padding (line 340). The 8/16 values also appear (line 320 height:8 is fine; fromLTRB top:80 and scrim heights 96/200/320 are layout dimensions, not spacing-scale tokens, so those are acceptable).
  - **Fix:** Change the height:10 to 8 (matching the _HeroStrip equivalent at line 320, which already uses 8 — so this is also an inconsistency between the two header variants) and reconsider the vertical:4 breadcrumb padding (use a scale value or accept it as an intentional chip-density exception). Minor, but the 8-vs-10 mismatch between _CompactHeader and _HeroStrip for the same breadcrumb-to-title gap is a visible rhythm inconsistency.
  - **Evidencia:** exercise_detail_screen.dart:222 (SizedBox height:10 in _CompactHeader) vs :320 (SizedBox height:8 in _HeroStrip) — same semantic gap, different value; :340 (vertical:4 breadcrumb padding). design-system.md:49 ('Sólo estos valores: 8·12·14·18·20. No usar 4/16/24').

- **[LOW · states]** The error state and not-found state are non-symmetric in affordances. _ErrorState offers a 'Reintentar' action, but _NotFoundState ('Ejercicio no encontrado') offers no action at all — only the floating back button (which is off in the top-left corner, not near the message). A user who deep-links to a stale exercise id sees a centered message with no in-context way forward.
  - **Fix:** Consider adding a 'Volver' TextButton to _NotFoundState mirroring _ErrorState's retry, so the recovery action is co-located with the message (recognition over recall). The persistent back button covers control/freedom, so this is a polish-level improvement rather than a functional gap.
  - **Evidencia:** exercise_detail_screen.dart:484-508 (_NotFoundState: message only, no action) vs :510-547 (_ErrorState: message + Reintentar button).

## lib/features/workout/presentation/my_exercises_screen.dart (workout module — trainer's custom exercise library)

_Solid, token-clean screen with good empty-state design and a persistent primary CTA across all states. No HEX/Colors.* literals and no direct PhosphorIcons — full design-system compliance on color and icons. The meaningful gaps are accessibility (small, unlabeled back button and unlabeled icon-only controls), a thin error state with no retry, fully hardcoded UI strings despite a working AppL10n + ARB system that siblings already use, and a header back-affordance pattern that diverges from the detail siblings in the same module (GestureDetector vs IconButton, and no canPop fallback)._

- **[HIGH · accessibility]** The header back control is a bare GestureDetector wrapping a 20px Icon (lines 30-35). Its tap target is roughly the icon size (~20pt), well below the 44pt iOS minimum, and it exposes no Semantics label, so VoiceOver announces nothing actionable for the only way back. Sibling detail screens solve this correctly with IconButton (routine_detail_screen.dart:122 and exercise_detail_screen.dart:111), which gives a 48pt target plus a built-in semantic role.
  - **Fix:** Replace the GestureDetector with IconButton (or wrap in a 44x44 padded, labeled Semantics button) matching the sibling pattern: IconButton(icon: Icon(TreinoIcon.back...), onPressed: () => context.canPop() ? context.pop() : context.go('/profile'), tooltip/Semantics label 'Volver'). This fixes tap target, screen-reader label, and the canPop fallback in one change.
  - **Evidencia:** my_exercises_screen.dart:30-35 (GestureDetector + Icon size:20); contrast with routine_detail_screen.dart:122-125 / exercise_detail_screen.dart:111-114

- **[MEDIUM · accessibility]** The card trailing icons carry meaning but have no Semantics. The accent play icon (line 196) signals 'this exercise has a reference video' and the forward caret (line 198) signals navigability, but neither is labeled, so a screen-reader user only hears the exercise name with no indication a video exists or that the row is tappable beyond the InkWell. The play icon is also only 16px — fine as a passive indicator, but it reads as an actionable play button while not being independently tappable.
  - **Fix:** Wrap the play indicator in Semantics(label: 'Con video de referencia') and exclude the decorative forward caret from semantics (ExcludeSemantics) since the InkWell already conveys tappability. Ensure the whole row's Semantics announces name + muscle group + 'tiene video' as one node.
  - **Evidencia:** my_exercises_screen.dart:193-198 (_ExerciseCard trailing icons, no Semantics)

- **[MEDIUM · states]** The error branch is a single muted line of text ('No pudimos cargar tus ejercicios.') with no retry affordance and no way to recover except leaving the screen (lines 53-59). For a stream-backed list this is a dead-end on transient failures. The loading branch is a bare centered spinner with no context (lines 51-52) — acceptable but minimal.
  - **Fix:** Add a retry action to the error state (a ghost/secondary button that calls ref.invalidate(customExercisesForTrainerStreamProvider(uid))), and consider an icon + slightly stronger heading to match the polish of the empty state. The bottom CTA already persists in error state, which is good — keep that.
  - **Evidencia:** my_exercises_screen.dart:53-59 (error: text only, no retry); 51-52 (bare spinner)

- **[MEDIUM · microcopy-i18n]** Every user-facing string is hardcoded: header 'MIS EJERCICIOS' (line 38), CTA '+ NUEVO EJERCICIO' (line 89), error copy (line 55), and the entire empty state (lines 120, 130). The project ships a real AppL10n system with intl_es_AR.arb / intl_es.arb / intl_en.arb and already-localized exercise keys (e.g. workoutPickerAddButton, coachEditorAddSlot), and sibling workout screens consume it via AppL10n.of(context) (routine_detail_screen.dart:595, post_workout_summary_screen.dart, session_detail_screen.dart). This screen bypasses that system entirely, so it will not translate and drifts from module convention. The design-system doc rule 3 also forbids hardcoded UI strings.
  - **Fix:** Move the five strings into the ARB files and read them via AppL10n.of(context), following the sibling pattern. The voseo copy itself ('Creá ejercicios con el nombre que vos usás...') is good and clear — preserve it as the es_AR value. This also de-risks German/English overflow noted below.
  - **Evidencia:** my_exercises_screen.dart:38, 55, 89, 120, 130; existing system at lib/l10n/app_l10n.dart + intl_es_AR.arb; sibling usage routine_detail_screen.dart:595

- **[LOW · consistency]** Header back affordance diverges from the detail siblings in the same module. routine_detail_screen and exercise_detail_screen use IconButton with a context.canPop() ? pop : go('/workout') fallback; this screen (and custom_exercise_editor_screen) use a bare GestureDetector with an unconditional context.pop() and no fallback. If this route is ever reached without a back-stack entry, pop() is a no-op leaving the user stuck. It's also a visual/interaction inconsistency between list and detail screens.
  - **Fix:** Standardize the trainer-exercise header on the same IconButton + canPop fallback used by the detail siblings. Best handled by extracting a small shared header widget (e.g. TreinoScreenHeader(title, onBack)) and reusing it across my_exercises, custom_exercise_editor, and the detail screens — eliminates the duplicated GestureDetector header and fixes the a11y/tap-target finding everywhere at once.
  - **Evidencia:** my_exercises_screen.dart:30-31 (GestureDetector + bare context.pop()); custom_exercise_editor_screen.dart:83-84 (same pattern); vs routine_detail_screen.dart:122-125 / exercise_detail_screen.dart:111-114

- **[LOW · responsive]** Layout risks under large dynamic type. The header title 'MIS EJERCICIOS' (line 37) sits in a Row with a fixed 14px gap and no Flexible/Expanded, so a longer localized title plus a larger text scale could overflow horizontally. In the card, the exercise name ellipsizes correctly (line 177) but the muscleGroup subtitle (line 181) has no overflow handling, and the empty-state body is fixed at fontSize 13 with no scaling consideration. CTA text uses fixed letterSpacing at small sizes which compounds width under translation.
  - **Fix:** Wrap the header title in Flexible with overflow: ellipsis, add overflow: TextOverflow.ellipsis (maxLines: 1) to muscleGroup, and verify the empty state under textScaleFactor 1.3+ (the centered Column should be fine but confirm no clipping). Prefer the design-system spacing scale; the 6/2px gaps in the empty state and card are below the documented 8/12/14/18/20 scale.
  - **Evidencia:** my_exercises_screen.dart:37-45 (title not Flexible), 181-188 (subtitle no overflow), 128/180 (2px/6px gaps off the 8-20 spacing scale)

## lib/features/workout/presentation/post_workout_summary_screen.dart (workout module — Post-Workout Summary)

_The screen is structurally solid: all four AsyncValue branches are handled (loading/error/not-found/data), colors and the close icon use AppPalette/TreinoIcon correctly, and almost all copy goes through AppL10n. The real issues are: (1) the COMPARTIR action is async and flips the notifier to AsyncLoading but the UI gives zero feedback during the share — no spinner, no disabled state, double-tap risk; (2) a decorative mood-emoji row that looks tappable but does nothing (mismatch between affordance and behavior, plus no Semantics); (3) stat values render raw numbers with no units ("1234.0" for volume, no "min"); (4) several spacing values (4/8/16/24/32/40) and most font sizes are ad-hoc, violating the documented spacing scale (8·12·14·18·20) and there are no shared typography tokens; (5) icon-only close button and the share/done buttons lack Semantics/dynamic-type robustness; (6) English ARB entries for this screen are all empty and the share post text is hardcoded Spanish in the notifier. None are blockers, but the loading-state gap and the fake-interactive emoji row are the ones worth fixing first._

- **[HIGH · states]** The COMPARTIR (share) action is asynchronous — shareWorkout() sets the notifier to AsyncLoading, awaits two Firestore-dependent reads plus a post create — but the screen never watches postWorkoutNotifierProvider, so the UI shows NO feedback while sharing. The OutlinedButton stays fully enabled and unchanged, so the user gets no visibility of system status and can tap it multiple times, creating duplicate posts before the first completes.
  - **Fix:** Watch postWorkoutNotifierProvider in the loaded body; when it's loading, disable the button (onPressed: null) and swap the label for a spinner or 'Compartiendo…' text. This both prevents double-submit (error prevention) and restores visibility of system status. Same applies to the LISTO button only if its nav can be slow, but share is the urgent one.
  - **Evidencia:** Screen build() never reads postWorkoutNotifierProvider; OutlinedButton at lines 198-201 calls onShare unconditionally. Notifier sets state=AsyncLoading() at post_workout_notifier.dart:17.

- **[HIGH · usability]** The 5-emoji mood row (😞😕😐🙂😄) is a const Row of plain Text widgets — purely decorative, with no tap handling and no state. It strongly reads as a 1–5 mood selector (recognition over recall pattern users expect from post-workout screens), so users will tap it expecting to log how the session felt and nothing happens. This is a false affordance / dead interaction.
  - **Fix:** Either make it a real selectable rating (wire each emoji to persist a mood value and show a selected state) or, if mood capture is out of scope for now, remove the row entirely until it's functional. Shipping a control that looks interactive but isn't is worse than omitting it.
  - **Evidencia:** Lines 177-187: const Row with five Text('😞'…) and no GestureDetector/onTap/state.

- **[HIGH · accessibility]** The mood emoji row has no Semantics. Screen readers will announce raw emoji names (e.g. 'disappointed face') in sequence with no grouping or meaning, and since they aren't interactive there's no role. Combined with the false-affordance issue, this is confusing for VoiceOver users. The icon-only close IconButton (top-right) also has no Semantics label/tooltip, so it announces generically.
  - **Fix:** If the emoji row stays as decoration, wrap it in ExcludeSemantics or give the group a single Semantics label. If it becomes interactive, give each option a Semantics label + selected state. Add a tooltip/Semantics label to the close IconButton (e.g. l10n 'Cerrar').
  - **Evidencia:** Emoji Row lines 178-187 (no Semantics); close IconButton lines 99-103 (Icon only, no tooltip/semanticLabel).

- **[MEDIUM · microcopy-i18n]** The shared post's body text is hardcoded Spanish inside the notifier: text: '¡Terminé mi entreno! 💪'. This bypasses AppL10n entirely, so it won't localize and isn't reviewable as copy alongside the other strings. Separately, every English ARB value for this screen (workoutSummaryHeader*, stat labels, buttons, snackbars) is an empty string, so an en-locale user sees blank headers, blank buttons and a blank close-screen — the screen is effectively unusable in English today.
  - **Fix:** Move the share body to an AppL10n key and read it where the post is built (pass it in, or read l10n at the call site). Fill in the intl_en.arb values for the workout summary keys (lines 139-155) — even if English isn't shipping yet, empty strings produce silently broken UI in tests/previews.
  - **Evidencia:** post_workout_notifier.dart:28 hardcoded text; intl_en.arb lines 139-155 all set to "".

- **[MEDIUM · usability]** Stat values display raw numbers with no units. Volume is a double rendered via session.totalVolumeKg.toString() → shows '1234.0' (trailing .0) with no 'kg', and duration via durationMin.toString() shows '45' with no 'min'. The unit only lives in the label ('VOLUMEN', 'DURACIÓN'), but the hero number itself is ambiguous and the '.0' looks unpolished on the most prominent figures of the screen.
  - **Fix:** Format volume without the trailing decimal (or with a 'kg' suffix) and append 'min' to duration — ideally via a small formatter so it's consistent with session_detail_screen, which has the same gap. Avoid toString() on doubles for display.
  - **Evidencia:** Lines 142-147: value: session.totalVolumeKg.toString() (double) and session.durationMin.toString(); StatTile renders the value verbatim (stat_tile.dart:25-32).

- **[MEDIUM · design-system]** Spacing and typography are ad-hoc and violate the documented system. design-system.md states the spacing scale is ONLY 8·12·14·18·20 and explicitly says do NOT use 4/16/24. This screen uses EdgeInsets.all(24), SizedBox heights of 4, 8, 12, 32, 40, and GridView spacing of 16 — most of which are off-scale. Typography is also hand-rolled GoogleFonts.barlowCondensed with literal fontSize 32/18/16/22/10 and per-widget letterSpacing instead of shared text-style tokens, so headings drift between this screen and session_detail_screen (e.g. routineName is 18/w600/muted here vs 28/w800/primary there).
  - **Fix:** Pull spacing from the approved scale (replace 4/16/24/32/40 with on-scale values or a spacing constant set) and introduce shared TextStyle tokens (heading / section-title / hero-number / caption) in the theme so both summary and detail screens reference the same definitions. This is the root cause of the cross-screen heading inconsistency.
  - **Evidencia:** padding EdgeInsets.all(24) line 92; SizedBox 4/8/12/32/40 throughout; GridView spacing 16 lines 136-137; inline GoogleFonts styles lines 112-128, 163-174.

- **[MEDIUM · accessibility]** Large dynamic type / long localized strings have clipping and layout risk. The 2x2 StatTile grid uses a fixed childAspectRatio: 2 with no min height; at large text scale the two-line value+label can overflow the fixed-ratio cell (RenderFlex/clip). The header uses a hard fontSize: 32 with letterSpacing 1.5 and textAlign center — a longer localized header than 'BUEN ENTRENO' (e.g. the English equivalent once filled in) plus a large text scale risks wrapping awkwardly or clipping. Body Text widgets at lines 173/181-185 don't cap maxLines, but the fixed-ratio grid is the concrete risk.
  - **Fix:** Let StatTile cells size to content (e.g. use a wrap/IntrinsicHeight or a min-height instead of a fixed aspect ratio) and verify the grid at textScaleFactor 1.3–2.0. Prefer style.fontSize via the theme so it scales, rather than fixed literals, or test that fixed sizes survive large type.
  - **Evidencia:** GridView childAspectRatio: 2 (line 138) feeding StatTile's 2-line Column (stat_tile.dart:22-43); header fixed fontSize 32 line 114.

- **[LOW · consistency]** Minor cross-screen inconsistencies with the sibling session_detail_screen: this screen places the close affordance top-RIGHT (Align centerRight, TreinoIcon.close → context.go('/workout')), while session_detail_screen places a back affordance top-LEFT (TreinoIcon.back → context.pop fallback go). The summary always force-navigates to '/workout' and never uses canPop/pop, which is reasonable for an end-of-flow screen, but the differing icon/position/behavior between two screens in the same module is a small recognition cost.
  - **Fix:** Intentional difference is fine (summary is a flow terminus, detail is a back-navigable view), but document/standardize the convention so it's a deliberate pattern, not drift. No code change required if the distinction is intended.
  - **Evidencia:** Summary close: lines 97-103 (centerRight, TreinoIcon.close, go('/workout')). Detail back: session_detail_screen.dart lines 81-88 (centerLeft, TreinoIcon.back, canPop?pop:go).

## lib/features/workout/presentation/routine_detail_screen.dart (workout module — RoutineDetailScreen)

_RoutineDetailScreen is a well-structured, design-system-compliant screen: all four AsyncValue branches are handled (loading skeleton, error+retry, not-found, empty), colors go through AppPalette, icons through TreinoIcon, the back button never dead-ends, and ExerciseSlotRow carries a proper Semantics label. The main gaps are accessibility (the icon-only back button has no Semantics label and the loading skeleton announces nothing to screen readers), incomplete localization (most user-facing strings are hardcoded Spanish while the screen already imports AppL10n and sibling screens like routine_editor/post_workout_summary are fully localized), and two system-status consistency bugs in the periodized path where the EJERCICIOS/SETS/MINUTOS stat tiles do not match the week-filtered exercise list shown below them. Typography hardcodes GoogleFonts.barlowCondensed/barlow inline everywhere rather than a shared text-style token, which is a module-wide pattern, not unique to this screen._

- **[HIGH · accessibility]** The floating back button (_BackBar) is an icon-only IconButton with no Semantics label, tooltip, or semanticLabel. VoiceOver announces it generically (the raw glyph / 'button') so a blind user cannot tell it goes back. This is the single most important control for escaping a deep-linked screen, and the screen file itself contains zero Semantics widgets (the only one in the render tree comes from the child ExerciseSlotRow).
  - **Fix:** Wrap the IconButton in Semantics(button: true, label: l10n.commonBack) or pass tooltip/semanticLabel. Use a localized 'Volver' string. Apply the same to any future icon-only control on this screen.
  - **Evidencia:** _BackBar.build, lines 110-130 (IconButton with Icon(TreinoIcon.back) and no Semantics). grep confirms no Semantics/tooltip/semanticLabel anywhere in the file.

- **[MEDIUM · states]** Periodized stat tiles disagree with the filtered exercise list (visibility of system status / accuracy). For numWeeks > 1, EJERCICIOS uses day.slots.length and SETS uses _totalSets(day) — both count ALL slots regardless of week presence — while the exercise list directly below is filtered by isPresentInWeek(viewedWeek). So a week where half the slots are absent shows e.g. '8 EJERCICIOS' over a list of 4. The MINUTOS estimate is also computed over week-filtered slots, so the three tiles are internally inconsistent for the same day.
  - **Fix:** For periodized routines, compute EJERCICIOS and SETS over the same presence-filtered slot set used by _buildExerciseList(viewedWeek) so the header counts match the body. Single-week path (numWeeks == 1) should stay untouched.
  - **Evidencia:** StatTile 'EJERCICIOS' value '${day.slots.length}' (line 290), 'SETS' value '${_totalSets(day)}' (line 294); _totalSets folds over d.slots unfiltered (lines 158-159); exercise list filters by isPresentInWeek (lines 200-205, 327).

- **[MEDIUM · consistency]** MINUTOS stat passes selectedWeekIndex (raw local state) instead of viewedWeek. For single-week routines viewedWeek is forced to 0 (line 268) and drives the whole render, but selectedWeekIndex can hold a stale non-zero value from a previously-viewed periodized routine in the same widget instance. The minutes tile would then estimate against a week index the rest of the screen ignores. It only happens to be correct today because periodized plans keep the two in sync.
  - **Fix:** Pass viewedWeek to _minutesValue (value: _minutesValue(day, viewedWeek)) so every stat and the list derive from one source of truth.
  - **Evidencia:** value: _minutesValue(day, selectedWeekIndex) at line 298 vs viewedWeek = isPeriodized ? selectedWeekIndex : 0 at line 268; exercise list uses viewedWeek (line 327).

- **[MEDIUM · microcopy-i18n]** Most user-facing strings are hardcoded Spanish even though the file already imports AppL10n and uses it for 3 keys (workoutSplitFallback, coachAssignedBy*). Hardcoded: 'Rutina no encontrada', 'Esta rutina no tiene días configurados.', 'No pudimos cargar la rutina.', 'Reintentar', 'Sin ejercicios esta semana', 'No hay ejercicios en este día', 'EJERCICIOS', 'SETS', 'MINUTOS', 'EJERCICIOS' section header, 'SUPERSERIE', 'DÍA n', 'SEM n', 'PLAN COMPLETADO', 'COMPLETADO', 'SEMANA BLOQUEADA', 'DÍA BLOQUEADO', 'EMPEZAR', plus 'ÚLTIMO' in ExerciseSlotRow. Sibling screens routine_editor_screen (36 l10n refs) and post_workout_summary_screen (22) are fully localized, so this screen is below the module's own bar. A reusable 'Reintentar' key already exists (workoutButtonRetry) and 'EMPEZAR' exists (authWelcomeCta) — they are being re-hardcoded.
  - **Fix:** Route all of these through AppL10n. Reuse existing keys where present (workoutButtonRetry for 'Reintentar'); add workout-scoped keys for the rest. Keep the voseo/UPPERCASE style. This also de-risks overflow: localized labels in other languages will be longer than the Spanish chips.
  - **Evidencia:** Hardcoded literals at lines 57, 63, 94, 256, 289, 293, 297, 320, 323, 388, 706, 752, 834, 898, 929, 969, 1064, 1126; ExerciseSlotRow 'ÚLTIMO' at line 289 of exercise_slot_row.dart. Existing keys: intl_es_AR.arb workoutButtonRetry line 149, authWelcomeCta line 7.

- **[MEDIUM · accessibility]** The DÍA and SEM selector chips set their selected label color to palette.bg (the near-black ink #0A0A0A) on a palette.accent (#2CE5A2 mint) fill. Dark text on a saturated mint passes contrast, but the UNSELECTED chips use palette.textMuted (white @55% alpha) on palette.bgCard (#0F1513) at fontSize 11 with letterSpacing — 55%-opacity white on a near-black card at 11px is borderline for WCAG AA small-text (4.5:1). Same muted-on-dark pattern appears in the locked-state CTA ('SEMANA/DÍA BLOQUEADA') and the ÚLTIMO badge.
  - **Fix:** Verify textMuted-on-bgCard contrast at these small sizes; if it falls under 4.5:1, bump unselected chip/label color to a higher-opacity token (textPrimary or a textSecondary at ~70%) for the small uppercase labels, or increase weight/size.
  - **Evidencia:** _DaySelector line 711 and _WeekSelector line 757 (color: textMuted for unselected); locked CTA line 934 (textMuted); _UltimoBadge exercise_slot_row.dart lines 291,300 (textMuted at fontSize 10).

- **[MEDIUM · states]** The periodized CTA bar swallows its loading and error states silently. loading returns a blank SizedBox(height: 56) (no spinner/skeleton, so the primary action area looks empty/frozen during progress fetch) and error returns SizedBox.shrink() — meaning if planProgressProvider fails, the athlete sees NO start button at all and no explanation, with no way to retry. The screen's top-level error branch handles routine load failure well, but this secondary async has no user-facing recovery.
  - **Fix:** Give the loading branch a subtle skeleton/disabled CTA matching the 56px pill so the action area reads as 'loading' not 'missing'. For the error branch, render a recoverable affordance (e.g. a disabled CTA with a small 'No pudimos cargar tu progreso — reintentar' link that invalidates planProgressProvider) instead of vanishing the primary action.
  - **Evidencia:** _PeriodizedCTABar.build, loading: () => const SizedBox(height: 56) line 812; error: (_, __) => const SizedBox.shrink() line 813.

- **[LOW · design-system]** Two raw color literals bypass AppPalette. The back-button chip uses Colors.black.withValues(alpha: 0.35) (line 119) and the hero scrims use Colors.black.withValues(alpha: 0.45) (line 532). These are intentional photo scrims (black is correct for legibility over arbitrary images, and a token may not exist), but they are still Colors.* constants the design-system rule flags. The textPrimary on the back icon is correct only because it's white over a dark scrim.
  - **Fix:** Low priority — scrims over photos are a legitimate exception. If you want strict compliance, add a palette.scrim token (semi-transparent black) and use it in both places so the exception is centralized and documented.
  - **Evidencia:** _BackBar Material color: Colors.black.withValues(alpha: 0.35) line 119; _HeroStrip top scrim Colors.black.withValues(alpha: 0.45) line 532.

- **[LOW · design-system]** Spacing largely respects the 8·12·14·18·20 scale, but a few values fall outside it: hero compact-header top padding 64 (line 478), hero bottom-overlay offsets bottom: 16 (line 563) and the 96/200px scrim heights, plus chip vertical padding of 4 (lines 606, 633) and SizedBox(height: 4) in StatTile. The 6px gaps between chips (lines 484, 570) are also off-scale. Most are minor visual offsets, but vertical: 4 chip padding and the 6px gaps repeat across components.
  - **Fix:** Where practical, snap to the documented scale (use 8 instead of 6 for chip gaps; 8 instead of 4 for chip vertical padding unless it breaks the pill height). Hero scrim heights and the 64px safe-area offset are layout-specific and can stay, but consider deriving the 64 from MediaQuery padding + a token rather than a magic number.
  - **Evidencia:** Top padding 64 line 478; chip padding vertical: 4 lines 606 & 633; SizedBox(height: 6) lines 484, 570, 571; SizedBox(height: 4) StatTile line 33.

- **[LOW · accessibility]** The loading skeleton (_RoutineLoadingSkeleton) is purely visual colored boxes with no Semantics — a screen-reader user gets silence with no 'loading' announcement during the fetch. Similarly the hero Image.asset has no semanticLabel (acceptable as decorative, but it is the only image and conveys the routine identity).
  - **Fix:** Wrap the skeleton root in Semantics(label: l10n.commonLoading, liveRegion: true) or use a single MergeSemantics announcing 'Cargando rutina'. Mark the hero image as decorative explicitly (ExcludeSemantics) since the title text already conveys the routine.
  - **Evidencia:** _RoutineLoadingSkeleton lines 1140-1205 (no Semantics); Image.asset lines 515-519 (no semanticLabel).

- **[LOW · responsive]** Several uppercase labels at fixed small font sizes with letterSpacing risk truncation/clipping under large dynamic type or longer localized strings. The day-chip badge composes '<SPLIT> · DÍA n' at fontSize 11 in a single-line chip; a long split name ('PUSH PULL LEGENDS') plus a localized 'DÍA' could overflow. The hero _DayTitle is fontSize 36 single Text — a long day name will ellipsize/clip with no maxLines/overflow set. Stat tile values and labels are single-line with no overflow handling.
  - **Fix:** Add maxLines + TextOverflow.ellipsis (or FittedBox for the hero title) to _DayTitle, _DayChipBadge, and StatTile so long routine/day names and large-type accessibility settings degrade gracefully instead of clipping or causing RenderFlex overflow in the chip rows.
  - **Evidencia:** _DayTitle Text fontSize 36 line 659-667 (no maxLines/overflow); _DayChipBadge fontSize 11 line 638-647; StatTile value/label lines 25-44 of stat_tile.dart.

## lib/features/workout/presentation/routine_editor_screen.dart (workout module — RoutineEditorScreen)

_The routine editor is functionally rich and architecturally disciplined: it uses AppPalette.of(context) and TreinoIcon.X almost everywhere, designs loading / not-found / disabled / per-week-invalid states explicitly, and handles iOS IME/keyboard edge cases carefully. The real gaps are accessibility (zero Semantics labels across 3228 lines; several sub-44pt icon tap targets; no dynamic-type tolerance) and i18n debt (~46 hardcoded Spanish strings even though the l10n keys it needs already exist and are used for some labels). Two Colors.red literals violate the no-HEX rule when palette.danger already exists. There is also no unsaved-changes guard on back, which can silently discard a fully built multi-week plan. Note: the hardcoded-string and Colors.* patterns also appear in the sibling custom_exercise_editor_screen.dart, so they are module-wide debt, not unique to this screen._

- **[HIGH · accessibility]** No Semantics labels or tooltips anywhere in the screen (0 matches for Semantics/tooltip/semanticLabel across 3228 lines). Every icon-only control is unlabeled for VoiceOver: the back button (line 1199/1248), the day-delete trash (line 1903), the slot overflow ⋮ menu (line 2249), the reorder chevrons in _MoveButtons (line 2124), the set-delete close icon (line 2806), and the +Semana / Quitar / Duplicar icon buttons. A screen-reader user hears nothing actionable for the core verbs of the editor.
  - **Fix:** Wrap each icon-only IconButton/GestureDetector in Semantics(button: true, label: ...) or pass tooltip:/an explicit semanticLabel. Localize those labels via AppL10n (e.g. l10n.commonBack, l10n.coachEditorDeleteDay, l10n.coachEditorSlotMenu). Also add a semantic label to the set-type chip and the week chips so their state (selected, has-warning) is announced.
  - **Evidencia:** Whole file: rg for Semantics/tooltip/semanticLabel returns 0 hits. Icon buttons at lines 1198-1203, 1247-1255, 1902-1908, 2123-2133, 2245-2302, 2802-2813.

- **[HIGH · accessibility]** Several icon tap targets fall below the 44pt minimum. The day-header trash IconButton (line 1902) sets constraints: const BoxConstraints() + padding: EdgeInsets.zero with an 18px icon, collapsing to ~18-24pt. The _MoveButtons reorder chevrons (line 2123) use BoxConstraints() + only 3px horizontal padding with an 18px icon. These are primary destructive/reorder actions sized too small for reliable touch.
  - **Fix:** Give these IconButtons constraints: const BoxConstraints(minWidth: 44, minHeight: 44) (the set-delete button at line 2809 already does minWidth:40/minHeight:44 — match that or 44/44). For the move chevrons, keep them visually compact but expand the hit area via constraints rather than padding:zero.
  - **Evidencia:** Lines 1902-1908 (trash, BoxConstraints()+padding:zero, size 18) and 2123-2133 (_MoveButtons, BoxConstraints()+EdgeInsets.symmetric(horizontal:3), size 18). Contrast with line 2809 set-delete using minWidth:40,minHeight:44.

- **[MEDIUM · design-system]** Two Colors.red literals are used for the 'failure' (Al fallo) set chip background and text (lines 2823 and 2833), violating the no-HEX/no-Colors.* rule. The palette already exposes a danger token (#E53935) used consistently elsewhere on this same screen (week-warning dot line 1702, delete-scope dialog line 753, slot menu danger item line 2388).
  - **Fix:** Replace Colors.red.withAlpha(30) with palette.danger.withAlpha(30) and Colors.red with palette.danger in _chipColor/_chipTextColor so the failure chip stays palette-driven and theme-correct under both Mint Magenta and Electric Violet.
  - **Evidencia:** lib/.../routine_editor_screen.dart:2823 `SetType.failure => Colors.red.withAlpha(30)` and :2833 `SetType.failure => Colors.red`. app_palette.dart:73 `danger: Color(0xFFE53935)`.

- **[MEDIUM · microcopy-i18n]** ~46 user-facing strings are hardcoded in Spanish instead of going through AppL10n, even though the editor already imports and uses AppL10n for many labels (coachEditorAddDay/AddSlot/AddSuperset, titles, submit labels) and the .arb files have a coachEditor* / workoutSelfEditor* section. Hardcoded examples: 'SEMANAS', 'NIVEL', 'DÍAS DEL PLAN', 'Duplicar semana' + body, 'Cancelar'/'Confirmar', the entire delete-scope dialog ('¿Eliminar ejercicio?', 'Solo esta semana', 'Todas las semanas'), the add-scope dialog, 'SUPERSERIE', 'Agregar ejercicio', 'Descanso', '+ Agregar set', 'Cambiar ejercicio'/'Subir'/'Bajar'/'Eliminar', set-type menu items ('Entrada en calor (W)', 'Drop (D)', 'Al fallo (F)'), table headers ('SET'/'KG'/'REPS'/'MÍN'/'MÁX'/'TIEMPO'), the 'Sets incompletos en Sem X · Día Y' hint, hints 'Ej: Fuerza PPL'/'PPL / Full Body', and default 'Día N' names. This blocks the en locale (intl_en.arb already has empty stubs waiting) and creates two sources of truth.
  - **Fix:** Move these strings into intl_es_AR.arb / intl_es.arb / intl_en.arb under the existing coachEditor*/workoutSelfEditor* namespace and read them via AppL10n.of(context). For the parameterized hint use a placeholder string (e.g. workoutEditorInvalidWeekHint(week, day)). Note this is module-wide debt — custom_exercise_editor_screen.dart has the same pattern — so consider a small shared batch.
  - **Evidencia:** rg count ≈46 hardcoded strings in the screen; l10n keys already exist (intl_es_AR.arb:84-90 coachEditor*, :175 workoutSelfEditorTitle) and intl_en.arb:85-91 are empty stubs. Sibling: custom_exercise_editor_screen.dart:106-129 hardcodes labels too.

- **[MEDIUM · usability]** No unsaved-changes guard on back navigation. The back button (lines 1200, 1250) calls context.pop()/context.go() unconditionally. After building a multi-day, multi-week plan, an accidental back tap (or iOS edge-swipe — the branch name fix/workout-swipe-back suggests this is an active concern) silently discards all work with no confirmation. Violates Nielsen 'user control & freedom' / error prevention.
  - **Fix:** Wrap the Scaffold body in a PopScope with canPop computed from a dirty flag (set true on any field/day/slot/week mutation), and on attempted pop show a 'Descartar cambios?' confirmation dialog (reuse the existing AlertDialog styling from _duplicateWeek). Keep create-with-no-edits popping freely.
  - **Evidencia:** rg for PopScope/WillPopScope/onPopInvoked/discard returns 0 hits; back handlers at lines 1200-1202 and 1250-1254 pop directly.

- **[MEDIUM · states]** The disabled save button gives no reason WHY it is disabled. _isValid (lines 525-543) gates on empty name, empty split (trainer), empty days, missing exercise, invalid presence mask, and any invalid week — but the only on-screen feedback is the 'Sets incompletos en Sem X' hint, which by design excludes the SELECTED week (hiddenInvalidWeeks filters out _selectedWeek, line 1230). So if the only problem is the name field empty, or invalid sets on the currently-viewed week, the user sees a greyed-out button with no explanation and must guess. Violates 'visibility of system status'.
  - **Fix:** When _isValid is false, surface a concise reason near/under the submit button (e.g. 'Completá el nombre', 'Hay sets incompletos en esta semana'), or allow the tap and validate-on-submit by scrolling to and highlighting the first offending field. At minimum, render the invalid-sets hint for the selected week too, not only hidden weeks.
  - **Evidencia:** Button onPressed null when !_isValid (line 1474); hint deliberately excludes selected week (lines 1230-1231, 1396-1408). _isValid checks at lines 525-543.

- **[LOW · accessibility]** No tolerance for large dynamic type. Every label uses a fixed fontSize (11-20px) and many controls have fixed heights/widths (week chip vertical:7 with fontSize 13, set chip 44x44 with fontSize 15, SET column SizedBox(width:44), header cells fontSize 12). There is no textScaler handling, so at large iOS accessibility text sizes the set-table header row and chips will clip or the columns will misalign.
  - **Fix:** Audit the set-table row and header for large text scaling: let the SET chip/column grow (use min constraints instead of fixed 44x44 where text lives), and verify the horizontal header row wraps or scrolls rather than overflowing. Consider clamping extreme scale only where layout truly can't flex, and test at the largest Dynamic Type setting.
  - **Evidencia:** rg for textScaler/textScaleFactor returns 0 hits. Fixed sizes at lines 1675 (chip padding), 1688 (fontSize 13), 2583 (SizedBox width:44 SET col), 2715-2716 (44x44 set chip), 2549 (header fontSize 12).

- **[LOW · consistency]** Spacing uses values outside the documented scale. The design system restricts spacing to 8/12/14/18/20 and explicitly forbids 4/16/24. This screen frequently uses SizedBox(height/width: 4) and 6 (e.g. lines 1256, 1292, 1376, 1397, 1440, 1462, 1597, 1632, 1817, 2078, 2336), and EdgeInsets with 16/24 (ListView padding fromLTRB(16,8,16,8) line 1276; dialog padding horizontal:24 lines 739, 811). Minor, but it drifts from the token rhythm the design doc calls non-negotiable.
