  - **Fix:** Normalize gaps to the 8/12/14/18/20 scale where it doesn't break the dense set-table layout; if 4/6 are genuinely needed for the compact table, codify them as an explicit exception in design-system.md rather than scattering raw values.
  - **Evidencia:** design-system.md:49 'Sólo estos valores: 8·12·14·18·20. No usar 4/16/24.' vs SizedBox(4/6) at lines 1256/1292/1376/1397/1440/1597/1632/1817/2078/2336 and EdgeInsets 16/24 at 1276/739/811.

## lib/features/workout/presentation/session_detail_screen.dart (workout module)

_The screen is structurally solid: it uses AppPalette and TreinoIcon correctly (no HEX literals or direct PhosphorIcons), routes all user-facing strings through AppL10n, and covers loading/error/not-found AsyncValue branches with retry. The real gaps are: (1) no empty-state when a session has zero set logs (the body just ends after the stats grid); (2) numeric formatting bugs from rendering raw doubles — volume shows "1250.0" and weight shows "60.0 kg" instead of clean integers, diverging from the sibling routine_detail_screen which has a _formatWeight helper; (3) stat values are unitless (duration "45" with no "min", volume with no "kg") so they rely on recall of the column label; (4) accessibility gaps — the icon-only back button has no Semantics label/tooltip, and several Text widgets bypass typography tokens with bare TextStyle; (5) hardcoded "reps" unit string in _SetRow not routed through AppL10n; (6) ad-hoc spacing values (24, 16, 32, 2, 4) that violate the documented spacing scale (8·12·14·18·20). Most are low/medium severity polish items; the empty state and double-formatting are the highest-value fixes._

- **[HIGH · states]** No empty state for a session with zero set logs. When setLogs is empty, the grouped map is empty, so `...grouped.entries.map(...)` renders nothing — the screen ends abruptly after the stat grid (which shows SETS = 0). The user sees a header and four stats with no explanation of why there are no exercises, which reads as a broken/truncated screen rather than a deliberate empty state.
  - **Fix:** Add an explicit empty branch in _DetailLoaded: if `grouped.isEmpty` (or `setLogs.isEmpty`), render a centered empty-state message (new AppL10n key, e.g. workoutDetailNoSets = 'Esta sesión no tiene sets registrados') instead of an empty Column tail. Keep the header + stats above it for context.
  - **Evidencia:** session_detail_screen.dart:155-160 (`...grouped.entries.map(...)` with no isEmpty guard); confirmed no `isEmpty` check exists anywhere in the file.

- **[MEDIUM · consistency]** Raw double values are rendered without formatting, producing ugly output. `session.totalVolumeKg` is a `double` (default 0.0), so the Volume StatTile shows '1250.0' / '0.0'. In _SetRow, `'${log.weightKg} kg'` (weightKg is double) shows '60.0 kg' instead of '60 kg'. The sibling routine_detail_screen.dart already solves this exact problem with a `_formatWeight` helper that prints '15 kg' for integers and '17.5 kg' for fractions — this screen ignores it, so the same data is formatted inconsistently across the module.
  - **Fix:** Reuse (or extract to a shared util) the `_formatWeight` logic from routine_detail_screen.dart for the set weight, and apply the same integer/fraction formatting to the Volume stat value (e.g. strip the trailing '.0'). Avoid `double.toString()` directly in the UI.
  - **Evidencia:** session_detail_screen.dart:144 (StatTile value: session.totalVolumeKg.toString()), :229 ('${log.weightKg} kg'); session.dart:20 (totalVolumeKg is double); set_log.dart:19 (weightKg is double); routine_detail_screen.dart:449-452 (existing _formatWeight helper).

- **[MEDIUM · microcopy-i18n]** Stat values are unitless. Duration renders just '45', Volume just '1250' — the unit lives only in the column label (DURACIÓN / VOLUMEN), forcing the user to recall what unit each number is (minutes? kg?). This breaks recognition-over-recall and is ambiguous, especially since the two numbers look similar in scale.
  - **Fix:** Either append units to the values ('45 min', '1250 kg') or include the unit in the label ('DURACIÓN (MIN)', 'VOLUMEN (KG)'). Add the unit strings/labels through AppL10n. Pick one approach and apply it consistently with post_workout_summary_screen.dart, which has the identical unitless grid.
  - **Evidencia:** session_detail_screen.dart:134-145 (Duration/Volume StatTiles pass bare numbers); post_workout_summary_screen.dart:140-147 (same pattern, same gap).

- **[MEDIUM · accessibility]** The icon-only back button has no accessible name. It is an IconButton with only an Icon(TreinoIcon.back) and no `tooltip` and no Semantics label, so VoiceOver announces it generically (or by the raw icon) with no indication it is the Back/Volver action. This is the primary navigation affordance on the screen.
  - **Fix:** Add `tooltip: l10n.workoutButtonBackToWorkout` (or a dedicated 'Volver' a11y label key) to the IconButton, or wrap it in Semantics(button: true, label: ...). Apply the same to the close button in the sibling post_workout_summary_screen.dart for consistency.
  - **Evidencia:** session_detail_screen.dart:82-88 (IconButton with icon only, no tooltip/Semantics); same omission in post_workout_summary_screen.dart:98-103.

- **[MEDIUM · microcopy-i18n]** Hardcoded UI string 'reps' in _SetRow bypasses AppL10n. The set row builds `'${log.reps} reps'` with the unit literal inline. This violates the no-hardcoded-strings rule, won't localize, and the design system explicitly requires user-facing strings to go through l10n. (Note the 'kg' literal is a unit symbol so lower priority, but 'reps' is a translatable word.)
  - **Fix:** Route the reps label through AppL10n — e.g. a new key `workoutDetailReps` rendered as '{count} reps' (use an intl plural/placeholder), so it can be translated and pluralized. Keep it consistent with how reps are labeled elsewhere in the module.
  - **Evidencia:** session_detail_screen.dart:224 (`'${log.reps} reps'` hardcoded literal).

- **[LOW · design-system]** Several Text widgets use bare `TextStyle(color: ...)` instead of the typography tokens. _SetRow (set number, reps, kg) and _DetailNotFound/_DetailError titles use plain TextStyle with only a color, skipping the Barlow / Barlow Condensed font + weight + size conventions used everywhere else on the screen. This produces a default-font fallback for the set rows, inconsistent with the headers and StatTile.
  - **Fix:** Use GoogleFonts.barlow(...) (Body font per design-system.md) with explicit weight/size for the set-row texts and the error/not-found titles, matching the typography scale used in _ExerciseBlock and StatTile.
  - **Evidencia:** session_detail_screen.dart:218, 225, 230 (bare TextStyle in _SetRow); :281 and :245-equivalent error/not-found titles rely on default Text style; contrast with :95-122 which use GoogleFonts.barlowCondensed.

- **[LOW · design-system]** Ad-hoc spacing values violate the documented spacing scale. design-system.md states only 8·12·14·18·20 are allowed and explicitly forbids 4/16/24. This screen uses padding EdgeInsets.all(24), SizedBox heights of 24/32/4/2, and GridView mainAxis/crossAxisSpacing of 16 — all off-scale. (The sibling screens share the same drift, so this is a module-wide pattern, not unique to this file.)
  - **Fix:** Align spacing to the approved scale (or, if 24/32/16 are intentionally in use across the app, update design-system.md to reflect reality). At minimum avoid 4 and 2 for the date/time/title gaps, which are below the smallest token (8).
  - **Evidencia:** session_detail_screen.dart:76 (EdgeInsets.all(24)), :89/:102/:112/:123/:152 (SizedBox 8/2/4/24/32), :130-131 (grid spacing 16); design-system.md:49 ('Sólo estos valores: 8·12·14·18·20. No usar 4/16/24').

- **[LOW · states]** Loading state is a bare, context-free spinner. `loading: () => const Center(child: CircularProgressIndicator())` gives no indication of what is loading. Minor for a fast detail fetch, but it offers no visibility-of-system-status text and no skeleton.
  - **Fix:** Optional: add a short label under the spinner (e.g. l10n loading-session key) or a lightweight skeleton of the header+stats layout. Low priority since the fetch is typically quick.
  - **Evidencia:** session_detail_screen.dart:32 (Center > CircularProgressIndicator with no accompanying text).

- **[LOW · accessibility]** The 'PR' badge stub renders on every set row regardless of whether the set was actually a PR (it is a hardcoded stub with no logic per the comment). For screen-reader users it announces 'PR' on every single set, which is misleading until the real PR logic lands. It also adds visual noise that undermines the meaning of a PR badge.
  - **Fix:** Until the real PR detection exists (Etapa 5 per the comment), either hide the badge entirely or gate it behind a real `isPr` flag. If kept, exclude it from semantics (Semantics(excludeSemantics) or ExcludeSemantics) so it isn't read on non-PR sets.
  - **Evidencia:** session_detail_screen.dart:233 (_PrBadgeStub rendered unconditionally per set) and :241-242 (comment: 'Placeholder widget — no params, no logic').

## lib/features/workout/presentation/session_player_screen.dart (workout module — active session player)

_The screen is well-architected and largely design-system compliant: colors via AppPalette, icons via TreinoIcon (no direct PhosphorIcons), and loading/error/empty/success block-gating states are all designed. Two systemic gaps stand out against the codebase's own conventions: (1) ZERO localization — ~25 hardcoded Spanish strings while AppL10n.of(context) is the established pattern used across many sibling widgets; (2) NO Semantics on the many icon-only GestureDetector controls (back, abandon, set-check, info, timer-start), even though the sibling exercise_slot_row.dart already demonstrates the Semantics(button:true,label:...) pattern. Accessibility also suffers from sub-44pt tap targets on critical controls and the future/completed blocks losing their meaning under TalkBack/VoiceOver (state conveyed only via opacity/color). A few smaller usability/state issues round out the list._

- **[HIGH · microcopy-i18n]** Every user-facing string on the screen is hardcoded Spanish — there is no AppL10n usage anywhere in the file. Examples: 'No pudimos iniciar la sesión.' (line 306), 'ABANDONAR' (427), 'Asistencia marcada' / 'Sin gimnasio asignado' (473, 481), 'SESIÓN ACTIVA' (531), 'EJERCICIOS' (343), 'SUPERSERIE'/'COMPLETA'/'VUELTA' (1004,1014), 'Iniciar' (1650), 'objetivo:' (1620), 'TERMINAR SESIÓN' (1696), the whole abandon dialog (1730-1758), 'Al fallo'/'reps' in repsDisplayText (134-146). This directly violates design-system rule §3 ('Nunca hard-code de strings de UI').
  - **Fix:** Route all strings through AppL10n.of(context) like the sibling widgets already do (session_detail_screen.dart, mi_plan_section.dart, historial_section.dart, etc.). The infrastructure exists (lib/l10n/app_l10n.dart + intl_es_AR.arb). This is the single biggest convention gap on the screen and should be a tracked follow-up even if done as one batch.
  - **Evidencia:** AppL10n.of(context) is unused in session_player_screen.dart yet present in ~15 sibling files; rule in docs/design-system.md §3.

- **[HIGH · accessibility]** Icon-only / glyph-only interactive controls have no Semantics labels, so a screen reader announces nothing meaningful. Affected: header back button (GestureDetector + Icon TreinoIcon.back, lines 389-401), the per-set check circle (GestureDetector with empty/filled check icon, 1365-1380), the technique info icon button (1206-1217), the duration 'Iniciar' button and timer icon (1635-1661). The module already has the pattern to follow — exercise_slot_row.dart line 151 wraps its tappable card in Semantics(button:true, label:'Ejercicio ...').
  - **Fix:** Wrap each icon-only control in Semantics(button: true, label: <localized>), e.g. 'Volver', 'Marcar serie ${setNumber} como completada', 'Ver técnica de ${exerciseName}', 'Iniciar temporizador'. Mirror the exercise_slot_row.dart approach.
  - **Evidencia:** No Semantics in this file; sibling exercise_slot_row.dart:151-153 establishes the expected pattern.

- **[HIGH · accessibility]** Several primary controls fall below the 44pt minimum tap target. The header back button is a 36x36 Container (lines 391-393). The per-set check toggle — the single most-tapped action in the whole flow — is a 32x32 box (lines 1368-1369). The info icon's hit area is only ~36pt tall (8px horizontal padding around a 20px icon, no vertical padding, lines 1209-1216). The ABANDONAR button uses tapTargetSize: shrinkWrap with vertical:8 padding around a 12px font (~28pt tall, lines 419-421).
  - **Fix:** Bump the back button and per-set check to at least 44x44 (the _StepperButton in set_entry_sheet.dart and _WeightField at height:44 already model this). Add vertical padding to the info icon hit area. Remove shrinkWrap or raise minimumSize on ABANDONAR so it clears 44pt.
  - **Evidencia:** Lines 391-393 (36x36), 1368-1369 (32x32), 1209-1216, 419-421; contrast with _WeightField height:44 (line 1467) and _StepperButton 44x44 (set_entry_sheet.dart:267-268).

- **[MEDIUM · accessibility]** Block gating state (completed / current / future-locked) is communicated only visually — strikethrough + accent color for done, Opacity(0.4) + lock glyph for future. A screen-reader user gets no announcement that a block is locked/not-yet-available or fully completed, and the dimmed future rows are still in the semantics tree as plain text. The 0.4 opacity also pushes textMuted (already rgba white 0.55) well below WCAG contrast on the dimmed future blocks.
  - **Fix:** Add Semantics with explicit state to the block wrappers: e.g. label 'Ejercicio X, bloqueado hasta completar el anterior' for _FutureBlockPreview, and 'Ejercicio X, completado, N de N series' for _CompletedBlockSummary. Consider ExcludeSemantics on purely decorative future rows or raise the dimmed contrast.
  - **Evidencia:** _FutureBlockPreview Opacity(0.4) lines 832-833; _CompletedBlockSummary strikethrough lines 730-739; future set rows Opacity(0.4) line 1168.

- **[MEDIUM · states]** The error branch swallows the real error and offers no recovery. sessionAsync.when(error: (_, __) => ...) (line 302) discards both error and stack and renders a static 'No pudimos iniciar la sesión.' with no Retry button and no back/exit affordance. If session init fails the user is stranded on a dead-end screen — they cannot retry and the only escape is the OS back gesture, which then triggers the abandon dialog for a session that never started.
  - **Fix:** Add a Retry action (ref.invalidate(sessionNotifierProvider(widget.init))) and an explicit 'Volver' button in the error state. Optionally log error/stack for diagnostics instead of discarding them.
  - **Evidencia:** Lines 302-311 — error: (_, __) with no retry/back, error params ignored.

- **[MEDIUM · usability]** Empty-day edge case silently auto-completes. SessionState.isFullyCompleted uses day.slots.every(...) (session_state.dart:36), which returns true for an empty slot list, so the TERMINAR SESIÓN button would be enabled immediately with an empty exercise list and no content. There is no empty-state copy for a day with zero exercises.
  - **Fix:** Guard the data branch for state.day.slots.isEmpty with a dedicated empty state (message + exit), and/or make isFullyCompleted require slots.isNotEmpty before returning true.
  - **Evidencia:** session_state.dart:36 (.every on possibly-empty list); session_player_screen.dart:354-355 enables button purely on state.isFullyCompleted; _buildExerciseList produces nothing for empty slots.

- **[MEDIUM · navigation]** The back/close affordance is ambiguous. The top-left control uses TreinoIcon.back (a back chevron) but its onTap is _showAbandonConfirm — identical to the ABANDONAR button. Tapping what looks like 'go back' actually prompts to abandon and discard the active session. There is no plain non-destructive 'minimize/leave running' path, and the same destructive action is bound to two different-looking controls (chevron vs. pill), which is inconsistent.
  - **Fix:** Either (a) use a clearly destructive/close glyph (e.g. an X) for the top-left control to signal 'exit session', or (b) if a true back is intended, route it somewhere non-destructive. Avoid mapping a back-chevron to a destructive confirm. Keep one clear primary exit affordance.
  - **Evidencia:** Lines 322-326 onBack: _showAbandonConfirm with TreinoIcon.back (399); duplicated by ABANDONAR OutlinedButton (414-435).

- **[MEDIUM · states]** Visibility-of-system-status gaps on async actions. _finishSession and _onAbandonConfirmed (lines 183-201) await notifier calls then navigate, but there is no in-flight indicator or button-disable during the await — a double tap on TERMINAR SESIÓN could fire finishSession twice before navigation. Similarly the abandon confirm has no pending state.
  - **Fix:** Disable the primary button / show a brief progress state while finishSession/abandonSession are in flight (e.g. a local isFinishing flag gating onPressed), preventing duplicate submissions.
  - **Evidencia:** Lines 192-201 (_finishSession awaits with no UI lock); 351-356 button enabled solely by isFullyCompleted.

- **[LOW · consistency]** Minor spacing/radius token drift vs design-system. Spacing scale is documented as 8·12·14·18·20 only, but the superset card uses fromLTRB(10,10,10,12) and fromLTRB(4,0,4,8) and a SizedBox(width:6) (lines 988, 998, 1002). Border radius tokens are 12/16/20/9999, but set rows use circular(8) (1429, 1585). These are small but they are exactly the kind of ad-hoc value the design system calls out.
  - **Fix:** Snap superset paddings/gaps to the 8/12/14/18/20 scale and set-row radii to the 12 token (or formalize 8 as an inner-radius token in the design system if it is intentional).
  - **Evidencia:** docs/design-system.md spacing scale + radii table; lines 988, 998, 1002, 1429, 1585.

- **[LOW · usability]** _AttendanceCard timestamp is captured once at build with DateTime.now() (lines 453-456) and never updates, and the SESIÓN ACTIVA elapsed timer (_formatMMSS(state.elapsedSeconds), line 554) depends on the provider emitting per-second ticks. If the attendance time is meant to show check-in time it is fine, but as displayed next to a live session it reads as a static clock that drifts from reality, a minor recognition/status inconsistency.
  - **Fix:** Clarify the attendance time as the check-in moment (label it as such / source it from the session start) rather than DateTime.now() at build, so it does not read as a stale live clock.
  - **Evidencia:** Lines 453-456 DateTime.now() at build time in _AttendanceCard.

## lib/features/workout/workout_screen.dart (athlete + trainer workout screen, module: workout)

_The workout screen is well-architected: every async section (MiPlan, MisRutinas, Plantillas, Historial, trainer templates) has loading/empty/error/success branches, retry affordances, AsyncValue.when fully covered, and tokens are used via AppPalette.of(context) almost everywhere. The strongest issues are accessibility (icon-only controls without Semantics labels, sub-44pt tap targets) and i18n debt (a cluster of hardcoded Spanish UI strings in plantillas_section, ver_mas_cell, trainer_templates_section, and the cap message in mis_rutinas_section, despite the project moving toward AppL10n). There is also one clear design-system violation (raw Icons.add in VerMasCell) and minor heading/spacing inconsistencies across sibling sections. No invented problems; the screen is solid overall._

- **[MEDIUM · design-system]** VerMasCell uses the raw Material icon Icons.add instead of the mandated TreinoIcon wrapper. The design system rule #2 is explicit: never use a non-TreinoIcon directly; missing icons must be added to lib/core/widgets/treino_icon.dart with a semantic name. Note this same widget already imports TreinoIcon elsewhere in the module (e.g. mis_rutinas uses TreinoIcon.plus for the equivalent add affordance), so the screen is internally inconsistent about the 'add' glyph.
  - **Fix:** Replace Icons.add with TreinoIcon.plus (already exists, used by MisRutinas CTA) for consistency, or add a semantic TreinoIcon.add entry if a distinct glyph is wanted.
  - **Evidencia:** lib/features/workout/presentation/widgets/ver_mas_cell.dart:35 (Icon(Icons.add, ...))

- **[HIGH · accessibility]** Icon-only controls expose no screen-reader label. The Historial completed indicator (_CompletedIcon) and the TrainerTemplate card's tinted workout-icon square are decorative Icons with no Semantics/label, and more importantly the interactive PopupMenuButton in _UserRoutineCard (the dotsThree overflow) has no tooltip/semanticLabel, so VoiceOver announces it as an unlabeled button. The athlete-side widgets contain zero Semantics wrappers (only exercise_slot_row.dart in the broader feature uses Semantics).
  - **Fix:** Add tooltip/semanticLabel to the overflow PopupMenuButton (e.g. l10n 'Opciones de rutina'); wrap purely decorative icons (_CompletedIcon, the TrainerTemplate icon square) in ExcludeSemantics or give the row a merged Semantics label that includes completion state and the kg/min stats so they read as one coherent item.
  - **Evidencia:** mis_rutinas_section.dart:332 (PopupMenuButton, no tooltip); historial_section.dart:240 (_CompletedIcon, no label); trainer_templates_section.dart:134 (decorative Icon)

- **[MEDIUM · accessibility]** Several tap targets fall below the 44pt minimum. In _TemplateCard (trainer view) the edit and delete IconButtons use constraints: BoxConstraints() (removing the default 48pt min) with only 8px horizontal padding and an 18px icon, yielding a ~34px target. The Plantillas level-filter pills and the VerMasCell rely on padding alone; the pills at vertical:8 + labelMedium text are ~32-34px tall. The Switch row in the trainer view is fine, but the destructive delete button being sub-44 is the riskiest.
  - **Fix:** Restore a 44x44 minimum on the icon buttons (drop the empty BoxConstraints or set minWidth/minHeight: 44), and bump pill vertical padding or wrap in a 44pt-min SizedBox. Destructive actions especially must be comfortably tappable.
  - **Evidencia:** trainer_workout_view.dart:498-499 & 535-536 (constraints: BoxConstraints(), padding horizontal:8); level_filter_pills.dart:60 (vertical:8)

- **[HIGH · microcopy-i18n]** A cluster of user-facing strings is hardcoded in Spanish despite the project shipping AppL10n (intl_es_AR.arb) and most sibling strings already being localized. Hardcoded: Plantillas empty ('No hay plantillas todavía.' / 'No hay plantillas para este nivel.'), Plantillas error ('Hubo un error cargando las plantillas.'); the section title literal 'PLANTILLAS'; VerMasCell 'Ver más'; MiPlan retry button 'Reintentar' (while a workoutButtonRetry key already exists in the ARB); the entire TrainerTemplates section ('PLANTILLAS DE ...', 'Tu entrenador compartió estas plantillas con vos.', fallback 'tu entrenador'); and the cap message in MisRutinas ('Llegaste al máximo de N rutinas activas...') duplicated in two places. This is both an i18n gap and a single-source-of-truth violation (the cap copy is repeated verbatim at lines 78 and 139).
  - **Fix:** Move these to AppL10n keys (reuse workoutButtonRetry for the MiPlan retry; add plantillasEmpty/plantillasEmptyForLevel/plantillasError/verMas/trainerTemplatesTitle/etc). Deduplicate the cap message into one l10n key with a placeholder for the count so it can't drift between the two render sites.
  - **Evidencia:** plantillas_section.dart:37,49-50,125; ver_mas_cell.dart:40; mi_plan_section.dart:131 ('Reintentar' literal vs existing l10n key); trainer_templates_section.dart:56,62,69; mis_rutinas_section.dart:78 & 139 (duplicated literal)

- **[MEDIUM · consistency]** Section headings are styled inconsistently. MiPlan, MisRutinas and Historial render their title via theme.textTheme.titleMedium (localized), but Plantillas and TrainerTemplates hardcode the string AND apply .copyWith(color: palette.textPrimary) on top of titleMedium — implying titleMedium's default color differs, so the five sibling headings on one scrolling screen are not guaranteed to share the same visual weight/color. RoutineCard titles also force titleMedium with an explicit textPrimary override, reinforcing that the base text style color is being patched ad hoc.
  - **Fix:** Define one section-heading helper/style (color + uppercase per the Barlow Condensed heading token) and use it for all five sections so headings are identical without per-call copyWith. Either fix titleMedium's default onSurface color in the theme or stop overriding it locally — pick one.
  - **Evidencia:** Localized+plain: mi_plan_section.dart:38, mis_rutinas_section.dart:48, historial_section.dart:41; hardcoded+copyWith: plantillas_section.dart:37-40, trainer_templates_section.dart:62-65

- **[LOW · states]** Loading affordances are bare spinners with no contextual label. Each section shows a centered CircularProgressIndicator with no accompanying text (and no Semantics value), so a screen-reader user hears nothing and a sighted user gets no 'Cargando tu plan...' context. The states themselves are complete and correct (all four branches present everywhere, retry on every error, distinct empty copy per section) — this is purely about the spinner lacking context, which the audit brief flags explicitly.
  - **Fix:** Add a short label beside/below the spinner (or a Semantics(label: 'Cargando...') wrapper) at least for the first paint, or use a skeleton placeholder consistent with HomeScreen/CoachScreen.
  - **Evidencia:** mi_plan_section.dart:79-92, mis_rutinas_section.dart:168-181, historial_section.dart:90-103, plantillas_section.dart:113-118 (all centered spinner, no text)

- **[LOW · usability]** The Historial empty-state CTA is a dead-end no-op for the athlete. workoutHistorialEmptyCta routes via context.go('/workout') — i.e. it navigates to the screen the user is already on, so tapping it does nothing visible. The intent was presumably to push the user toward starting a workout, but there is no actual start action on this surface for the athlete.
  - **Fix:** Point the empty-state CTA at a real next step (e.g. scroll/navigate to Plantillas or open the routine that lets them start a session), or remove the CTA if no meaningful destination exists yet.
  - **Evidencia:** historial_section.dart:160 (onPressed: () => context.go('/workout'))

- **[LOW · visual-hierarchy]** Spacing rhythm drifts from the documented scale (8/12/14/18/20 only; 4/16/24 forbidden but smaller values used liberally). The athlete sections mix SizedBox heights of 10 (plantillas_section.dart:42,44) and 6 (mi_plan_section.dart:118) and several 2/3/4 px micro-gaps. Some of the 2-4px gaps are legitimate label/subtitle leading, but the 10px and 6px section-internal gaps are off-scale and make inter-section rhythm subtly uneven next to the 12px gaps used elsewhere.
  - **Fix:** Snap the off-scale section gaps (10 -> 8 or 12, 6 -> 8) to the documented scale; keep intentional 2-4px line-leading but document it as a typographic exception rather than spacing.
  - **Evidencia:** plantillas_section.dart:42 & 44 (SizedBox height:10); mi_plan_section.dart:118 (height:6)


---

# Pruebas de usabilidad (journeys)

## Onboarding alumno (Welcome → Register → Profile setup → Home)

_The athlete onboarding is a clean, well-instrumented 4-step flow with solid loading states, an error banner on register, a SnackBar on save failure, and a hard-cancel escape on step 0. But it has high-severity gaps that bite a first-time user: (1) the username (a public @handle) is never checked for uniqueness, so two athletes can claim the same handle and there is no "taken" feedback; (2) Home's first-entry "Empezar Entrenamiento" card is 100% hardcoded fake data ("PUSH · HOY JUEVES · 6 ejercicios") shown to a brand-new athlete who has zero routines, then routes nowhere useful — a classic false-affordance dead-end; (3) email verification is sent silently at signup but never surfaced or enforced, so the user gets a "verify your email" inbox message the app never explained. Medium issues: the gym step is mandatory with only 3 hardcoded gyms (escape exists but is buried as the last card), Android hardware-back is unhandled in the PageView flow, avatar-upload failure is swallowed with no feedback, and terminology drifts (USERNAME label vs "¿cómo te llamás?" title vs displayName). The flow is friction-light on taps but the destination (Home) does not reflect the data the user just entered, breaking the trust the onboarding built._

- **[HIGH · usability]** The username chosen in ProfileSetup step 1 is the public social handle (persisted as displayName, rendered as @handle on public profiles and as 'HOLA, {NAME}!' on Home), yet it is only format-validated (3-20 chars, allowed charset). There is NO uniqueness check at any layer — no available/taken query before or during submit.
  - **Fix:** Add an async availability check (Firestore query on userPublicProfiles handle, or a callable CF) on the step-1 field with debounce, showing inline 'Ese username ya está en uso' before allowing SIGUIENTE. At minimum, validate at submit() and surface a specific failure instead of silently persisting a duplicate. Nielsen: error prevention + match between system and real-world (a handle people expect to be unique).
  - **Dónde:** lib/features/profile_setup/domain/profile_setup_validators.dart:13-22 (validateUsername only checks length + regex). lib/features/profile_setup/application/profile_setup_notifier.dart:148-158 writes 'displayName': draft.username with no availability call. rg for 'uniqu|isUsernameAvailable|checkUsername|taken' across lib returned zero matches in the auth/profile/profile_setup modules.

- **[HIGH · usability]** The destination of the whole journey — Home for a first-time athlete — shows a fully hardcoded fake workout. EmpezarEntrenamientoCard renders static const strings ('HOY · JUEVES', 'PUSH', 'Pecho · Hombros · Tríceps', '6 ejercicios', '~55 min') with no provider/empty-state, regardless of the brand-new athlete having no routine. Its CTA routes to context.go('/workout'), not to an actual session. A user who just spent 4 steps personalizing their profile lands on data that is not theirs and a button that doesn't start the advertised workout.
  - **Fix:** Show a genuine empty/first-run state on Home for athletes with no routine: a 'Creá tu primera rutina' or 'Buscá un entrenador' CTA. If the hardcoded card is a known placeholder, gate it behind real data and render an onboarding-aware empty state otherwise. This is the single biggest credibility break in the journey (Nielsen: match system to real world; visibility of system status).
  - **Dónde:** lib/features/home/widgets/empezar_entrenamiento_card.dart:18-23 (all labels are static const), :97-101 (onPressed: () => context.go('/workout')). HomeScreen._AthleteHome (lib/features/home/home_screen.dart:79-97) renders EmpezarEntrenamientoCard + EstaSemanaCard unconditionally with no first-run/empty branch.

- **[HIGH · states]** Email verification is sent silently at signup but never surfaced in the UI nor enforced. signUpWithEmail calls user.sendEmailVerification(), so the user receives a 'verify your email' message in their inbox that the app never mentioned and never gates on. There is no verification screen, no banner, and no router redirect on emailVerified — creating confusion ('why am I getting this email?') and a dangling, unexplained side effect.
  - **Fix:** Either (a) remove the silent sendEmailVerification if verification isn't part of the product, or (b) make it visible: a post-signup 'Te enviamos un mail para verificar tu cuenta' banner/step, and optionally a soft gate. Decide intentionally — right now the side effect exists with zero UX around it (Nielsen: visibility of system status).
  - **Dónde:** lib/features/auth/data/auth_service.dart:50 (await user.sendEmailVerification() inside signUpWithEmail). router.dart _publicRoutes / authRedirect contain no emailVerified gate. No verification screen exists under lib/features/auth/presentation (only welcome/login/register/forgot_password/splash). register_screen _submit (register_screen.dart:67-79) goes straight to /home → router sends to /profile-setup.

- **[MEDIUM · states]** Avatar upload failure during final submit is silently swallowed: on FirebaseException/any error the code sets avatarUrl = null and proceeds, so the athlete who picked a photo lands on Home with NO avatar and no explanation of why. The user has no idea their photo was dropped.
  - **Fix:** Surface a non-blocking SnackBar after submit when an avatar was provided but upload failed ('No pudimos subir tu foto, podés agregarla luego desde Perfil'). Persist the rest as it does today, but make the partial failure visible (Nielsen: visibility of system status, help users recognize errors).
  - **Dónde:** lib/features/profile_setup/application/profile_setup_notifier.dart:131-140 (try { upload } on FirebaseException { avatarUrl = null } catch (_) { avatarUrl = null }) — no state flag, no SnackBar. The in-code comment even says 'el atleta puede reintentar desde Perfil → Ajustes' but the user is never told.

- **[MEDIUM · navigation]** ProfileSetupFlow uses a PageView with NeverScrollableScrollPhysics and an in-state currentStep, but has no PopScope/WillPopScope. On Android the hardware back button does not map to the flow's 'VOLVER' — back will try to pop the /profile-setup route rather than decrement the step, fighting the visible footer Back affordance and the router redirect that pins the user to /profile-setup until displayName is set.
  - **Fix:** Wrap the flow in PopScope(canPop: currentStep == 0) and route onPopInvoked to notifier.goBack() for steps 1-3, so hardware back mirrors the on-screen VOLVER. On step 0, either trigger _onCancel() or allow pop to /welcome consistently (Nielsen: consistency & user control).
  - **Dónde:** lib/features/profile_setup/presentation/profile_setup_flow.dart — no PopScope anywhere; step navigation is purely via _onBack()/ProfileSetupFooter. rg 'PopScope|WillPopScope' over lib/features/profile_setup returned nothing. Footer hides VOLVER on step 0 (profile_setup_footer.dart:34-60) so hardware-back is the only 'back' a user might reach for there.

- **[MEDIUM · usability]** Step 2 (gym) is a mandatory step (isStep2Valid => gymId != null) but the gym catalog is a hardcoded list of only 3 gyms. The only way to proceed without a listed gym is to scroll past all cards and tap the LAST card 'OTRO GYM / SIN GYM'. A user who doesn't train at one of the 3 gyms must hunt for the escape hatch at the bottom, and the search box ('Buscar gym') implies a real searchable database that doesn't exist.
  - **Fix:** Make this step optional/skippable, or promote the 'SIN GYM' option to the top (or as a persistent 'Skip' in the footer), and either hide the search box until the catalog is real or label it as coming soon. Forcing a required choice from a 3-item hardcoded list adds friction with no data value (Nielsen: flexibility & user control, error prevention).
  - **Dónde:** lib/features/profile_setup/application/profile_setup_providers.dart:7-25 ('Catálogo hardcodeado de gyms' — 3 Gym() entries). lib/features/profile_setup/domain/profile_setup_draft.dart:53 (isStep2Valid => gymId != null). lib/features/profile_setup/presentation/steps/step_2_gym.dart:58-65 ('OTRO GYM / SIN GYM' is the last card after the loop).

- **[MEDIUM · microcopy-i18n]** Terminology and i18n are inconsistent across the journey. The step-1 field is labelled 'USERNAME' with hint '@julieta' while the step title asks '¿CÓMO TE LLAMÁS?' (a name question, not a handle) and the value is stored as displayName and greeted as 'HOLA, {NAME}!' — three different mental models (handle vs name vs display name) for one field. Additionally, register/profile-setup mix localized l10n strings with hardcoded Spanish literals (e.g. SnackBars 'Aceptá los Términos...', dialog buttons 'Volver al setup'/'Cancelar cuenta', step titles, validator messages), and one literal is marked 'i18n: Fase 6 Etapa 3' / 'Tu cuenta fue eliminada'.
  - **Fix:** Pick one term for the handle and use it consistently (title, label, greeting). Route all user-facing strings through AppL10n so the flow is translatable and consistent; the codebase already uses l10n for register/welcome, so the profile_setup literals are a regression (Nielsen: consistency & standards).
  - **Dónde:** step_1_username_avatar.dart:85-87 (label: 'USERNAME', hint: '@julieta') vs profile_setup_flow.dart:34-39 (_titles '¿CÓMO TE LLAMÁS?') vs home_header.dart:29 ('HOLA, ${displayName.toUpperCase()}!'). Hardcoded literals: register_screen.dart:89, profile_setup_flow.dart:98-104, welcome_screen.dart:36. Validators return hardcoded es-AR (profile_setup_validators.dart).

- **[LOW · consistency]** Sign-in/up entry points are inconsistent in their Terms gating and navigation, which a careful first-time user notices. On Welcome, Google/Apple buttons sign in with NO Terms checkbox (and jump straight to /home), while on Register the same providers REQUIRE the Terms checkbox and show a SnackBar if unchecked. Same OAuth account creation, two different consent requirements depending on which screen you tapped from.
  - **Fix:** Apply the Terms requirement uniformly to OAuth sign-up regardless of entry screen, or clarify that Welcome is sign-in-only. Inconsistent consent gating is both a UX and a compliance smell (Nielsen: consistency & standards).
  - **Dónde:** welcome_screen.dart:223-240 (_signInWithGoogle/_signInWithApple: 'No intent gating on Welcome' comment, no Terms check). register_screen.dart:81-124 (both social handlers gate on _termsAccepted with a SnackBar).

- **[LOW · states]** The primary CTA disable logic gives no reason for the disabled state. Across all 4 steps, ProfileSetupFooter's primary button is simply null (greyed) when the step is invalid (state.canGoNext false), with no hint about what's missing — e.g. step 3 needs BOTH an experience card AND a gender chip, but a user who picks only experience sees a dead button and no 'elegí tu género' cue.
  - **Fix:** When a selection step is incomplete, either keep the button enabled and show a brief inline cue on tap ('Elegí tu género para continuar'), or add a subtle helper text. A silently-dead primary button is the most common 'why can't I continue?' confusion point (Nielsen: visibility of system status, help users recognize errors).
  - **Dónde:** profile_setup_flow.dart:205 (onPrimary: state.canGoNext ? _onPrimary : null). profile_setup_draft.dart:56 (isStep3Valid => experienceLevel != null && gender != null). ProfileSetupFooter (profile_setup_footer.dart:19) just disables when onPrimary is null. No per-field validation message is shown on the selection-based steps (2 & 3) — only the text-input steps (1 & 4) have validators.

## Login y recuperar contraseña (Login -> Forgot password -> volver a la app)

_The login -> forgot-password -> back journey is short and mostly coherent: navigation is sound (no dead-ends from the back stack, back always resolves to /login or /welcome), the success state correctly masks userNotFound to prevent account enumeration (REQ-AUTH-011), and loading/error feedback exists on both screens via AuthPillButton spinner + AuthFailureBanner. The biggest gaps are in ERROR RECOVERY and FEEDBACK on the forgot-password screen: a generic catch block silently swallows any non-AuthFailure error (the user taps ENVIAR LINK, the spinner stops, and NOTHING happens — no banner, no success, a true dead-end). Neither the login nor the forgot-password email field validates format client-side (the register screen does), so users only learn an email is malformed after a network round-trip. There is also no resend/cooldown affordance after success. Secondary issues: inconsistent back-button widget between Login (plain IconButton) and ForgotPassword (AuthCircleBackButton), the login password field has no placeholder/hint, mixed pop/go navigation semantics, and error copy that is permanently es-AR-only by ADR._

- **[HIGH · states]** On the forgot-password screen, the submit handler has a generic `catch (_)` branch that only sets `_isLoading = false` and shows NO feedback. If sendPasswordResetEmail throws anything that is not an AuthFailure (e.g. a PlatformException, a TimeoutException, an unexpected Firebase error not mapped by AuthFailure.fromFirebase, or any plugin-level error), the user taps ENVIAR LINK, the spinner spins and then stops, and absolutely nothing changes on screen. No banner, no success text, no navigation. This is a silent dead-end mid-flow: the user has no idea whether the email was sent, failed, or what to do next.
  - **Fix:** In the generic catch, set `_failure = const AuthFailure.unknown('reset-failed')` (or a dedicated 'no pudimos enviar el link' message) so the AuthFailureBanner renders. Never leave a submit path that ends with the spinner stopping and zero visible change. Nielsen #1 (visibility of system status) and #9 (help users recover from errors).
  - **Dónde:** forgot_password_screen.dart lines 74-77: `} catch (_) { if (!mounted) return; setState(() => _isLoading = false); }` — no _failure set, no _sent set. Compare to the AuthFailure branch (lines 60-73) which does surface a banner.

- **[HIGH · usability]** Neither the login email field nor the forgot-password email field runs any client-side format validation, even though the project already has EmailPasswordValidator.validateEmail and uses it on the register screen. Both screens only gate the submit button on `text.trim().isEmpty`. A user who types 'tincho' or 'tincho@' can tap ENTRAR / ENVIAR LINK; the only feedback is a server round-trip that returns invalidEmail (login) or, on forgot-password, the success state will even mask it. This adds friction (a full network trip to learn about a typo) and is inconsistent with register.
  - **Fix:** Attach EmailPasswordValidator.validateEmail to both email fields and validate before submit (login already has a _formKey it can use; forgot-password should add one or do an inline check). Catch malformed emails before the network call to reduce friction and align with the register screen's pattern.
  - **Dónde:** login_screen.dart line 51-52 `_fieldsEmpty` only checks emptiness; AuthInput on login (lines 143-152) passes no `validator`. forgot_password_screen.dart AuthInput (lines 156-166) passes no `validator`. register_screen.dart line 193 DOES pass `validator: EmailPasswordValidator.validateEmail`. The login screen has a Form/_formKey but never calls validate().

- **[MEDIUM · states]** After a successful reset request, the success state shows static text ('Si tu email está registrado, te enviamos un link...') plus a disabled read-only email field and a 'Volver al login' link. There is no way to RESEND the email and no countdown/cooldown messaging. If the email never arrives (spam folder, typo masked by the anti-enumeration success behavior, mail delay), the user's only recourse is to go back to login and start the whole flow again. For a recovery flow this is a common, painful path.
  - **Fix:** Add a 'Reenviar link' affordance (with a short cooldown, e.g. 30-60s, to respect Firebase rate limits and tooManyRequests) and a 'revisá tu carpeta de spam' line. This turns a dead-end into a recoverable state.
  - **Dónde:** forgot_password_screen.dart lines 122-153: success branch renders success text + disabled AuthInput + a single 'Volver al login' TextButton. No resend action, no 'revisá tu carpeta de spam' hint, no timer.

- **[MEDIUM · consistency]** The back control differs between the two steps of the journey. Login uses a bare Material IconButton with TreinoIcon.back (no border, no circle). Forgot-password uses AuthCircleBackButton (outlined circle). Same journey, two visually different back affordances in consecutive screens, which breaks the 'consistency and standards' heuristic and makes the flow feel less polished. The widget comment on AuthCircleBackButton even claims it is the back button 'used on ForgotPassword, Login, Register' — but Login does not actually use it.
  - **Fix:** Use AuthCircleBackButton consistently across Login, ForgotPassword and Register so the back affordance is identical step to step, and fix/realign the widget's doc comment.
  - **Dónde:** login_screen.dart lines 107-116 use `IconButton(icon: Icon(TreinoIcon.back ...))`. forgot_password_screen.dart lines 95-98 use `AuthCircleBackButton(...)`. auth_circle_back_button.dart doc comment lists Login as a user, but it is not imported/used there.

- **[LOW · navigation]** The two ways to leave the forgot-password screen behave differently: the top-left back button uses context.pop() (returning to whatever was below, normally /login since it was pushed) while the success-state 'Volver al login' link uses context.go('/login') (a replace). The end destination is the same in the normal case, but the mixed pop/go semantics within one screen are inconsistent and could diverge if the screen is ever reached via a different entry (e.g. deep link), where pop() would have no /login below it. The pop() path is guarded with a canPop fallback to /login, so it is safe, but the inconsistency is worth aligning.
  - **Fix:** Pick one return semantic for the journey. Since login pushes forgot-password (login_screen.dart line 169 `context.push('/forgot-password')`), both exits should prefer pop() with the same canPop/go fallback, so the back stack stays correct and the two controls behave identically.
  - **Dónde:** forgot_password_screen.dart line 96-97 back button: `context.canPop() ? context.pop() : context.go('/login')`. Lines 143-144 success link: `context.go('/login')` (unconditional replace).

- **[LOW · microcopy-i18n]** All auth error messages shown in this journey (wrong password, invalid email, network error, too many requests, etc.) are permanently hardcoded in es-AR by design (ADR-I18N-002 / kAuthFailureI18nExclusionNote), because AuthFailure lives in the domain layer and cannot receive BuildContext. So even though titles/labels/CTAs are localized via AppL10n, the actual failure feedback the user sees during recovery will never localize. For a journey whose entire value is error recovery, the most important strings are the least localizable.
  - **Fix:** If multi-locale support is on the roadmap, move user-facing messaging out of the domain layer (e.g. map AuthFailure variants to l10n keys at the presentation layer) so recovery copy can localize. If es-AR-only is truly permanent, that is acceptable, but document it as a known limitation for the journey rather than a per-string ADR note.
  - **Dónde:** auth_failure.dart lines 6-10 and 53-78: userMessage getter returns hardcoded Spanish; AuthFailureBanner (auth_failure_banner.dart line 22) renders failure.userMessage directly. Banners appear on both login (login_screen.dart line 181) and forgot-password (forgot_password_screen.dart line 169).

- **[LOW · states]** On the login screen the password AuthInput has no hint/placeholder (the `hint` param is omitted), while the email field shows 'tu@email.com'. A first-time user sees an icon-only field with no label and no placeholder for the password, which is slightly less discoverable than the email field. Labels were intentionally dropped per mockup (icon-only), but the asymmetry (email has a hint, password has none) is a minor clarity gap.
  - **Fix:** Add a password hint (e.g. 'Tu contraseña' / placeholder dots) or a subtle accessible label so the icon-only password field is as discoverable as the email field. Minor, but improves first-time clarity and accessibility (the field currently relies solely on the lock icon to convey purpose).
  - **Dónde:** login_screen.dart email field line 145 `hint: l10n.authLoginEmailHint`; password field lines 155-164 has no `hint:` argument. AuthInput renders nothing when both label and hint are null.

## Crear rutina propia (alumno): Workout -> CREAR RUTINA -> routine editor (SelfCreating) -> guardar

_Traced the full self-create routine journey: entry CTA lives in MisRutinasSection on the Workout tab (lib/features/workout/presentation/widgets/mis_rutinas_section.dart) -> context.push('/workout/my-routine-editor') -> RoutineEditorScreen in SelfCreating mode (lib/features/workout/presentation/routine_editor_screen.dart, a top-level route outside the shell) -> exercise picker bottom sheet (lib/features/coach/presentation/widgets/exercise_picker_sheet.dart) -> _submit() calls RoutineRepository.createUserOwned, shows a SnackBar, and pops back. The flow is functional and reasonably guarded (loading/not-found states, per-week validation, disabled save until valid, cap enforcement, retry on list error). The biggest journey-level gaps are: NO unsaved-changes guard on back (silent data loss is the most severe issue), the save button is disabled with NO explanation of WHY (largest friction/feedback problem for a first-timer), an empty editor opens with zero exercises and a non-obvious next step, and a hard 10-routine cap whose only escape ('archivar') is mislabeled in the UI as 'ELIMINAR'. Findings are ordered by severity._

- **[HIGH · usability]** No unsaved-changes guard anywhere in the editor. The back arrow (routine_editor_screen.dart ~line 1250) just calls context.pop()/context.go('/workout'), and the screen is a top-level route with the native iOS edge-swipe-back gesture enabled. A user who fills in a name, adds several days, exercises and sets, then taps back or swipes (very easy to do accidentally on the swipe-back branch this app is currently on) loses EVERYTHING with zero warning. This is the most damaging step in the journey because it silently discards potentially minutes of work.
  - **Fix:** Wrap the editor Scaffold in a PopScope (canPop computed from a _isDirty flag) and, when dirty, show a 'Descartar cambios?' confirm dialog before popping. Track dirtiness on first edit (name change, day/slot/set mutation). Apply to both the AppBar back button and the gesture/system back.
  - **Dónde:** routine_editor_screen.dart back handlers at lines ~1200 and ~1250 call context.pop()/context.go with no confirmation; grep for PopScope/WillPopScope returns nothing — only canPop() checks exist. The route uses `builder` (CupertinoPageRoute), so edge-swipe-back is active.

- **[HIGH · states]** The primary action (CREAR RUTINA / save) is disabled until the form is valid, but there is NO inline feedback telling the user WHAT is missing while the editor is in its NORMAL state. Validation requires: non-empty name AND every day has >=1 exercise AND every visible set has a valid reps/duration value. A first-timer who opens the empty editor sees a greyed-out button with no hint about which of those three conditions is unmet. The only validation affordance (the red 'Sets incompletos en Sem X' hint and per-week warning dot) ONLY fires for non-selected weeks in a multi-week plan — single-week self-routines (the common case) get nothing.
  - **Fix:** Either keep the button enabled and surface a specific SnackBar on tap ('Poné un nombre' / 'Agregá al menos un ejercicio al Día N' / 'Completá las reps del set X'), or render a persistent inline helper under the save button listing the first unmet requirement. This is Nielsen #1 (visibility of system status) and #9 (help users recognize errors).
  - **Dónde:** routine_editor_screen.dart _isValid (lines 525-543) gates the ElevatedButton onPressed (line 1473-1474) with no accompanying message; the invalid-week hint (lines 1396-1408) is gated on `hiddenInvalidWeeks.isNotEmpty`, i.e. only weeks OTHER than the selected one, so a 1-week plan never shows it.

- **[MEDIUM · usability]** The editor opens cold with one collapsible 'Día 1' card containing only a '+ Agregar ejercicio' link and no exercises, no description of what to do, and the SEMANAS / DÍAS DEL PLAN machinery (week chips, 'Duplicar semana', 'Quitar última') all visible at once. A first-time athlete has no guidance that the minimum viable routine is name + 1 exercise + reps. There is no empty-state coaching inside the editor itself, and the periodization controls add cognitive load the casual self-author rarely needs.
  - **Fix:** For SelfCreating mode with a fresh routine, consider hiding the SEMANAS block until the user opts into periodization (or collapsing it behind an 'Avanzado' toggle), and add a one-line helper in the first empty day ('Agregá tu primer ejercicio para empezar'). Reduces cold-start cognitive load for the athlete persona.
  - **Dónde:** routine_editor_screen.dart initial state: _days = [_EditableDay(dayNumber:1, name:'Día 1')] (line 350), _numWeeks=1; the body renders the SEMANAS section + week tab bar even for a brand-new single-week routine (lines 1375-1408). No onboarding/empty copy in the day card beyond the 'coachEditorAddSlot' link.

- **[MEDIUM · microcopy-i18n]** Terminology mismatch for the cap-escape action. The 10-routine cap message tells the user to 'Archivá una para crear otra', but the actual overflow action in the routine card menu is labeled 'ELIMINAR' and the confirm dialog is titled 'Eliminar rutina' with delete language — yet it calls repository.archive(), not a hard delete. So the user is told to 'archive', shown only a 'delete' control, and the system actually archives. Three different words for one operation break the cap-recovery path conceptually.
  - **Fix:** Pick ONE verb. Since the operation is non-destructive (archive), either rename the menu item + dialog to 'Archivar'/'Archivar rutina' to match the cap guidance, or change the cap copy to say 'Eliminá una'. Keeping 'archive' semantics with 'delete' wording also risks the user expecting permanent removal.
  - **Dónde:** mis_rutinas_section.dart: cap copy says 'Archivá una' (lines 78-79, 139); overflow item uses l10n.workoutMisRutinasOverflowArchive which resolves to 'ELIMINAR' (app_l10n_es.dart line 548); _confirmArchive titles 'Eliminar rutina' but calls ref.read(routineRepositoryProvider).archive(routine.id) (lines 251-273).

- **[MEDIUM · states]** On a successful save the editor shows a SnackBar ('Rutina creada') and immediately context.pop()s back to the Workout tab. Because the SnackBar is shown on the editor's ScaffoldMessenger right before the pop, the confirmation can be torn down with the editor and is easy to miss; meanwhile the new routine appears in the MIS RUTINAS list with no highlight/scroll-to, so the user gets little confirmation that what they just built actually landed where they expect.
  - **Fix:** Show the success SnackBar on the destination (root) ScaffoldMessenger after popping, or briefly highlight/scroll to the newly created card in MIS RUTINAS so the success is anchored to the result the user can see.
  - **Dónde:** routine_editor_screen.dart SelfCreating create branch (lines 1128-1133): showSnackBar then context.pop() on the same frame. The destination list (MisRutinasSection) re-renders from userCreatedRoutinesProvider with no new-item affordance.

- **[MEDIUM · usability]** Adding an exercise is a multi-step modal chain. Tapping '+ Agregar ejercicio' opens the exercise-picker bottom sheet (tap exercise(s) -> tap sticky 'Agregar (N)' CTA), and for multi-week plans on week >=2 a SECOND dialog ('En que semanas agregar?') appears before the slot is added. New slots are then seeded with an empty set (blank reps/kg), so the exercise still does not satisfy validation — combined with finding #2, the path from 'add exercise' to a SAVEABLE routine is long and the missing piece (reps) is never signposted.
  - **Fix:** Consider pre-filling a sensible default set (placeholder reps) when a slot is created, and pair with finding #2 so the user is told reps are the missing requirement. The scope dialog is correctly skipped for single-week plans, which is good.
  - **Dónde:** routine_editor_screen.dart _pickExercisesForDay (lines 866-894) -> showExercisePicker then _promptAddScope; exercise_picker_sheet.dart sticky add bar only renders when _selected.isNotEmpty (lines 303-308). New slots seeded with restSeconds:0 and a single empty _EditableSet that blocks save.

- **[LOW · consistency]** Error-copy specificity is inconsistent across editor modes. SelfCreating distinguishes permission-denied vs generic error (good), while trainer modes collapse everything to coachCreatePlanError. Within the self-create journey the messaging is fine; the inconsistency is cross-mode and only matters if these strings are meant to feel uniform across the shared editor.
  - **Fix:** Low priority — optionally give trainer modes the same permission-vs-generic split for consistency, or document that self-create intentionally has richer error handling.
  - **Dónde:** routine_editor_screen.dart _submit catch block (lines 1155-1168): SelfCreating branch checks e.toString().contains('permission-denied') and picks workoutSelfEditorPermissionDenied vs workoutSelfEditorError; trainer branches always use coachCreatePlanError.

- **[LOW · usability]** Dead/misleading callback in the empty state. _SectionEmptyState receives an onCta callback (wired to context.push('/workout/my-routine-editor')) but its build() renders only a Text widget — the callback is never invoked. The empty-state copy ('Tocá CREAR RUTINA para armar la primera') relies on the header CTA instead, which IS present in the empty state, so the journey still works; but the unused onCta is dead code implying a tappable empty-state CTA that doesn't exist.
  - **Fix:** Either make the empty state's CTA tappable (a button using onCta) for a clearer call to action right where the user is looking, or remove the unused onCta param to avoid the misleading contract.
  - **Dónde:** mis_rutinas_section.dart: _SectionEmptyState constructor takes onCta (line 221) but build() returns a Padding>Text only (lines 226-236); the empty branch passes onCta: () => context.push('/workout/my-routine-editor') (lines 96-98).

- **[LOW · navigation]** The not-found recovery state is a near dead-end. If the routine being EDITED was deleted before opening, the editor shows 'Esta rutina ya no existe. Volve y actualiza la lista.' with only a back arrow, and asks the user to manually refresh; the list provider is not invalidated automatically on return. Only affects the edit sub-path, not first-time create.
  - **Fix:** On returning from the not-found state, invalidate userCreatedRoutinesProvider so the stale card disappears without a manual pull-to-refresh, and soften the copy.
  - **Dónde:** routine_editor_screen.dart _loadNotFound branch (lines 1188-1219) renders back arrow + workoutSelfEditorNotFound text; no automatic ref.invalidate(userCreatedRoutinesProvider) on pop.

## Ejecutar sesión de entrenamiento (Routine detail → session player → loguear sets → finish → post-workout summary)

_The workout-execution journey is well-architected for the happy path: block-gating focuses the user on one exercise at a time, the player auto-advances, abandon is confirmed and progress saved, and the routine-detail screen never dead-ends (persistent back button in every state). But the flow has serious gaps in the FAILURE half of the experience. Set logging and editing are fire-and-forget with zero feedback: if the Firestore write fails mid-session (network/permission), the check icon silently never fills and the user has no idea their set was lost. `_finishSession` has no try/catch, so a failed finish-write strands the user on the player with a dead timer and no message. The post-workout summary renders BLANK text for English users (all English ARB strings are empty) and shows two permanent dead stubs (PRs "Próximamente", non-interactive mood emojis) that imply functionality that does not exist. There is also no rest timer between sets — a core gym-flow expectation. Terminology and button placement are otherwise consistent across steps._

- **[HIGH · states]** Logging a set is fire-and-forget with NO failure feedback. In the session player, tapping the check icon calls `_logSet` → `SessionNotifier.logSet()`, which awaits `repo.addSetLog` inside a try/finally. The `finally` only resets the `_isLoggingSet` guard; if the Firestore write throws (network drop, permission, offline), the exception is swallowed — no snackbar, no retry, no error state. The check icon simply never fills and the set count never increments. The user believes they logged the set when they did not, and mid-workout they cannot tell logging is broken. `updateSet` (editing a done set's weight) has the same silent-failure problem.
  - **Fix:** On `addSetLog`/`updateSetLog` failure, surface an inline error: revert the optimistic UI, show a snackbar ('No pudimos guardar la serie, reintentá') with a retry action, and keep the row in its un-logged interactive state. Consider an optimistic-then-reconcile pattern so the tap feels instant but failures are visible.
  - **Dónde:** lib/features/workout/application/session_notifier.dart: `logSet` (lines 174-218) wraps `await repo.addSetLog` in try/finally with no catch and no error surfaced to state; `updateSet` (223-244) also has no error handling. Player `_logSet`/`_updateSet` (session_player_screen.dart 204-222) do not await or catch. No `ScaffoldMessenger`/snackbar anywhere in session_player_screen.dart.

- **[HIGH · states]** `_finishSession` has no error handling and can strand the user. It sets `_isFinalizing = true`, calls `notifier.finishSession()` (which internally calls `_finalize()` — cancelling the session timer — BEFORE awaiting the Firestore `repo.finish` write), then navigates to the summary only on success. If `repo.finish` throws, navigation never happens: the user is left on the player with a frozen timer, the session marked finalized internally, `canPop` now true, and no error message. The session is effectively half-finished with no recovery path from this screen.
  - **Fix:** Wrap `finishSession` in try/catch in the player. On failure: show a snackbar with retry, do NOT leave `_isFinalizing` stranding the user, and ensure the timer/finalized state can be recovered or the retry re-attempts the write. The same applies to `abandonSession` (also no catch — line 183-190).
  - **Dónde:** lib/features/workout/presentation/session_player_screen.dart `_finishSession` (192-201) has no try/catch; navigation is gated behind the await completing. lib/features/workout/application/session_notifier.dart `finishSession` (269-302) calls `_finalize()` (cancels timer) at line 278, then awaits `repo.finish` at 283 — a throw leaves `_finalized=true` and timer dead but session not navigated away.

- **[HIGH · microcopy-i18n]** The post-workout summary screen renders BLANK text for English-locale users. Every English ARB key the summary depends on is an empty string: the header ('BUEN ENTRENO' / 'SESIÓN INTERRUMPIDA'), routine-stat labels, the PRs section, the LISTO/COMPARTIR buttons, and the share snackbars. An English user finishes a workout and lands on a summary with no visible header, blank stat labels, and blank buttons — a broken final impression at the journey's emotional peak.
  - **Fix:** Fill in all English ARB strings for the workout-summary keys (and audit the rest of the workout namespace). Add a CI/l10n lint that fails the build on empty ARB values so this cannot ship again.
  - **Dónde:** lib/l10n/intl_en.arb lines 139-155: workoutSummaryHeaderCompleted, workoutSummaryHeaderAbandoned, workoutStatPrsTodayStub, workoutPrsPlaceholder, workoutButtonDone, workoutButtonShare, workoutSnackShareSuccess, workoutSnackShareError are all "". post_workout_summary_screen.dart reads all of these via AppL10n.of(context).

- **[MEDIUM · usability]** The post-workout summary shows two prominent dead/stub UI elements that imply functionality that does not exist. (1) The 'PRs HOY' stat tile shows '—' and a full PRs section reads 'Próximamente' (Coming soon) — a permanent placeholder occupying premium space on the celebration screen. (2) A 5-emoji mood row is rendered but is purely visual: the emojis are plain `Text` widgets with no tap handlers, so a user who taps to rate their session gets no response. This is a Nielsen 'match between system and real world' + 'visibility of system status' violation — affordances that look interactive but do nothing.
  - **Fix:** Either wire up the mood row (persist RPE/mood to the session) and the PRs computation, or remove these elements until they work. Shipping non-functional affordances on the summary erodes trust. At minimum, make the mood emojis non-tappable in appearance (reduce them to a static illustration) so users don't expect interaction.
  - **Dónde:** lib/features/workout/presentation/post_workout_summary_screen.dart: PRs section (160-174) renders `workoutPrsPlaceholder`; mood row (177-187) is `const Row` of bare `Text('😞')` … `Text('😄')` with zero gesture handlers.

- **[MEDIUM · usability]** No rest timer between sets. After logging a set, the player auto-advances to the next set but provides no rest countdown — a core expectation of a guided gym session (the routine model even stores `restSeconds`, which is used for the routine-detail minute estimate but never surfaced during execution). Only DURATION-type sets get a countdown (`_DurationSetRow`). For standard reps sets, the user must time rest themselves with an external timer, breaking the in-app flow.
  - **Fix:** After a reps set is checked, surface an auto-starting rest countdown using the slot's `restSeconds` (skippable, with the haptic buzz already used by `_DurationSetRow`). This keeps the user in-app for the whole session and uses data already authored in the routine.
  - **Dónde:** session_player_screen.dart: `_RepsSetRow` logs and immediately moves on; no rest timer widget exists for reps sets. `restSeconds` is read only in routine_detail_screen.dart `_minutesValue` (lines 165-179). `_DurationSetRow` (1515+) is the only timer in the player.

- **[MEDIUM · states]** Empty-day edge case enables TERMINAR instantly. `SessionState.isFullyCompleted` uses `day.slots.every(...)`, which returns `true` for an empty slot list. If a session is ever started for a day with zero (present) slots, the TERMINAR button is enabled immediately and 'finishes' a workout with no exercises. The routine-detail entry guards against empty days, and presence-filtering reduces the risk, but the player itself has no floor — a periodized week where all slots are absent, or a data inconsistency, would produce a zero-work 'completed' session that still logs `routine_finished` analytics and writes a finished session doc.
  - **Fix:** Guard `isFullyCompleted` (or the start path) so a session with zero present slots cannot be created/finished — e.g. block session creation with an explainer when `presentSlots.isEmpty`, mirroring the routine-detail 'Sin ejercicios esta semana' message.
  - **Dónde:** lib/features/workout/application/session_state.dart `isFullyCompleted` (36-39) — `.every` on empty list is vacuously true. session_notifier.dart `_buildFresh` builds `presentSlots` which can be empty (89-93). Player gates TERMINAR on `state.isFullyCompleted` (session_player_screen.dart 354-356).

- **[MEDIUM · states]** No success confirmation when finishing, and the abandon flow's destination makes the abandoned-summary unreachable. On TERMINAR the user is navigated straight to the summary with no transient 'saved' confirmation; the 'BUEN ENTRENO' header is the only success signal. More importantly, ABANDONAR → confirm navigates to `/workout` (NOT the summary), so an abandoned session's partial data and the 'SESIÓN INTERRUMPIDA' summary header are never shown to the user who abandoned — the summary's abandoned-state branch is only reachable by deep link, making that whole code path effectively dead in the normal flow and denying the user a record of their partial work.
  - **Fix:** After abandon, route to the post-workout summary (same as finish) so the user sees the 'SESIÓN INTERRUMPIDA' recap with their partial volume/sets — this gives closure and makes the existing abandoned-state UI reachable. Add a brief success snackbar/animation on finish.
  - **Dónde:** session_player_screen.dart: `_onAbandonConfirmed` (183-190) navigates to `/workout`; `_finishSession` (192-201) navigates to the summary. post_workout_summary_screen.dart header branch (107-118) renders `workoutSummaryHeaderAbandoned` only when `wasFullyCompleted == false`, but no in-flow navigation reaches it with an abandoned session.

- **[LOW · consistency]** Back-affordance and exit behavior is inconsistent across the journey's steps. Routine detail uses a circular translucent back chip that pops the navigator (or falls back to `/workout`). The player's back chip and ABANDONAR button both trigger the SAME abandon-confirm dialog (good intent), but visually the player back arrow looks like a normal 'go back' control while it actually means 'abandon workout' — a back-affordance that destroys progress is a surprising mapping. The summary uses yet a third pattern: a close (X) icon top-right plus a LISTO button, both `context.go('/workout')`.
  - **Fix:** Differentiate the player's exit affordance from a normal back arrow (e.g. use a distinct 'close/X' icon, matching the destructive 'abandon' semantics) so users don't expect a non-destructive back. Keep the confirm dialog. This aligns the player with the summary's X pattern and removes the 'back = lose progress' surprise.
  - **Dónde:** routine_detail_screen.dart `_BackBar` (110-130) pops; session_player_screen.dart `_SessionHeader` onBack==onAbandon (322-327, 389-401) opens abandon dialog; post_workout_summary_screen.dart close icon (96-103) and LISTO button (191-194).

- **[LOW · usability]** Reps are not editable during logging — only weight is. For a reps-range prescription the player logs `repsMax` (top of range) automatically and the expanded panel shows reps as a fixed, non-editable label; only the weight field is editable. A user who actually did fewer reps than the top of the range (very common: 'aim 8-12', got 9) cannot record their true reps, so logged volume and history are systematically inaccurate. This undermines the value of the whole logging flow.
  - **Fix:** Allow editing actual reps performed (default to the planned value) at least for range and failure sets, so logged volume reflects reality. This is foundational to the app's training-history value proposition.
  - **Dónde:** session_player_screen.dart comment 'Fixed reps display — NOT editable' (1391) and `_RepsSetRow` expanded panel (1386-1423) renders reps as a static Container; `plannedRepsForSpec` always returns the planned/repsMax value (124-130).

## Historial de entrenamiento (Workout → historial → session detail)

_End-to-end the journey is short and technically solid: every async step has loading/error/empty states with retry, the entry filter is consistent across the codebase, and Rioplatense terminology is coherent. The friction is concentrated at the two ends. The entry point is buried: Historial is the 5th and last block of a long scrolling Workout list with no dedicated tab or "ver todo" full-history screen, so a first-time user may never discover it, and a power user with many sessions can only ever paginate inline 5-at-a-time. The exit/detail screen is where most heuristic violations cluster: a custom in-body back button instead of a real AppBar (inconsistent with the native slide+swipe pattern the rest of the app standardizes on, and the very thing the current branch is fixing), volume rendered as a raw double ("1234.0 kg"), a permanently-visible "PR" badge stub on every set that signals a personal record that isn't real, and a "PRS HOY" stat hardwired to "—". No screen titles its content as "Historial" once you leave the list, and the empty-state CTA is a no-op self-navigation. Severity is mostly medium: nothing dead-ends the user, but the detail screen actively shows misleading data (fake PR badges, float volume) and the journey lacks a true history destination._

- **[HIGH · navigation]** The history entry point is buried as the last of five stacked sections in a single scrolling Workout list (Mi plan → Trainer templates → Mis rutinas → Plantillas → Historial). There is no dedicated Historial tab, no anchor, and no full-history screen — the only way to reach past sessions is to scroll past everything else on the Workout tab.
  - **Fix:** Give history a first-class destination: either a 'Ver todo el historial' link in the section header routing to a dedicated full-list screen, or surface recent activity higher (e.g. on Home). At minimum add a 'Ver todo' affordance so the inline 5-item cap isn't the only access path.
  - **Dónde:** lib/features/workout/workout_screen.dart:51-70 places HistorialSection() dead last in the ListView. The router (lib/app/router.dart:255) only exposes /workout/historial/:sessionId (a single-session detail) — there is no list route like /workout/historial.

- **[MEDIUM · usability]** The list caps at 5 cards and only expands inline via 'Ver más (N)'. For an athlete with dozens/hundreds of finished sessions, the entire history is rendered into one un-paginated Column on tap of 'Ver más', and there is no search, date filter, or grouping. This scales badly and makes finding a specific past session tedious.
  - **Fix:** Move the full list to a dedicated lazy (builder-based) screen with date grouping (this week / this month / older) and ideally a routine/date filter. Keep the 5-item preview on the Workout tab as a teaser linking to it.
  - **Dónde:** lib/features/workout/presentation/widgets/historial_section.dart:58-78 — const limit = 5; overflow expands to the full completed list with a plain `for` loop (no ListView.builder, no pagination). _expanded just toggles take(5) vs all.

- **[MEDIUM · consistency]** The session detail screen uses a custom in-body back IconButton at the top of a SingleChildScrollView instead of a standard AppBar with a leading back button. This breaks the navigation pattern the rest of the app standardizes on (native CupertinoPageRoute slide + edge swipe-back) and is the exact class of issue the current branch fix/workout-swipe-back is addressing.
  - **Fix:** Replace the in-body back button with a transparent AppBar (automaticallyImplyLeading or a back IconButton in the leading slot) so back placement, hit target, and the swipe-back gesture match every other sub-route. Add a title ('Historial' or the routine name) so the screen self-identifies.
  - **Dónde:** lib/features/workout/presentation/session_detail_screen.dart:28-52 Scaffold has body only, no appBar. The back affordance is a manual Align→IconButton at lines 81-88. Router comments (lib/app/router.dart:212-213, 311-314) describe the intended native slide + edge swipe-back gesture for sub-routes; a custom in-body button is the inconsistent outlier.

- **[MEDIUM · states]** Every set row in the detail screen renders a permanent 'PR' badge stub, signaling a personal record that was never computed. A user reading their history will believe every single set is a PR, which is misleading feedback. The 'PRS HOY' stat tile is likewise hardwired to '—'.
  - **Fix:** Hide the PR badge and the PRS HOY stat entirely until real PR detection exists, or compute actual PRs from setLogs. Showing a non-functional 'PR' on every row erodes trust in the data — worse than omitting it.
  - **Dónde:** lib/features/workout/presentation/session_detail_screen.dart:233 (_SetRow always renders const _PrBadgeStub()), :243-267 (_PrBadgeStub is a static placeholder showing the literal 'PR' label, comment says 'Placeholder widget — no params, no logic. Grep-friendly name for Etapa 5'). Stat tile :146-149 uses workoutStatPrsTodayStub which is '—' (lib/l10n/app_l10n_es.dart:407).

- **[MEDIUM · microcopy-i18n]** Total volume is a double and is rendered without formatting, so it displays with a trailing '.0' (e.g. '1234.0 kg' in the card and '1234.0' in the detail stat). Reps/weight rows likewise interpolate raw numeric fields. This looks unpolished and inconsistent with the rounded 'min' duration shown beside it.
  - **Fix:** Format volume/weight for display (round to int when whole, e.g. via a shared numeric formatter, and consider thousands separators). Centralize it so the card and detail render identically.
  - **Dónde:** Session.totalVolumeKg is `@Default(0.0) double` (lib/features/workout/domain/session.dart:20). Card: lib/features/workout/presentation/widgets/historial_section.dart:213 interpolates `${session.totalVolumeKg}` directly. Detail: session_detail_screen.dart:144 uses `session.totalVolumeKg.toString()`; set row :229 shows `${log.weightKg} kg`.

- **[MEDIUM · states]** The detail header shows raw date + start time + routine name but no closing/finish time and no clear 'completed' confirmation. The list card communicates completion via a green check icon, but on the detail screen that signal is dropped, so the per-session 'this was finished successfully' feedback is weaker than on the card you came from.
  - **Fix:** Surface a completion indicator and the finish time (or 'completado') in the detail header so the success state is reinforced, matching the green-check semantics of the card.
  - **Dónde:** session_detail_screen.dart:92-122 renders formatSessionDate(startedAt) + _formatTime(startedAt) + routineName only; session.finishedAt and the completed status are never surfaced. The list card carries _CompletedIcon (historial_section.dart:188, :234-242) but it is not reflected in the detail.

- **[LOW · usability]** The empty-state CTA 'Empezar entrenamiento' navigates with context.go('/workout') — i.e. back to the very screen the user is already on. It does not start a workout or scroll to Mi plan, so tapping it appears to do nothing (a no-op self-navigation), which reads as a dead/broken action to a first-time user.
  - **Fix:** Point the CTA at the real start-workout entry (Mi plan / session player launch) or scroll the list to the Mi plan section, so the action visibly advances the user toward their first workout.
  - **Dónde:** lib/features/workout/presentation/widgets/historial_section.dart:159-164 — onPressed: () => context.go('/workout'); the user is already on /workout.

- **[LOW · microcopy-i18n]** Session dates omit the year. 'Mié 27 nov' is fine for recent sessions but becomes ambiguous in a long history spanning multiple years — a user can't tell a session from this November versus last November. This compounds with the buried/un-grouped full list.
  - **Fix:** Append the year for sessions outside the current year (or relative labels like 'hoy'/'ayer' for very recent ones). Do it in the shared helper so card and detail stay aligned.
  - **Dónde:** lib/features/workout/presentation/utils/date_helpers.dart:43-47 formatSessionDate returns '$dow ${date.day} $month' with no year; the `now` param is explicitly ignored. Used by both the card and the detail header.

- **[LOW · consistency]** Button/label casing and terminology vary across the flow's states: the empty/error CTAs are sentence-case ('Reintentar', 'Empezar entrenamiento', 'Volver a Entrenar') while other workout buttons are ALL-CAPS ('LISTO', 'COMPARTIR'), and the not-found/error screens use full centered FilledButtons whereas the inline list error uses a flat TextButton. Same conceptual action ('reintentar') is styled two different ways within one journey.
  - **Fix:** Standardize retry/primary-action button style and casing across the journey's loading/error/empty/not-found states (pick one casing convention and one button hierarchy for primary vs secondary actions).
  - **Dónde:** List error uses TextButton (historial_section.dart:128-131, label 'Reintentar').
